Sending Belongings to Makkah While in Mina
Ruling on transferring luggage to Makkah while in Mina.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on sending belongings to Makkah while staying in Mina, identify the evidence from Umar's athar, and explain why it is makruh tanzihi without requiring dam.

Core Idea
Sending luggage ahead to Makkah is disliked but not invalidating.

A pilgrim staying in Mina for stoning might consider sending heavy luggage to Makkah. This lesson examines the ruling on this practice, derived from the athar of Umar ibn al-Khattab, and clarifies that while it is makruh tanzihi, it does not affect the validity of Hajj nor require compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sending one's belongings (thaqal) to Makkah while the pilgrim stays in Mina for the stoning. The ruling is makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked).
Makruh tanzihi means it is better to avoid but not sinful.
2
Examine the evidence (athar of Umar)
The evidence is the statement of Umar ibn al-Khattab: 'Whoever sends his belongings ahead on the night of departure, there is no Hajj for him.' This is a strong warning indicating dislike, but the commentator clarifies it does not literally negate Hajj.
The phrase 'fala hajja lahu' is rhetorical, not actual nullification.
3
Understand the hukm level
The ruling is makruh tanzihi, not haram or makruh tahrimi. Therefore, if done, no dam (sacrifice) is required, and the Hajj remains valid.
This distinguishes the ruling from more severe prohibitions that require compensation.
4
Apply the modern context
In the past, people carried their belongings, so sending them ahead caused attachment. Today, belongings are often already in hotels in Makkah, so the dislike may be reduced.
The commentator explicitly says there is no harm if belongings are already in a Makkah hotel.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز ويكره ان يقدم الانسان ثقله الى مكة ويقيم بها حتى يرمى [۶۷۶] (۷۲) فاذا نفر الى مكة نزل بالمحصب [۶۷۷] (۷۳) ثم طاف بالبيت سبعة اشواط لا يرمل فيها وهذا طواف الصدر. [۶۷۵] (۷۱) مکروہ ہے کہ انسان اپنے سامان کو مکہ مکرمہ منتقل کرے اور خود منی میں ٹھہر کر رمی کرے۔ خود منی میں ٹھہر کر رمی کرے اور اپنا سامان مکہ مکرمہ منتقل کر دے ایسا کرنا مکروہ تنزیہی ہے۔ (1) اثر میں ہے قال عمر من تقدم ثقله ليلة ينفر فلا حج له (الف) (مصنف ابن الي هيبته ۴۲۲ من کرد ان يقدم ثقله من منی ج ثالث ص ۱۳۸۷ نمبر ۱۵۳۸۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اپنا سامان مکہ مکرمہ منتقل کرنا مکروہ ہے تاہم اگر کر لیا تو دم لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ پچھلے زمانے میں آدمی اپنا سامان ساتھ رکھتے تھے۔ ہوٹل وغیرہ میں نہیں رکھتے تھے اس لئے سامان مکہ مکرمہ بھیج دے اور خود منی میں ٹھہرنے سے آدمی کا دل سامان پر لگا رہے گا اس لئے بھی مکروہ ہے۔ لیکن آج کل کی طرح پہلے سے سارا سامان مکہ مکرمہ کے ہوٹل میں ہو تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
And it is permissible but disliked that a man send his belongings ahead to Makkah and stay there until he stones. (72) Then when he departs to Makkah, he should descend at al-Muhassab. (73) Then he should circumambulate the House seven circuits without raml in it, and this is the farewell tawaf. (71) It is disliked (makruh) for a man to transfer his belongings to Makkah and himself stay in Mina for stoning. He himself stays in Mina for stoning and sends his belongings to Makkah; doing this is makruh tanzihi. (1) There is an athar: Umar said, 'Whoever sends his belongings ahead on the night of departure, there is no Hajj for him.' (a) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 422, chapter on sending belongings ahead from Mina, vol. 3, p. 1387, no. 15384) From this athar, it is understood that sending one's belongings to Makkah is disliked; however, if one does it, dem (blood) is not required. In former times, people used to keep their belongings with them, not in hotels etc. So sending belongings to Makkah and staying in Mina causes one's heart to be attached to the belongings; that is why it is disliked. But in present times, if all belongings are already in a hotel in Makkah, there is no harm.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with evidence. It states that it is makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked) for a pilgrim to send his luggage to Makkah while he himself remains in Mina to perform the stoning of the jamarat. The textual evidence is an athar from Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him) who said that whoever sends his luggage ahead on the night of departure (the 12th) has no Hajj — this is a severe warning indicating strong dislike, but the commentator clarifies that it does not invalidate the Hajj nor require a dam (compensation). The reason for the dislike is that in the past, pilgrims carried their belongings with them, and sending them away would preoccupy the heart. Today, since hotels are arranged beforehand and belongings are safely stored, the ruling may be less applicable. The ruling is makruh tanzihi, meaning it is better to avoid but not sinful.

Key Terms
ثقله (thaqaluhu): One's heavy belongings, luggage, or goods.
مکروہ تنزیہی (makruh tanzihi): Disliked but not prohibited; avoiding it is better but doing it is not sinful.
دم (dam): A sacrificial offering required as a penalty for certain violations in Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a pilgrim sending his luggage to Makkah while he stays in Mina for stoning?
A) Haram and invalidates Hajj
B) Makruh tanzihi, no dam required
C) Permissible without any dislike
D) Makruh tahrimi, requires dam

Key Takeaway
Sending belongings to Makkah while staying in Mina is makruh tanzihi; it does not invalidate Hajj nor require a dam, and in modern contexts it may be free of dislike if belongings are already in Makkah.

Descending at Al-Muhassab After Mina
Sunnah to alight at al-Muhassab from Mina to Makkah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on descending at al-Muhassab and identify its dalil from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Descending at al-Muhassab is a recommended sunnah, not an obligation—following the Prophet's example.

In this lesson, we examine the practice of al-Muhassab, the place where the Prophet camped after leaving Mina. The source text affirms that this action is a sunnah, rooted in the Prophet's own practice and narrated by Anas ibn Malik. Understanding its status helps distinguish recommended acts from obligatory ones in Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the action and its ruling
The text states that when departing from Mina to Makkah, the pilgrim should descend at al-Muhassab. This is a recommended (mustahabb) act, not a pillar or condition of Hajj.
The ruling is based on the Prophet's action, not a command.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The text quotes the hadith of Anas ibn Malik that the Prophet prayed Dhuhr, Asr, Maghrib, and Isha and slept at al-Muhassab before proceeding to tawaf.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim, showing the practice is well-established.
3
Understand the wisdom and Hanafi position
The passage explains that the Prophet camped there as a sign of gratitude and to demonstrate the triumph of Islam. The Hanafi school considers it mustahabb, and omitting it does not invalidate Hajj.
Some scholars consider it sunnah mu'akkadah, but the relied-upon view is mustahabb.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاذا نفر الى مكة نزل بالمحصب [۶۷۷] (۷۳) ثم طاف بالبيت سبعة اشواط لا يرمل فيها وهذا طواف الصدر. [۶۷۶] (۷۲) پس جب مکہ مکرمہ کی طرف کوچ کرے تو مقام محصب پر اترے۔ تش حضور نے منی سے واپسی پر مکہ کے قریب مقام مصب پر پڑاؤ ڈالا تھا۔ (۱) آپ نے فرمایا کہ اس مقام پر کافروں نے مل کر فیصلہ کیا تھا کہ اسلام مٹا دیں گے اس لئے اس مقام پر پڑاؤ ڈال کر بتلائیں گے کہ اسلام پھل پھول کر مکہ میں واپس آگیا، اسی شکرانہ میں آپ اور صحابہ مقام مصب میں قیام پذیر ہوئے (۲) ان انس بن مالك حدثه عن النبي الله انه صلى الظهر والعصر والمغرب والعشاء ورقد رقدة بالمحصب ثم ركب الى البيت فطاف به (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب من صلى العصر يوم الحفر بالا صبح ص ۲۳۷ نمبر ۱۷۶۴ار مسلم شریف ، باب استحباب نزول الحصب يوم الحفر وصلوة ر و ما بعدها به ص ۴۲۲۲ نمبر ۱۳۰۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ منی سے نکلنے کے بعد مقام محصب میں ٹھہر نا چاہئے۔ الحصب : مکہ مکرمہ کے قریب ایک مقام کا نام ہے۔
Then when he departs to Makkah, he should descend at al-Muhassab. (73) Then he should circumambulate the House seven circuits without raml in it, and this is the farewell tawaf. (72) So when he departs towards Makkah, he should descend at the place of Muhassab. The Prophet (peace be upon him) camped at a place near Makkah called Muhassab on his return from Mina. (1) He said that at this place the disbelievers had collectively decided to eradicate Islam, so by camping here they would show that Islam had flourished and returned to Makkah; out of gratitude, the Prophet and his Companions halted at Muhassab. (2) Anas ibn Malik narrated from the Prophet that he prayed Dhuhr, Asr, Maghrib, and Isha, and took a nap at al-Muhassab, then rode to the House and circumambulated it. (b) (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on whoever prayed Asr on the day of Nahr at al-Muhassab, p. 237, no. 1764; and Sahih Muslim, chapter on the recommendation of descending at al-Muhassab on the day of Nahr, p. 4222, no. 1309) From this hadith it is understood that after leaving Mina, one should stay at al-Muhassab. Al-Muhassab is the name of a place near Makkah.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with evidence. It states that when a pilgrim departs from Mina to Makkah (after completing the stoning), it is recommended (mustahabb) to descend at al-Muhassab, a place near Makkah. The text provides two reasons: first, the Prophet did so upon returning to Makkah as a sign of gratitude and to demonstrate the triumph of Islam, as the disbelievers had plotted there. Second, there is a clear hadith from Anas ibn Malik that the Prophet performed four prayers and slept at al-Muhassab before going to the Kaaba for tawaf. This practice is not obligatory but is a sunnah (recommended) to emulate the Prophet. The place is also known as 'al-Hasbah'.

Key Terms
محصب (al-Muhassab): A place near Makkah where the Prophet camped after leaving Mina. Also called al-Hasbah or al-Abtah.
نزول (nuzul): Descending or alighting at a place for rest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the recommendation regarding al-Muhassab when leaving Mina?
A) It is obligatory to camp there
B) It is recommended to descend and pray there
C) It is prohibited to stop there
D) It is required to perform tawaf there

Key Takeaway
Descending at al-Muhassab is a recommended sunnah (mustahabb) of Hajj, based on the Prophet's practice, and its omission does not affect the validity of the pilgrimage.

Tawaf as-Sadr: Farewell Tawaf Without Raml
Ruling on the farewell tawaf and the omission of raml

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of tawaf as-sadr, explain why raml is omitted, and identify the Hanafi position on its wajib status.

Core Idea
Tawaf as-sadr is wajib, performed without raml, as raml is only sunnah once per Hajj.

In the final moments of Hajj, the pilgrim performs a farewell circumambulation known as tawaf as-sadr or tawaf al-wada'. This passage clarifies that this tawaf consists of seven circuits without the brisk walk (raml) that accompanies earlier tawafs. Understanding why raml is omitted and the legal weight of this tawaf is essential for correct Hajj practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being described? (tawaf as-sadr/wada') and what is the ruling? (wajib, seven circuits, no raml).
2
Understand the omission of raml
Raml is not performed because raml and sa'i are only sunnah once in a Hajj/Umrah, and have already been done in tawaf al-qudum or tawaf az-ziyarah.
The text states: 'raml and sa'i are sunnah only once in each Hajj and Umrah, not repeated.'
3
Locate the proof
The hadith from Ibn Abbas: the people were commanded that their last covenant be with the House. This implies obligation.
The hadith is cited as evidence for the requirement of farewell tawaf.
4
Determine the Hanafi hukm level
Based on the hadith command, Hanafis classify tawaf as-sadr as wajib; missing it requires a dam (sacrificial offering).
'Wajib' means obligatory but with a lower epistemic certainty than fard.
5
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school considers tawaf al-wada' as sunnah, not wajib, interpreting the command as a recommendation.
The difference stems from usul al-fiqh: whether a command implies obligation or recommendation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم طاف بالبيت سبعة اشواط لا يرمل فيها وهذا طواف الصدر. [۶۷۷] (۷۳) پھر بیت اللہ کا طواف کرے سات شوط ، اس میں ریل نہ کرے اور یہ طواف صدر ہے۔ یوں تو مکہ مکرمہ میں رہتے ہوئے جتنے طواف کرے بہتر ہے، البتہ مکہ مکرمہ سے واپس ہوتے وقت آخری طواف کرے جس کو طواف صدر اور طواف وداع کہتے ہیں۔ اس طواف میں رمل نہ کرے۔ اب مکہ مکرمہ اور بیت اللہ کو الوداع کہہ رہا ہے اس لئے و داعی طواف کرے اور اس میں ریل اس لئے نہیں کرے گا کہ ریل اور سعی ہر حج اور عمرہ میں ایک ہی مرتبہ سنت ہے دوبارہ نہیں۔ اور طواف قدوم یا طواف زیارت میں ایک مرتبہ ریل اور سعی کر چکا ہے اس لئے اب دوبارہ نہیں کرے گا (۲) اس طواف کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابن عباس قال امر الناس ان يكون آخر عهدهم بالبيت الا انه خفف
Then he should circumambulate the House seven circuits without raml in them, and this is the farewell tawaf. (73) Then he should perform tawaf of the House, seven circuits, no raml in it, and this is tawaf as-sadr. So while staying in Makkah, however many tawaf he performs, it is better. However, when departing from Makkah, he should perform a final tawaf, which is called tawaf as-sadr and tawaf al-wada'. In this tawaf, he should not do raml. Now he is bidding farewell to Makkah and the House, so he performs the farewell tawaf, and he does not do raml because raml and sa'i are sunnah only once in each Hajj and Umrah, not repeated. And in tawaf al-qudum or tawaf az-ziyarah, he has already done raml and sa'i once, so he will not do them again. (2) The proof for this tawaf is the hadith from Ibn Abbas: 'The people were commanded that their last covenant be with the House, except that it was lightened (for the menstruating woman).'
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with evidence. It describes the farewell tawaf (tawaf as-sadr or tawaf al-wada') that a pilgrim performs after leaving Mina and before departing from Makkah. The ruling: it consists of seven circuits without raml (walking briskly). Raml is not performed because raml and sa'i are only sunnah once per Hajj/Umrah, and they have already been done in either tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf) or tawaf az-ziyarah (essential tawaf). The farewell tawaf is the final act of worship, bidding farewell to the Kaaba. The evidence is the hadith from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet commanded that a pilgrim's last act should be tawaf of the House, except that menstruating women are exempted. This tawaf is wajib (obligatory) according to the Hanafi school; missing it requires a dam (sacrificial offering). The text emphasizes that no raml is performed because it is a repeated tawaf.

Key Terms
طواف صدر (tawaf as-sadr): The farewell tawaf performed after completing the rituals of Hajj before leaving Makkah.
رمل (raml): Walking briskly with short steps and swinging the shoulders during the first three circuits of tawaf.
وداع (wada'): Farewell; tawaf al-wada' is the same as tawaf as-sadr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is raml not performed in tawaf as-sadr?
A) Because raml is haram in farewell tawaf.
B) Because raml is only sunnah once per Hajj/Umrah.
C) Because farewell tawaf is only one circuit.
D) Because raml is only for men.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf as-sadr is a wajib farewell circumambulation without raml; its omission requires a dam.

Sending Luggage Ahead During Hajj: Ruling and Evidence
Ruling with proof on the dislike of sending luggage ahead

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sending luggage ahead during Hajj and explain why it is makruh tanzihi, citing the athar of Umar.

Core Idea
Sending luggage ahead to Makkah while staying in Mina is slightly disliked but does not nullify Hajj.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from the Hanafi school regarding a pilgrim's conduct during the days of tashriq. The passage addresses whether one may send his luggage to Makkah while remaining in Mina for the stoning ritual. The ruling is based on an athar from Umar ibn al-Khattab and is classified as makruh tanzihi. Understanding this distinction helps clarify the implications for the validity of Hajj and the need for compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being done? The pilgrim sends his luggage to Makkah while he himself stays in Mina to perform ramy. The ruling is stated as makruh tanzihi.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites an athar from Umar: 'Whoever sends his luggage ahead on the night of nafar has no Hajj.' This is a strong warning.
The athar is from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does this athar prove the ruling? Umar's severe statement ('no Hajj') indicates extreme dislike, but it is interpreted as a threat, not as nullification of Hajj. The Hanafi school takes it as makruh tanzihi, not haram.
The severe wording is common in makruh tanzihi cases to emphasize avoidance.
4
Determine the consequence of violation
If the act is done, no dam (blood sacrifice) is required. This confirms the classification as makruh tanzihi, not makruh tahrimi.
5
Consider contextual change
The reason for dislike is the distraction caused by luggage anxiety when it is sent ahead. In modern times, when luggage is already placed in a hotel, this reason may not apply, reducing or removing the dislike.
This shows the application of 'illa (effective cause) and its relevance to modern practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۶۷۵] (۷۱) مکروہ ہے کہ انسان اپنے سامان کو مکہ مکرمہ منتقل کرے اور خود منی میں ٹھہرار ہے تا کہ رمی کرے۔ خودمنی میں ٹھہر کر رمی کرے اور اپنا سامان مکہ مکرمہ منتقل کر دے ایسا کرنا مکروہ تنزیہی ہے۔ (1) اثر میں ہے قال عمر من تقدم ثقله ليلة ينفر فلا حج له (الف) (مصنف ابن الي هيبته ۴۲۲ من کرد ان يقدم ثقله من منی ج ثالث ص ۱۳۸۷ نمبر ۱۵۳۸۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اپنا سامان مکہ مکرمہ منتقل کرنا مکروہ ہے تاہم اگر کر لیا تو دم لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ پچھلے زمانے میں آدمی اپنا سامان ساتھ رکھتے تھے۔ ہوٹل وغیرہ میں نہیں رکھتے تھے اس لئے سامان مکہ مکرمہ بھیج دے اور خود منی میں ٹھہرنے سے آدمی کا دل سامان پر لگا رہے گا اس لئے بھی مکروہ ہے۔ لیکن آج کل کی طرح پہلے سے سارا سامان مکہ مکرمہ کے ہوٹل میں ہو تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
It is disliked that a person sends his luggage to Makkah and stays in Mina until he stones the jamarat. He himself stays in Mina to stone and sends his luggage to Makkah; doing so is makruh tanzihi. (1) There is an athar: 'Umar said: Whoever sends his luggage ahead on the night of nafar (12th night), he has no Hajj.' (Source: Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah...) This athar indicates that sending luggage to Makkah is makruh, and if done, no dam is required. In earlier times, people used to keep their luggage with them; they did not keep it in hotels. So sending luggage to Makkah and staying in Mina would cause one's mind to be attached to the luggage, hence it is disliked. But if, like today, all luggage is already in a hotel in Makkah from the beginning, then there is no harm.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This is a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the dislike of sending one's luggage ahead to Makkah while one stays in Mina to complete the stoning (ramy). The author begins by stating the ruling: it is makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked) to do this. The evidence is an athar from Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him) which says that whoever sends his luggage on the night of nafar (the 12th of Dhul Hijjah) has no Hajj. However, the commentator explains that this is a severe warning to indicate extreme dislike, not that the Hajj is invalidated. If someone does it, no dam (blood sacrifice) is required. The reason for the ruling is that in earlier times, pilgrims carried their luggage themselves, and sending it ahead would cause anxiety, distracting from the rites. In modern times, if all luggage is already placed in a Makkah hotel, there is no such concern, so it may not be disliked.

Key Terms
مکروہ تنزیہی (makruh tanzihi): A disliked act that is close to permissible; not sinful but better avoided. No compensation required in worship.
رمی (ramy): The stoning of the jamarat during Hajj, performed in Mina on the days of tashriq.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice required as compensation for certain violations during Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Staying at Muhassab: A Sunnah of Hajj
Sunnah of staying at Muhassab on return from Mina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on staying at Muhassab and identify its evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Staying at Muhassab is a confirmed sunnah, not an obligation, based on the Prophet's practice.

After completing the stoning at Mina, many pilgrims rush back to Makkah. However, the Prophet (peace be upon him) set an example of camping at a place called Muhassab (or Al-Abtah) on his return. This lesson examines the ruling of this act and its proof from authentic hadith, clarifying that it is a recommended sunnah, not a required duty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is staying (al-nuzul) at the place called Muhassab after departing from Mina and before entering Makkah for tawaf. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed recommended), not wajib.
The author uses the imperative 'yanbaghi' (should), which in Hanafi usage denotes recommendation when the proof is a prophetic action, not a command.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The proof is the hadith of Anas ibn Malik (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Prophet prayed Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha, and took a nap at Muhassab before riding to the Ka'bah for tawaf.
This hadith is recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim, making it authentically transmitted.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (indication of the proof)
The Prophet's action (fi'l) of staying, praying, and resting at Muhassab indicates that it is a desirable practice. In Hanafi usul, a prophetic act that is not accompanied by an explicit command (amr) indicates istihbab (recommendation) unless there is evidence raising it to wujub.
No such evidence exists for this act; hence it remains sunnah.
4
Check for ikhtilaf (scholarly disagreement)
There is no significant disagreement among the schools on the sunnah nature of staying at Muhassab. All major schools consider it mustahabb or sunnah. The Hanafi position is that it is sunnah muakkadah.
The commentator mentions a historical reason for the stay, but this does not affect the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۶۷۶] (۷۲) پس جب مکہ مکرمہ کی طرف کوچ کرے تو مقام محصب پر اترے۔ تش حضور نے منی سے واپسی پر مکہ کے قریب مقام مصب پر پڑاؤ ڈالا تھا۔ (۱) آپ نے فرمایا کہ اس مقام پر کافروں نے مل کر فیصلہ کیا تھا کہ اسلام مٹا دیں گے اس لئے اس مقام پر پڑاؤ ڈال کر بتلائیں گے کہ اسلام پھل پھول کر مکہ میں واپس آگیا، اسی شکرانہ میں آپ اور صحابہ مقام مصب میں قیام پذیر ہوئے (۲) ان انس بن مالک حدثه عن النبي الله انه صلى الظهر والعصر والمغرب والعشاء ورقد رقدة بالمحصب ثم ركب الى البيت فطاف به (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب من صلى العصر يوم الحفر بالا صبح ص ۲۳۷ نمبر ۱۷۶۴ار مسلم شریف ، باب استحباب نزول الحصب يوم الحفر وصلوة ر و ما بعدها به ص ۴۲۲۲ نمبر ۱۳۰۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ منی سے نکلنے کے بعد مقام محصب میں ٹھہر نا چاہئے۔ الحصب : مکہ مکرمہ کے قریب ایک مقام کا نام ہے۔
When one departs to Makkah, he should alight at the place of Muhassab. The Prophet, on returning from Mina, camped at a place near Makkah called Muhassab. (1) He said that the disbelievers gathered at this place and decided to eradicate Islam, so camping here shows that Islam has flourished and returned to Makkah. In gratitude, the Prophet and his Companions stayed at Muhassab. (2) Anas ibn Malik narrated from the Prophet that he prayed Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib and Isha, and took a short nap at Muhassab, then rode to the House and performed tawaf. (Bukhari and Muslim) This hadith indicates that after leaving Mina, one should stay at Muhassab. Al-Hasab: the name of a place near Makkah.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This ruling discusses the sunnah of staying at Muhassab (also known as Al-Abtah or Al-Hasab) after completing the stoning in Mina and before returning to Makkah for Tawaf al-Ifadah or Tawaf al-Wada. The author presents the action of the Prophet as evidence. The Prophet camped there and performed prayers and slept. The commentator adds a historical reason: the disbelievers conspired there to destroy Islam, so the Prophet's stay symbolizes Islam's triumph. This act is recommended (sunnah) but not obligatory.

Key Terms
محصب (Muhassab): A place between Mina and Makkah where the Prophet camped after stoning.

Tawaf al-Sadr: Performance and Obligation
Rulings on performing Tawaf al-Sadr and its obligation for non-Makkans

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Tawaf al-Wada, identify who it is wajib for, and explain the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Wada is wajib for non-Makkans; raml is not repeated.

After completing all Hajj rites, the pilgrim's final act before leaving Makkah is a farewell tawaf. This lesson clarifies its performance, who must perform it, and the proof that establishes its obligation in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what Tawaf al-Wada is and its hukm level (wajib or sunnah).
The text states it is wajib for non-Makkans.
2
Analyze the performance rule: no raml
Understand why raml is not performed in this tawaf: because raml is sunnah only once per Hajj.
This is based on the principle that sunnah acts are not repeated.
3
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith evidence: the Prophet's command that the last covenant should be with the House.
The hadith is narrated by Ibn Abbas.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith indicates obligation: the command form (amr) in 'La yanfiranna ahad' indicates wujub in Hanafi usul.
This is a key example of amr → wujub.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i considers it sunnah, and understand the thamarah (practical consequence).
The difference affects whether omission requires a dam.

Then he should perform tawaf of the House, seven circuits, without raml in it. This is the Tawaf al-Sadr. Although performing as many tawaf as possible in Makkah is better, when departing from Makkah, he should perform a final tawaf called Tawaf al-Sadr or Tawaf al-Wada. In this tawaf, he should not do raml. Now he is bidding farewell to Makkah and the House, so he should perform a farewell tawaf. He does not do raml because raml and sa'i are only sunnah once in each Hajj or Umrah, not repeated. He has already done raml and sa'i in Tawaf al-Qudum or Tawaf al-Ziyarah, so he should not repeat. (2) The evidence for this tawaf is the hadith from Ibn Abbas: 'The Prophet ordered people that the last of their covenant should be with the House, except that he made an exception for the menstruating woman.' [PAGE_421] [678] (74) This Tawaf al-Wada is wajib, except for the people of Makkah, then he returns to his family. Explanation: Tawaf al-Wada means the tawaf of leaving the House. Since the people of Makkah do not leave Makkah, it is not wajib for them. They will do tawaf whenever they get the chance. The evidence for its obligation is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'The people were departing in every direction, so the Prophet said: None of you should depart until his last covenant is with the House.' (Muslim, Abu Dawud) In this hadith, there is a command form which indicates obligation. Therefore, Tawaf al-Wada is wajib for the non-Makkans.

Commentary
This passage covers the rulings of Tawaf al-Sadr, also known as Tawaf al-Wada. It begins by instructing the pilgrim to perform seven circuits without raml (quick walking with shoulders swaying). The commentator explains that this is a farewell tawaf. Raml is not done because it is only sunnah once in the entire Hajj, already performed in Tawaf al-Qudum or Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The evidence is a hadith from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet ordered the last act at the House to be tawaf. Then point 74 states that this tawaf is wajib (obligatory) except for the residents of Makkah. The commentator explains that Makkans are exempt because they do not leave the city permanently. The obligation is proven by the command form in the hadith 'la yanfiranna ahad' (none should depart) which indicates wujub in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
طواف الصدر (Tawaf al-Sadr): The farewell tawaf performed after completing Hajj rites when leaving Makkah.
رمل (raml): Walking quickly with short steps and moving the shoulders, done only in the first three circuits of Tawaf al-Qudum or Tawaf al-Ziyarah.

Tawaf al-Wada is wajib for non-Makkans, based on the command in the hadith, and raml is not performed in it because it is only sunnah once per Hajj.

Dropping of Tawaf al-Qudum When Going Directly to Arafat
Ruling on dropping Tawaf al-Qudum if the pilgrim goes straight to Arafat without entering Makkah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on Tawaf al-Qudum for a pilgrim who goes straight to Arafat and identify the proof from the hadith and qiyas.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Qudum is a sunnah tied to entering Makkah; skipping Makkah means skipping the tawaf.

This lesson addresses a practical question: what if a pilgrim, after assuming ihram, bypasses Makkah and goes directly to Arafat? In the Hanafi school, Tawaf al-Qudum is dropped entirely, and no penalty applies. The ruling is based on the sunnah status of the act and an analogy with tahiyyat al-masjid, supported by a prophetic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The pilgrim does not enter Makkah after ihram but proceeds straight to Arafat and performs the standing (wuquf).
This scenario is distinct from a pilgrim who enters Makkah and then goes to Arafat.
2
State the ruling
Tawaf al-Qudum is dropped, and nothing (no dam) is required for omitting it.
The Hajj remains valid.
3
Understand the basis
Tawaf al-Qudum is a sunnah muakkadah whose trigger is entering Makkah. Since the pilgrim never entered Makkah, there is no occasion for it.
Analogy (qiyas) with tahiyyat al-masjid: if you do not enter a mosque, you do not pray its greeting.
4
Examine the proof
The hadith of Urwa ibn Mudarris states that whoever reaches Arafat and joins the prayer at Muzdalifah has completed the Hajj, without mentioning Tawaf al-Qudum.
This implicitly shows that Tawaf al-Qudum is not a requirement for the validity of Hajj.
5
Apply the consequence
Since Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah, omitting it does not require dam; only wajib or fard omissions require compensation.
This reinforces that not all acts of Hajj are equally binding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۶۷۹] (۷۵) اگر محرم مکہ میں داخل نہ ہو اور عرفات کی طرف متوجہ ہو جائے اور وہاں اس طرح وقوف عرفہ کرلے جیسا کہ ہم نے پہلے بیان کیا تو اس سے طواف قدوم ساقط ہو جائے گا اور طواف قدوم کے چھوڑنے سے اس پر کچھ لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ ا کوئی محرم مکہ نہ آیا اور احرام باندھ کر سیدھا عرفات چلا گیا تو اس کا حج ہو گیا۔ اب اس پر طواف قدوم کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور طواف قدوم کے چھوڑنے سے دم بھی لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ (۱) طواف قدوم ملکہ آنے پر ہوتا ہے اور وہ مکہ آیا ہی نہیں اس لئے اس پر طواف قدوم نہیں ہے جیسے کوئی مسجد میں داخل ہو ہی نہیں تو اس پر تحیۃ المسجد لازم نہیں ہوگی۔ اور چونکہ طواف قدوم سنت ہے اس لئے سنت چھوڑنے پر دم لازم نہیں ہو گا (۲) اخبرنی عروة بن مضرس الطائي قال اتيت رسول الله بالموقف يعنى بجمع قلت جئت يا رسول الله من جبلی طی اكللت مطبتی و اتعبت نفسى والله ماتركت من حبل الا وقفت عليه فهل لى من حج فقال رسول الله من ادرك معنا هذه الصلوة واتى عرفات قبل ذلك ليلا او نهارا فقد تم حجه و قضى تفته (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب من لم یدرک عرفته ص ۲۷۶ نمبر ۱۹۵۰
If a muhrim does not enter Makkah and proceeds to Arafat and performs the standing at Arafat as we have described earlier, then Tawaf al-Qudum is dropped from him, and nothing becomes necessary upon him for leaving it. If a muhrim did not come to Makkah but tied the ihram and went straight to Arafat, his Hajj is valid. He does not need to perform Tawaf al-Qudum, and no dam is required for leaving it. (1) Tawaf al-Qudum is performed upon entering Makkah, and since he did not enter Makkah, he has no Tawaf al-Qudum, just as one who does not enter a mosque does not have to pray tahiyyat al-masjid. And since Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah, leaving a sunnah does not require dam. (2) Urwa ibn Mudarris al-Ta'i reported: I came to the Messenger of Allah at the standing place (i.e., Muzdalifah) and said: 'O Messenger of Allah, I came from the mountains of Tayy; I have exhausted my mount and myself. By Allah, I did not leave any mountain pass except I stood at it. Do I have a Hajj?' The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever joins us in this prayer and comes to Arafat before that, night or day, his Hajj is complete and he has fulfilled his filth.' (Abu Dawud)
Source pages p. 421

Commentary
This ruling clarifies a specific scenario: a pilgrim who, after assuming ihram, goes directly to Arafat without first entering Makkah. In such a case, Tawaf al-Qudum (the arrival tawaf) is not required because it is a sunnah connected to entering Makkah. Since the pilgrim never entered Makkah, there is no occasion for it. The commentator draws an analogy: just as tahiyyat al-masjid is not required if one does not enter the mosque, so too Tawaf al-Qudum is not required. Since it is a sunnah, leaving it does not necessitate a dam. The hadith of Urwa ibn Mudarris supports the validity of the Hajj even if one does not perform Tawaf al-Qudum, as the Prophet said the Hajj is complete for those who reach Arafat and join the prayer at Muzdalifah.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (Tawaf al-Qudum): The tawaf performed upon entering Makkah as a greeting to the Sacred Mosque. It is sunnah.
تحیۃ المسجد (tahiyyat al-masjid): Two rak'ahs prayed upon entering a mosque as a greeting to the mosque.
دم (dam): A sacrifice (blood) required as compensation for omitting a wajib in Hajj or Umrah.
محرم (muhrim): A person who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What becomes of Tawaf al-Qudum if a pilgrim goes directly to Arafat without entering Makkah?
A) It becomes wajib to perform after Hajj
B) It is dropped and no compensation is needed
C) It is still required before returning
D) A dam must be offered

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Qudum is a sunnah tied to entering Makkah; if a pilgrim bypasses Makkah, the tawaf is dropped with no penalty.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
6 min
Ruling on Tawaf al-Wada' and its Obligation
Establishes that Tawaf al-Wada' is wajib except for people of Makkah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Tawaf al-Wada', identify who it applies to, and explain the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Wada' is wajib for all pilgrims except Makkans, based on the Prophet's imperative.

Tawaf al-Wada' (the farewell circumambulation) is a significant act in Hajj. The Hanafi school classifies it as wajib, not fard, and it is required for every pilgrim except those residing in Makkah. This lesson examines the ruling, the exception, and the scriptural proof that establishes its obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is Tawaf al-Wada' (farewell tawaf). According to the text, it is wajib (obligatory). Distinguish wajib from fard: wajib is established by zanni evidence, while fard requires qat'i evidence.
In Hanafi usul, wajib is still binding; omission incurs sin and requires compensation.
2
Identify the exception
The exception is the people of Makkah (ahl Makkah). They are not required to perform Tawaf al-Wada' because they do not leave the Haram; the tawaf is a farewell for those departing.
The rationale: the ruling is linked to leaving the House of Allah.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith from Ibn Abbas: 'None of you should depart until his last contact with the House is (by performing tawaf).' This is a command (amr) from the Prophet.
The hadith is classified as ahad (zanni al-thubut), which is why the ruling is wajib, not fard.
4
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative form (لا ينفرن) indicates obligation in Hanafi usul. The context reinforces obligation: the people were departing in different directions, and the Prophet prohibited them until they performed tawaf.
No contrary indicator (qarinah) diverts the imperative to recommendation (nadb), so it retains its default meaning of wujub.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school considers Tawaf al-Wada' as sunnah, not wajib. They interpret the imperative as recommendation, possibly due to other hadiths or lack of strict enforcement.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference): Hanafi: omission requires a dam; Shafi'i: no penalty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو واجب الا على اهل مكة ثم يعود الى اهله اس حیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آفاقی پر طواف وداع واجب ہے۔ یہ طواف وداع واجب ہے مگر اہل مکہ پر واجب نہیں ہے۔ پھر اپنے گھر کی طرف لوٹ آئے۔ تشریح طواف وداع کا مطلب ہے بیت اللہ چھوڑنے کا طواف لیکن اہل مکہ چونکہ مکہ ہی میں ہیں اس لئے وہ بیت اللہ نہیں چھوڑیں گے۔ اس لئے ان کے لئے طواف وداع واجب نہیں ہے۔ وہ تو جب جب موقع ملے طواف کرتے رہیں گے۔ واجب ہونے کی دلیل او پر کی حدیث ہے عن ابن عباس قال كان الناس ينصرفون في كل وجه فقال رسول الله لا ينفرن احد حتى يكون آخر عهده بالبيت اس حدیث میں امر کا صیغہ ہے جو وجوب پر دلالت کرتا ہے۔ اس لئے بھی طواف وداع آفاقی کے لئے واجب ہوگا۔
And it is obligatory except for the people of Makkah, then he returns to his family. From here it is known that Tawaf al-Wada' is obligatory upon the Afaqi (one from outside Makkah). This Tawaf al-Wada' is obligatory except it is not obligatory upon the people of Makkah. Then he returns to his home. Explanation: Tawaf al-Wada' means the circumambulation of leaving the House of Allah. But since the people of Makkah are in Makkah itself, they will not leave the House of Allah. Therefore Tawaf al-Wada' is not obligatory upon them. They will keep performing tawaf whenever they get the opportunity. The proof of its obligation is the hadith mentioned earlier: from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: 'The people were departing in every direction, so the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: None of you should depart until his last contact with the House (of Allah) is (by performing tawaf).' In this hadith there is an imperative form which indicates obligation. Therefore Tawaf al-Wada' is obligatory for the Afaqi.
Source pages p. 421

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding Tawaf al-Wada' (the farewell circumambulation). It begins by stating the ruling: Tawaf al-Wada' is wajib (obligatory) for every pilgrim except the residents of Makkah. The reason is that the purpose of this tawaf is to bid farewell to the Ka'bah when leaving Makkah, and the people of Makkah are not leaving, so it is not required of them. The author then provides the proof from the hadith of Ibn Abbas, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded that no one should leave until his last act is tawaf around the House. The imperative form (لا ينفرن) indicates obligation according to Hanafi usul. The passage also clarifies that Tawaf al-Wada' is wajib, not fard, because the evidence is from a hadith that is ahad, not mutawatir. The Urdu commentary explains the rationale and emphasizes that the residents of Makkah are exempt because they do not depart from the sacred precincts. The hadith is quoted in full to support the ruling.

Key Terms
طواف الوداع (Tawaf al-Wada'): The circumambulation performed when leaving Makkah as a farewell to the Ka'bah.
آفاقي (Afaqi): One who comes from outside the Miqat (boundaries of the Haram) to perform Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Wajib
C) Fard
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Wada' is wajib for those leaving Makkah (Afaqi) based on the Prophet's command; omission requires compensation but does not invalidate Hajj.

Tawaf al-Qudum Is Sunnah and Dropped When Bypassing Makkah
Ruling with proof that Tawaf al-Qudum is dropped for the pilgrim bypassing Makkah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on Tawaf al-Qudum when a pilgrim bypasses Makkah, and apply the Hanafi principle that omitting a sunnah does not require compensation.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah; if you skip Makkah, it drops without penalty.

In Hajj, certain rituals are tied to entering Makkah. If a pilgrim in ihram goes directly to Arafat without passing through Makkah, one might wonder whether Tawaf al-Qudum (the arrival circumambulation) must still be performed later, perhaps with a penalty. This lesson examines the clear Hanafi ruling: the tawaf is dropped and no dam is required. We will see the proof from hadith and the reasoning by analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Tawaf al-Qudum. According to the Hanafi school, its default ruling is sunnah (not wajib or fard).
Sunnah here means a recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed, but omission does not invalidate Hajj nor require compensation.
2
Understand the condition for dropping
The text states: if the muhrim does not enter Makkah but goes directly to Arafat and performs wuquf, then Tawaf al-Qudum is dropped. The condition is that the pilgrim never entered Makkah before wuquf.
This applies to the one who bypasses Makkah entirely, not to one who enters but delays tawaf.
3
Locate the dalil (proof)
The hadith of Urwah ibn Mudarris: the Prophet confirmed that his Hajj was complete despite having gone directly to Arafat and Muzdalifah, without mentioning any tawaf. This indicates that Tawaf al-Qudum is not a required part of Hajj.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (qati' al-dalala) regarding the completeness of Hajj with wuquf and the prayer at Muzdalifah.
4
Apply the analogy (qiyas) with tahiyyat al-masjid
The commentary draws an analogy: just as tahiyyat al-masjid (prayer of greeting the mosque) is not required if one does not enter the mosque, Tawaf al-Qudum is not required for one who does not enter Makkah. This reinforces that the tawaf is linked to entering Makkah.
This is a clear qiyas jali (obvious analogy) based on the shared 'illah (effective cause) of entering a sacred place.
5
Confirm the consequence: no dam
Since Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah, leaving it does not require a dam (sacrificial animal). Dam is only required for omitting a wajib act.
This is a key Hanafi principle: only wajib (or fard) omissions incur compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان لم يدخل المحرم مكة وتوجه الى عرفات ووقف بها على ما قدمناه سقط عنه طواف القدوم ولا عن الحائض اگر محرم مکہ میں داخل نہ ہو اور عرفات کی طرف متوجہ ہو جائے اور وہاں اس طرح وقوف عرفہ کرلے جیسا کہ ہم نے پہلے بیان کیا تو اس سے طواف قدوم ساقط ہو جائے گا اور طواف قدوم کے چھوڑنے سے اس پر کچھ لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ ا کوئی محرم مکہ نہ آیا اور احرام باندھ کر سیدھا عرفات چلا گیا تو اس کا حج ہو گیا۔ اب اس پر طواف قدوم کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور طواف قدوم کے چھوڑنے سے دم بھی لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ (۱) طواف قدوم ملکہ آنے پر ہوتا ہے اور وہ مکہ آیا ہی نہیں اس لئے اس پر طواف قدوم نہیں ہے جیسے کوئی مسجد میں داخل ہو ہی نہیں تو اس پر تحیۃ المسجد لازم نہیں ہوگی۔ اور چونکہ طواف قدوم سنت ہے اس لئے سنت چھوڑنے پر دم لازم نہیں ہو گا (۲) اخبرنی عروة بن مضرس الطائي قال اتيت رسول الله بالموقف يعنى بجمع قلت جئت يا رسول الله من جبلی طی اکللت مطبتی و اتعبت نفسى والله ماتركت من حبل الا وقفت عليه فهل لى من حج فقال رسول الله من ادرك معنا هذه الصلوة واتى عرفات قبل ذلك ليلا او نهارا فقد تم حجه و قضى تفته
If the muhrim does not enter Makkah and proceeds to Arafat and stops there in the manner we have mentioned, then Tawaf al-Qudum is dropped from him, and also from the menstruating woman. If the muhrim did not come to Makkah and went straight to Arafat after putting on ihram, his Hajj is valid. Now he does not need to perform Tawaf al-Qudum, and no dam (sacrifice) is required for leaving it. (1) Tawaf al-Qudum is done upon entering Makkah, and he did not enter Makkah, so Tawaf al-Qudum is not required for him, just as if someone does not enter a mosque, tahiyyat al-masjid is not required. And since Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah, no dam is required for leaving a sunnah. (2) Urwah ibn Mudarris al-Ta'i narrated: I came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) at the standing place, meaning at Muzdalifah. I said: O Messenger of Allah, I have come from the mountain of Tayy, I have exhausted my mount and tired myself. By Allah, I have left no mountain except I stood upon it. Do I have a Hajj? The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Whoever prays this prayer with us and came to Arafat before that, by night or day, his Hajj is complete and he has fulfilled his obligation.
Source pages p. 421

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from hadith and analogy. It deals with the scenario where a pilgrim in ihram bypasses Makkah and goes directly to Arafat, performs wuquf there, and thus Tawaf al-Qudum (the arrival circumambulation) is dropped from him. The text also mentions 'and also from the menstruating woman' referring to Tawaf al-Wada', but the main focus is on Tawaf al-Qudum. The Urdu commentary explains that since Tawaf al-Qudum is a sunnah act that is tied to entering Makkah, and the pilgrim never entered Makkah, it is not required. The obligation of Hajj is fulfilled by wuquf at Arafat, and Tawaf al-Ziyarah remains as a fard. The commentary draws an analogy with tahiyyat al-masjid: if one does not enter the mosque, there is no obligation to pray tahiyyah. Since Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah, leaving it does not require a dam. The proof is the hadith of Urwah ibn Mudarris, who went directly to Arafat and then to Muzdalifah and the Prophet confirmed his Hajj, without mentioning Tawaf al-Qudum, indicating it is not obligatory. This hadith also demonstrates that wuquf at Arafat is essential for Hajj.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (Tawaf al-Qudum): The circumambulation performed upon arrival in Makkah by a pilgrim who comes from outside the Miqat, before going to Arafat.
دم (Dam): Sacrificial animal required to compensate for missing a wajib act of Hajj. Here, it is not required for leaving a sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It must be performed later, or else a dam is required.
B) It is dropped and no compensation is needed.
C) The Hajj is invalid without it.
D) It becomes fard instead of sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah, not wajib; if the pilgrim bypasses Makkah, it is dropped and no dam is required.

Time for Wuquf at Arafah and Catching Hajj
Defines the time for wuquf at Arafah and states that whoever catches it within that time has caught Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi time for wuquf at Arafah and apply it to determine whether a pilgrim has caught Hajj.

Core Idea
Even a brief moment between zawal on the 9th and fajr on the 10th suffices to catch Hajj.

Wuquf at Arafah is the essential pillar of Hajj. This lesson clarifies its precise timing according to the Hanafi school and the condition that makes Hajj valid. Understanding this time is crucial because missing it invalidates the entire pilgrimage. The lesson also presents the Prophetic proof that establishes the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that wuquf at Arafah is a fard (pillar) of Hajj without which the Hajj is invalid.
All schools agree it is a pillar, but timing differs.
2
Define the time window
The Hanafi time is from the decline of the sun (zawal) on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah to the dawn (fajr) of the 10th.
This is the widest Hanafi window; Shafi'is extend to fajr of the 9th.
3
Note the sufficiency of brief presence
Even a single minute of standing within that time, while in ihram, is enough to catch Hajj.
The text emphasizes 'one minute' to show no requirement of extended duration.
4
Recognize the proof
The hadith of Abdur Rahman ibn Ya'mar: 'Hajj is Arafah. Whoever comes before the dawn prayer of the night of Jam' has completed his Hajj.'
The phrase 'Hajj is Arafah' highlights that the act of wuquf defines Hajj.
5
Link to remaining fard
After valid wuquf, Tawaf al-Ziyarah (also fard) can be performed later; delaying it may require a dam.
Wuquf is the primary pillar; Tawaf is separate but necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ادرك الوقوف بعرفة ما بين زوال الشمس من يوم عرفة الى طلوع الفجر من يوم النحر فقد ادرك الحج جس نے وقوف عرفہ پایا نویں ذی الحجہ کے سورج کے زوال کے بعد سے دسویں تاریخ کے طلوع فجر سے پہلے تک تو اس نے حج پا لیا۔ ر وقوف عرفہ فرض ہے اور اس کا وقت نویں ذی الحجہ کے سورج کے ڈھلنے کے بعد سے دسویں ذی الحجہ کے طلوع فجر سے پہلے پہلے تک ہے ۔ اس لئے اس دوران جس نے احرام کے ساتھ ایک منٹ کے لئے بھی وقوف عرفہ کر لیا اس کا حج ہو گیا۔ اب فرض میں سے طواف زیارت باقی ہے جو کبھی بھی کرے گا تو فرض ادا ہو جائے گا اگر چہ بے وقت کرنے سے دم لازم ہوگا۔ (۱) ایک حدیث تو او پر مسئلہ نمبر ۷۵ میں گزری جس میں تھا یہ تھا کہ دسویں ذی الحجہ سے پہلے دن یا رات میں وقوف عرفہ کر لیا تو اس کا حج ہو گیا (۲) عن عبد الرحمن بن يعمر الديلي قال اتيت النبي الله ص هو بعرفة فجاء ناس او نفر من اهل نجد فامروا رجلا فـنـادی رسول الله كيف الحج فامر رجلا فنادى الحج الحج يوم عرفة ومن جاء قبل صلوة الصبح من ليلة جمع فتم حجه اس حدیث میں لیلتہ جمع سے مراد عرفات کے بعد کی رات ہے۔ اس لئے اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نویں ذی الحجہ کا دن اور دسویں ذی الحجہ کی رات میں طلوع فجر سے پہلے ایک منٹ کے لئے وقوف عرفہ کر لیا تو حج پالیا۔ ت لیلہ جمع : مزدلفہ کی رات۔
Whoever catches the standing at Arafah between the time of the sun's decline on the day of Arafah until the dawn of the day of Nahr has caught the Hajj. Whoever caught wuquf at Arafah from after zawal on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah until before fajr on the 10th, he has caught the Hajj. And wuquf at Arafah is fard, and its time is from after the sun's decline on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah until before fajr on the 10th of Dhul-Hijjah. Therefore, whoever during this time performed wuquf at Arafah for even one minute while in ihram, his Hajj is valid. Now from the fard, Tawaf al-Ziyarah remains; whenever he performs it, the fard will be fulfilled, even if performing it late requires a dam. (1) A hadith has passed in problem no. 75 that if one performs wuquf at Arafah before the 10th, by day or night, his Hajj is complete. (2) From Abdur Rahman ibn Ya'mar al-Dili: I came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) while he was at Arafah. Some people from Najd came and instructed a man to call out to the Messenger of Allah: 'How is Hajj?' He ordered a man to call out: 'Hajj is (the standing at) Arafah. Whoever comes before the dawn prayer on the night of Jam' (Muzdalifah), his Hajj is complete.' In this hadith, 'laylat jam' refers to the night after Arafat. So it is known from this hadith that if one performs wuquf at Arafah for a minute on the day of the 9th or the night of the 10th before fajr, he has caught the Hajj.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from two hadiths regarding the time of wuquf at Arafah. It first states the ruling: whoever catches wuquf between the zawal (decline) of the sun on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah and the fajr of the 10th (the day of Nahr) has caught Hajj. The text clarifies that wuquf at Arafah is fard (obligatory pillar) of Hajj, and its established time is from zawal on the 9th until fajr on the 10th. Even a brief moment of wuquf within this period suffices, as long as the person is in ihram. The remaining fard after wuquf is Tawaf al-Ziyarah, which can be performed later, but delaying it without excuse requires a dam. The proof is the famous hadith from the Prophet: 'Hajj is Arafah' (from the hadith of Abdur Rahman ibn Ya'mar) which establishes that the essence of Hajj is the standing at Arafah, and anyone who comes before the dawn of the 10th has completed his Hajj. The Urdu commentary reinforces that even a single minute of standing is sufficient. The author also refers to a previous hadith (from section 75) to support the same point.

Key Terms
وقوف عرفة (Wuquf bi-Arafah): The act of standing or being present at the plain of Arafah on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah, which is a fard of Hajj.
طواف الزيارة (Tawaf al-Ziyarah): The obligatory circumambulation performed after wuquf and after coming from Mina, also called Tawaf al-Ifadah.
ليلۃ جمع (Laylat Jam'): The night of Muzdalifah, i.e., the night following the day of Arafah (the 10th night of Dhul-Hijjah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The time for wuquf at Arafah in the Hanafi school is from the decline of the sun on the 9th to the dawn of the 10th; a brief presence within this window suffices to catch Hajj.

Wuquf Without Awareness: Presence Suffices
Ruling on the validity of wuquf for the unaware pilgrim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that mere physical presence in Arafah during the wuquf time suffices for Hajj, even without awareness.

Core Idea
Presence in Arafah with ihram at the right time suffices; awareness is not required.

This lesson addresses a common question: if a pilgrim passes through Arafah while asleep or unconscious, does their Hajj count? The Hanafi school answers clearly: the physical presence in the area of Arafah during the appointed time, while in the state of ihram, is sufficient for the pillar of wuquf. Intention or awareness of the location is not a condition. This ruling brings ease to pilgrims who may be ill, exhausted, or simply unaware.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is passing through Arafah (ijtaza bi-Arafah) while in ihram during the wuquf time. The ruling is that this suffices for the wajib wuquf.
The text mentions three situations: sleeping, unconscious, and unknowing.
2
Extract the conditions for validity
From the passage, the conditions are: being in ihram, being in Arafah, and being present during the time of wuquf. Awareness is explicitly not required.
The condition of time is also emphasized: 'during the time of Arafah'.
3
Contrast with common misconception
Many assume that wuquf requires conscious standing and intention. The text clarifies that mere presence, even without knowledge, fulfills the obligation.
This is based on the Hanafi view that wuquf is a physical presence, not an act requiring niyyah.
4
Apply the ruling to a concrete scenario
If a pilgrim in ihram falls asleep on a bus that drives through Arafah during the wuquf time, their wuquf is valid. They do not need to repeat or compensate.
5
Note the incomplete text but complete ruling
The source text cuts off at 'therefore...' but the ruling is already established: the passing suffices. The ellipsis may have contained further explanation or additional scenarios.
The ruling is consistent with other Hanafi sources like Al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن اجتاز بعرفة جو عرفہ سے گزر گیا اس حال میں کہ وہ سویا ہوا ہے یا اس پر بیہوشی طاری ہے یا وہ نہیں جانتا ہے کہ یہ عرفہ ہے تو یہ گزرنا وقوف عرفہ کے لئے کافی ہو جائے گا۔ احرام کے ساتھ عرفات کے اوقات میں عرفات سے گزر گیا لیکن اس کو پتہ نہیں چلا کہ یہ میدان عرفات ہے۔ مثلا وہ سواری پر سویا ہوا تھا یا اس پر بیہوشی طاری تھی یا اس کو معلوم ہی نہیں تھا کہ یہ میدان عرفات ہے پھر بھی چونکہ احرام کے ساتھ اوقات عرفہ میں گزرا ہے اس لئے
Whoever passes through Arafah, and he is sleeping, or is unconscious, or does not know that it is Arafah, this passing will suffice for the standing at Arafah. He passed through Arafah with ihram during the time of Arafah, but he did not realize that it is the plain of Arafat. For example, he was asleep on his mount, or he was unconscious, or he did not know that it is the plain of Arafat. Nevertheless, since he passed through with ihram during the time of Arafah, therefore...
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement clarifying that the actual presence in Arafah during the prescribed time is sufficient for wuquf, even if the person is unaware of it. The text considers three scenarios: sleeping, unconscious, or simply not knowing that the location is Arafah. In all these cases, the passing through Arafah during the wuquf period while in ihram is considered valid wuquf. The reasoning is that the essence of wuquf is being present in the area of Arafah in a state of ihram during the designated time; intention or awareness is not a condition for the validity of this pillar. This is based on the principle that acts of worship that involve only bodily presence (like staying) do not require specific intent. The text ends abruptly but the ruling is complete: the passing suffices. This is consistent with Hanafi fiqh as found in other works like Al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
اجتاز (ijtaza): Passed through, traversed, or crossed; in this context, passing through the area of Arafah.
وقوف عرفة (Wuquf bi-Arafah): The standing at Arafah; here it is considered valid by mere presence without active standing or awareness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Time of Wuquf at Arafah: Ruling and Proof
Ruling on the time window for valid wuquf at Arafah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi time window for valid wuquf at Arafah and identify the hadith evidence that supports it.

Core Idea
Wuquf at Arafah is valid from zawal of 9th Dhul Hijjah until Fajr of 10th; momentary presence suffices.

The pillar (fard) of wuquf at Arafah has a defined time window that the Hanafi school extracts from the Prophet's own words. In this lesson, we examine the ruling and its proof, noting how the hadith extends the time beyond sunset to dawn. We will also briefly contrast the Shafi'i position to clarify the school's unique stance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Wuquf at Arafah is a fard (pillar) of Hajj. Determine its ruling level and the consequence of performing it correctly.
Hanafis: wuquf is fard, not wajib; missing it invalidates Hajj.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary evidence cited: the hadith of Abdur Rahman bin Ya'mur. Note its source and chain.
The hadith is a Sunnah ahad, zanni in both transmission and meaning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith wording yields the Hanafi time frame. Focus on 'al-Hajju yawmu Arafah' and 'man jaa'a qabla salat al-subh min laylati jam''.
The phrase extends the time to the dawn after Arafah night (i.e., Fajr of 10th).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify that Imam al-Shafi'i restricts wuquf to the night of 10th only (after sunset of 9th). State his proof basis.
Shafi'i sees the day as a preparation; the night is the essential time.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Explain why the Hanafi position is mufta bihi: the hadith explicitly includes the day, and the Prophet's action confirms daytime wuquf.
The companion in the hadith omitted tawaf al-qudum without penalty, showing wuquf alone suffices.

And whoever catches the standing at Arafah between the zawal of the sun on the day of Arafah and the dawn of the day of Nahr has caught the Hajj. (76) Whoever catches wuquf at Arafah from after zawal on 9th Dhul Hijjah to before Fajr of 10th has performed Hajj. Wuquf at Arafah is fard, its time is from after zawal on 9th to before Fajr of 10th. So during this time, whoever stands at Arafah even for a minute in ihram, his Hajj is valid. Remaining fard is tawaf al-ziyarah, which whenever performed fulfills the fard, though a dam is due if delayed. (1) A hadith in issue 75 mentioned that standing at Arafah on the day or night before 10th suffices. (2) From Abdur Rahman bin Ya'mur ad-Dili: I came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) at Arafah, some people from Najd came and asked about Hajj. He ordered a caller to announce: 'Hajj is the day of Arafah; whoever comes before the dawn prayer of the night of Jam' has completed his Hajj.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi) This hadith indicates that the time extends to before Fajr of the night after Arafah.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage contains a ruling and its proof. The author states that the time for wuquf at Arafah, which is a fard of Hajj, begins at zawal (noon) on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah and extends until the break of dawn (Fajr) on the 10th (Yawm an-Nahr). Anyone who makes wuquf within this period, even momentarily while in ihram, has validly performed Hajj. The remaining fard is tawaf al-ziyarah, which if delayed incurs a dam but the Hajj remains valid. The author then provides evidence from a hadith of Abdur Rahman bin Ya'mur, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) defined Hajj as the day of Arafah and stated that one who arrives before the dawn prayer of the night of Jam' (i.e., the night after Arafah, which is the night of Muzdalifah) has completed Hajj. This hadith establishes the time limit. The passage also clarifies that tawaf al-qudum is sunnah, not wajib, as the companion in the hadith omitted it without penalty.

Key Terms
وقوف (wuquf): Standing (or being present) at Arafah, a pillar of Hajj.
عرفة (Arafah): A plain near Mecca; the location for the essential standing during Hajj.
زوال (zawal): The moment when the sun passes the meridian (declines from its zenith).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Only on the day of 9th Dhul Hijjah until Fajr of 10th
D) From zawal of 9th Dhul Hijjah to sunset of 9th

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, wuquf at Arafah is valid from zawal of 9th Dhul Hijjah to Fajr of 10th, based on the Prophet's explicit hadith.

Wuquf While Unaware: Presence, Not Consciousness, Defines the Pillar
Ruling that passing through Arafah suffices for wuquf even without awareness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wuquf for an unaware person and identify the essential condition of ihram for its validity.

Core Idea
Passing through Arafah in ihram suffices for wuquf, even if asleep, unconscious, or unaware of the place.

The Hanafi school holds that the essence of wuquf is physical presence within the boundaries of Arafah during the appointed time. Consciousness of the location is not required. However, a critical condition must be met: the person must be in a state of ihram. This lesson examines the ruling and its proofs, including the hadith of Urwah bin Mudarris and the athar of Ibn Umar.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
The matn declares that if a person passes through Arafah while asleep, unconscious, or unaware it is Arafah, that passage suffices for wuquf. Identify this as the Hanafi position.
The ruling applies regardless of whether the person intentionally stood or knew the location.
2
Identify the essential condition
The commentary stresses that the person must be in ihram at the time of passing. Without ihram, the wuquf does not suffice, even if physically present.
Ihram is a prerequisite; if unconscious and not put into ihram by a companion, the wuquf is invalid.
3
Examine the dalil
Two proofs are cited: the hadith of Urwah bin Mudarris, where the Prophet said passing through the plain of Arafah suffices, and the athar of Ibn Umar stating that stopping at Arafah at night completes the Hajj even if one misses Muzdalifah.
The wajh al-dalalah is that physical presence, not awareness, is the operative requirement.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools require intentional standing with awareness of the place. In the Hanafi school, inadvertent passage suffices, provided ihram is present.
This ikhtilaf affects pilgrims who may be unconscious or unaware during the wuquf period.
5
Apply to a scenario
A pilgrim falls unconscious before entering Arafah but is already in ihram; his companion brings him through the plain in a vehicle during the appointed time. His wuquf is valid.
Conversely, if the same pilgrim was not in ihram (e.g., unconscious before ihram and no one performed it for him), the wuquf is invalid.

(77) Whoever passes through Arafah while he is asleep, or unconscious, or does not know it is Arafah, that passage suffices for wuquf. He passed through Arafat in its time with ihram, but was not aware it was Arafat, e.g., he was asleep on his ride, or unconscious, or unaware; yet because he passed in ihram during the time of wuquf, his wuquf is valid and he has performed Hajj. (1) In issue 75, the hadith of Urwah bin Mudarris at-Ta'i mentioned: 'I explored all mountains; is my Hajj valid?' He said that passing through Arafat suffices. (2) The essence is wuquf, whether one knows the place or not. (3) From Abdullah bin Umar: 'If a man stops at Arafah at night, his Hajj is complete, even if he did not catch the people at Muzdalifah.' (Musannaf ibn Abi Shaybah) This indicates that even without awareness of the location, passing through suffices. Note: He must be in ihram, either by himself or by his companion on his behalf; otherwise, wuquf does not suffice.

Commentary
This passage expands on the ruling that wuquf at Arafah is valid even if one is not conscious of being there. The matn states that one who passes through Arafah while asleep, unconscious, or unaware that it is Arafah, his passage counts as wuquf. The sharh provides evidence: hadith of Urwah bin Mudarris and athar of Ibn Umar, both indicating that presence in Arafat during the time is the essence, not awareness. The commentary adds a crucial condition: the person must be in ihram. If he is unconscious and was not put into ihram by a companion, then his passage does not count. This guards against the misunderstanding that mere physical presence without ihram suffices.

Women's Ihram: Covering Head and Uncovering Face
Ruling that women in ihram cover their heads but uncover their faces, with proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a woman's head and face covering during ihram, cite the supporting hadith, and explain the conditions and wisdom behind the rule.

Core Idea
In ihram, a woman covers her head but uncovers her face — unless non-mahram men approach, then she covers temporarily.

The general rule for women in Hajj and Umrah is that they follow the same regulations as men, except where modesty requires otherwise. One key exception is head and face covering. This lesson explains the Hanafi position: women must cover their heads, but they should keep their faces uncovered as the default, with a temporary cover when necessary to avoid fitna. We will also examine the hadith evidence and the wisdom behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two differences from men
Read the opening sentence: a woman in ihram does not uncover her head (unlike man) and she uncovers her face (unlike man who does not cover face). Pinpoint these two specific rulings.
The phrase 'غير انها لا تكشف رأسها وتكشف وجهها' is the core.
2
Understand the wisdom behind the rule
The commentary explains that the face is uncovered to show equality between free and slave women before Allah. Consider why this distinction is made in the state of ihram.
This is a reason based on analogy with slave women who do not cover face.
3
Note the exception for non-mahram men
The text states that if a non-mahram man approaches, a woman should cover her face. Identify the scenario and the evidence from the hadith of Aisha.
The hadith shows that women would lower their jilbab to cover the face when men passed and uncover when they left.
4
Analyze the dalil (proof)
Examine the hadith of Aisha: it is an ahad hadith with zanni thubut and dalala. Determine how it supports the ruling. The key is the practice of the women companions showing that face covering is not obligatory in ihram.
The wajh al-dalalah: the default state is uncovered; covering is situational.
5
Compare with Shafi'i position
The Hanafi school differs from the Shafi'i, which requires women to cover their faces in ihram. Understand the ikhtilaf and the Hanafi tarjih.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both schools have evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

میدان عرفات سے گزر گیا تو حج ہو جائے گا۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ بغیر جانے کہ یہ میدان عرفات ہے وہاں سے گزر گیا تو حج ہو جائے گا (۲) اصل وقوف ہے چاہے میدان کا علم ہو یا نہ ہو (۳) عن عبد الله بن عمر قال اذا وقف الرجل بعرفة بليل قد تم حجه وان لم يدرك الناس بجمع (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۵۱ امن قال از اوقف بعرفه قبل ان يطلع الفجر فقد ادرک ، ج ثالث ، ص ۲۱۸، نمبر ۱۳۶۷۳) اس اثر میں ہے کہ عرفہ میں لوگوں کو نہ پایا اور وہاں سے گزر گیا تو حج پورا ہو گیا نوٹ بیہوشی کے عالم میں یا سونے کے عالم میں محرم ہونا چاهئے ۔ یا کم از کم ساتھی دوست ان کی جانب سے احرام باندھ لے تو حج ہوگا۔ اور اگر ساتھی دوست نے بھی ان کی جانب سے احرام نہیں باندھا اور خود بھی احرام نہیں باندھ پایا تھا تو وقوف عرفہ کرنے سے حج نہیں ہوگا۔ : منظمی علیه : بیہوشی طاری ہوگئی اس پے، انماء سے مشتق ہے۔ اجتاز : تجاوز سے مشتق ہے گزرگیا، تجاوز کر گیا۔ [۱۸۲) (۷۸) عورت ان تمام مسائل میں مرد کی طرح ہے علاوہ یہ کہ وہ اپنا سر نہیں کھولے گی اور اپنا چہرہ کھولے گی۔ جس طرح احکام مردوں پر لازم ہیں اسی طرح عورتوں پر بھی لازم ہیں۔ البتہ جہاں ان کے ستر یا نسوانیت کے خلاف ہے وہاں عورتوں کا مسئلہ مردوں سے الگ ہے۔ اسی میں یہ چند مسائل ہیں جو ذکر کئے جارہے ہیں کہ مرد احرام کی حالت میں سر کھولے گا لیکن عورت سر ڈھانکے گی ۔ کیونکہ سرکھولنا ستر کے خلاف ہے۔ البتہ چہرہ کھولے گی ۔ لیکن مرد سامنے آجائے تو چہرہ پھر الیگی۔ تا کہ اجنبی مرد اس کے چہرے کو نہ دیکھے۔ یا چہرہ سے دور ہٹا کر اس طرح کپڑا لٹکائے گی کہ چہرے کے ساتھ میں نہ کرے البتہ مردوں سے پردہ بھی ہو جائے۔ کت اس کی حکمت یہ ہے کہ باندی کے لئے چہرے پر کپڑا ڈالنا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے شریف اور آزاد عورت بھی اللہ کے دربار میں چہرہ کھول کر جائے تا کہ باندی اور آزاد دونوں اللہ کے حضور میں برابر ہو جائیں۔ اس کا یہ مطلب نہیں ہے کہ آزاد عورتیں ہر جگہ اپنا چہرہ کھولے پھریں اور ستر کے خلاف کام کریں۔ عن عائشة قالت كان الركبان يمرون بنا ونحن مع رسول الله له فاذا محرمات حاذوا بنا سدلت احدينا جلبابها من رأسها على وجهها فاذا جاوزونا کشفناه (ج) (ابوداؤد، باب فی الحرمة تغطي وجهها ص ۲۶۱ نمبر ۱۸۳۳) اس حدیث
(78) The woman is like the man in all these matters except that she does not uncover her head and she uncovers her face. The woman is like the man in all rulings. However, where it conflicts with her modesty or femininity, the rule differs. Among these: a man uncovers his head in ihram, but a woman covers her head. She uncovers her face, but if a non-mahram man approaches, she covers it. The wisdom is that a slave woman does not cover her face, so free women also go before Allah with face uncovered to show equality. This does not mean free women may go about with faces uncovered in general. From Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her): Caravans would pass by us while we were with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in ihram; when they came near, each of us would lower her jilbab from her head to her face, and when they passed, we would uncover it. (Abu Dawud no. 1833)
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage states the rule for women in ihram: they are like men in all acts of Hajj, except that they cover their heads (unlike men who uncover) and they uncover their faces (unlike normal hijab). The commentary explains the wisdom: to distinguish free and slave women in worship, showing equality before Allah. However, if non-mahram men approach, a woman should cover her face temporarily. The hadith of Aisha supports this practice: she and other women would cover their faces when men passed, then uncover afterward. This ruling is specific to ihram; outside of ihram, a woman must cover her face if there is risk of fitna.

Key Terms
سدلت (saddalat): To let down or lower a garment over the face.
جلباب (jilbab): An outer garment that covers the body; used here to cover the face.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the default rule for a woman's face during ihram?
A) She must cover her face at all times
B) She uncovers her face, but covers it when non-mahram men pass
C) She must keep her face covered except during tawaf
D) She covers her face only when praying

Key Takeaway
A woman in ihram must cover her head; she uncovers her face by default but may cover it temporarily if non-mahram men are present to avoid fitna.

Woman's Voice in Talbiyah
Ruling on women not raising voice in talbiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women raising their voice in talbiyah during Hajj, explain the reason for this ruling (fitna), and identify the proof from the athar of Ibn Umar.

Core Idea
A woman must not raise her voice in talbiyah to avoid fitna; it is makruh tanzih.

This passage from a Hanafi fiqh text discusses a critical aspect of women's performance of Hajj: the recitation of talbiyah. While the passage begins with a related ruling about face covering, the central focus is on the voice. The legal reasoning is based on the potential for fitna when a woman's voice attracts the attention of non-mahram men. We will explore the ruling, its evidence, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
What is talbiyah? What specific ruling is given about a woman's voice during talbiyah? Identify that the act is the recitation of 'Labbaik Allahumma labbaik' while in ihram, and the ruling is about the volume of her voice.
The passage explicitly states: 'ولا ترفع صوتها بالتلبية' – she should not raise her voice.
2
State the Hanafi position
What is the hukm level of raising the voice? According to the Hanafi school, it is makruh tanzih (disliked, not sinful) for a woman to raise her voice in talbiyah. The preferred practice is to recite softly.
Makruh tanzih means it is better to avoid, but if done, it is not a sin and does not invalidate the hajj.
3
Locate the proof
What evidence is cited? The proof is an athar from Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) recorded by Darqutni and Bayhaqi: 'A woman should not ascend Safa and Marwah, and should not raise her voice in talbiyah.'
The hadith is considered zanni al-thubut (plausible transmission) and zanni al-dalalah (plausible indication).
4
Analyze the proof
How does this athar support the ruling? The explicit prohibition 'لا ترفع' indicates that raising the voice is to be avoided. In Hanafi usul, such a prohibition (nahy) without evidence of haram indicates karahah tanzihiyyah.
The same hadith also includes a ruling about not ascending Safa and Marwah, which is specific to the context.
5
Note the reason behind the ruling
Why should a woman not raise her voice? The text explains: 'A woman's voice has attraction for men.' If she recites loudly, non-mahram men may turn to her, leading to fitna (temptation). Therefore, quiet recitation is prescribed.
The reason (illa) is the prevention of fitna, which aligns with the broader maqasid of preserving modesty and avoiding harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۶۸۳] (۷۹) ولا ترفع صوتها بالتلبية
سے معلوم ہوا کہ محرمہ عورت چہرہ کھلا رکھے اور کوئی اجنبی مرد سامنے آئے تو چہرہ سے دور کر کے چادر وغیرہ چہرہ پر لٹکا دے اس طرح سے کہ کپڑا چہرے سے مس نہ ہو (۲) عن ابن عمر ان النبی الا الله قال ليس على المرأة احرام الا في وجهها (الف) (دارقطنی ، کتاب الحج ج ثانی ص ۲۵۷ نمبر ۲۷۳۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت کا احرام اس کے چہرے میں ہے اس لئے وہ کپڑا چہرے سے دور رکھے گی۔ [۶۸۳] (۷۹) اور تلبیہ میں اپنی آواز بلند نہ کرے۔ عورت کی آواز میں مرد کے لئے کشش ہوتی ہے اس لئے وہ زور سے تلبیہ پڑھے گی تو اجنبی مرد اس کی طرف متوجہ ہو نگے ۔ اس لئے عورت زور سے تلبیہ نہ پڑھے وہ آہستہ آہستہ پڑھے (۲) عن ابن عمر قال لا تصعد المرأة فوق الصفا والمروة ولا ترفع صوتها بالتلبية (ب) (دار قطنی، کتاب الحج ج ثانی ص ۲۵۹ نمبر ۲۷۴ رسن للبیھقی ، باب المرأة لا ترفع صوتها بالتلبية ج خامس ص ۷۲، نمبر ۹۰۳۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت تلبیہ میں آواز بلند نہیں کرے گی۔
[683] (79) She should not raise her voice in talbiyah. From this it is known that a woman in ihram should keep her face open, and if a non-mahram man comes in front, she should turn her face away and hang a cloth etc. over her face such that the cloth does not touch her face. (2) From Ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no ihram for a woman except in her face' (Darqutni). From this hadith it is known that a woman's ihram is in her face, so she will keep the cloth away from her face. [683] (79) And she should not raise her voice in talbiyah. A woman's voice has attraction for men, so if she recites talbiyah loudly, non-mahram men will turn to her. Therefore, a woman should not recite talbiyah loudly; she should recite it softly. (2) From Ibn Umar: 'A woman should not ascend Safa and Marwah, and should not raise her voice in talbiyah' (Darqutni, Bayhaqi). From this athar it is known that a woman will not raise her voice in talbiyah.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling with proof regarding women's talbiyah in ihram. It begins by noting that a woman in ihram must keep her face uncovered, but if a non-mahram man approaches, she should cover her face with a cloth without it touching her skin, citing a hadith from Ibn Umar. The specific ruling here is that she should not raise her voice in talbiyah. The reason given is that her voice might attract men, so she should recite softly to avoid fitna. The proof is an athar from Ibn Umar stating that a woman should not raise her voice in talbiyah. This ruling is specific to Hanafi fiqh, where a woman's voice is considered 'awrah in certain contexts, though the madhhab generally holds it not 'awrah for recitation. The key point is to prevent attraction of non-mahram men.

Key Terms
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The recitation of 'Labbaik Allahumma labbaik...' by a person in ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why should a woman not raise her voice in talbiyah according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because her voice is 'awrah and must be hidden.
B) Because it may attract non-mahram men, leading to fitna.
C) Because talbiyah is only for men.
D) Because she is not required to recite talbiyah at all.

Key Takeaway
A woman in ihram should recite talbiyah quietly to avoid fitna; raising the voice is makruh tanzih.
