Ruling on Women Not Performing Ramal or Running in Sa'i
Ruling on women not doing ramal and not running in sa'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women's ramal and running in sa'i and explain the proof from the hadith of Ibn Umar.

Core Idea
Women must avoid ramal and running during hajj and umrah because modesty (satr) takes precedence.

In this passage, we learn that while men are encouraged to walk briskly (ramal) during tawaf and run between the green milestones during sa'i, women are exempt from these acts. The reason is rooted in the principle of satr (modesty) — a woman's worship should not involve physical movements that draw attention to her. The Hanafi school supports this with a clear narration from Ibn Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and ruling
The passage explicitly states that women should not do ramal in tawaf nor run between the two green milestones during sa'i. This is a prohibition (makruh tanzih).
Ramal is brisk walking with shoulder movement; running is between the green markers on Safa and Marwah.
2
Locate the proof
The proof is a hadith from Ibn Umar: 'ليس على النساء رمل بالبيت ولا بين الصفا والمروة' (There is no ramal for women in the House nor between Safa and Marwah). This is a sunnah ahad narration recorded by Darqutni and Bayhaqi.
The hadith is quoted in the text.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The negation 'ليس على' (not upon) indicates that the act is not prescribed for women. In Hanafi usul, this negation implies that the act is not required and should be avoided, leading to the ruling of makruh tanzih.
The dalala is zanni, but the ruling is supported by the principle of satr.
4
Understand the rationale
The text states that ramal and running go against a woman's modesty (satr). The underlying principle is that women should not perform actions that attract attention during worship.
This rationale is independent of the hadith and also used as a basis for the ruling.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school does not prohibit women from doing ramal or running; it is considered permissible but not recommended. The Hanafi school is stricter due to the modesty concern.
This is a point of ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۶۸۴] (۸۰) ولا ترمل في الطواف ولا تسعى بين الميلين الاخضرين
(۶۸۴ (۸۰) طواف میں اکثر کر نہیں چلے گی اور نہ میلین اخضرین کے درمیان دوڑے گی ۔
ان مرد طواف قدوم میں پہلے تین شوط میں رمل کرتے ہیں اور اکثر کر چلتے ہیں لیکن اکثر کر چلنا عورت کے ستر کے خلاف ہے اس لئے وہ رمل نہیں کرے گی۔ اسی طرح صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان سعی کرتے وقت میلین اخضرین میں عورت نہیں دوڑے گی کیونکہ یہ اس کے ستر کے خلاف
ہے۔
(1) عن ابن عمر قال ليس على النساء رمل بالبيت ولا بين الصفا والمروة (ج) (دار قطنی ، کتاب الحج حج ثانی ص ۲۰۸ نمبر ۲۷۴۰ / باب نمبر ۲۹۴ رسن للبیھقی ، باب المرأة تطوف وسعی لیلا اذا كانت مشهورة بالجمال ولا ریل علیھاج خامس ص ۷ ۷ے نمبر ۹۰۵۵) اس ار سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت نہ رل کرے گی اور نہ صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان دوڑے گی ۔
ا میلین اخضرین : صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان دوہری بتیاں لگی ہوئی ہیں جہاں سعی کرنے والے تیز چلتے ہیں۔
[684] (80) She should not do ramal in tawaf and should not run between the two green milestones. (684 (80) She will not walk briskly in tawaf, and not run between the two green milestones. Men do ramal in the first three circuits of tawaf al-qudum and walk briskly, but walking briskly is against a woman's modesty (satr), so she will not do ramal. Similarly, during sa'i between Safa and Marwah, a woman should not run between the two green milestones because it is against her modesty. (1) From Ibn Umar: 'There is no ramal for women in the House (Kaaba) nor between Safa and Marwah' (Darqutni, Bayhaqi). From this athar it is known that a woman will not do ramal nor run between Safa and Marwah. The two green milestones: the two green lamps placed between Safa and Marwah where those performing sa'i walk quickly.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling that women should not perform ramal (walking briskly) in tawaf nor run between the two green milestones during sa'i. The reason given is that such actions would go against a woman's modesty (satr), as they would attract attention. Men are required to do ramal in the first three circuits, but women are exempt from this and should walk normally. The proof is a narration from Ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly negated any ramal for women in tawaf or between Safa and Marwah. The Hanafi school emphasizes that women's worship should be concealed and not involve physical exertion that draws attention.

Key Terms
رمل (ramal): Walking briskly with short steps and shoulder movement, done by men in the first three circuits of tawaf.
میلین اخضرین (al-milayn al-akhdarayn): The two green markers (originally lamps) between Safa and Marwah where runners would run.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is not prescribed in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Women should not perform ramal in tawaf nor run between the green markers in sa'i to preserve modesty, based on the hadith of Ibn Umar and the principle of satr.

Women’s Head Shaving Prohibited: Only Trimming Allowed
Ruling with proof on women's hair trimming vs shaving.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women's hair removal during ihram and explain the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Women must not shave their heads in Hajj or Umrah; they only trim a fingertip-length of hair.

In Hajj and Umrah, men shave or trim their heads, but the ruling for women is different. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position: women must not shave, and the only valid act is trimming (qasr). We will examine the direct proof from the Sunnah and understand why this ruling is unique to women.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being governed (hair removal for women in ihram) and what ruling applies (shaving is prohibited, trimming is required).
The act is part of exiting ihram after completing major rituals (rami, dhabh, sa'i).
2
Locate the primary dalil
Identify the hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'There is no shaving for women; only trimming is for women.' This is the direct textual evidence.
The hadith is related by Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi, considered sound.
3
Analyze the linguistic indication (wajh al-dalalah)
Examine how the negation ('laysa') and restriction ('innama') in the hadith convey prohibition. 'Laysa' negates the prescription, and 'innama' confines the act to trimming, implying shaving is not allowed.
In Hanafi usul, 'laysa' in such context indicates a prohibition (tahrim) when linked to a command.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Contrast the Hanafi position with the Shafi'i view, which permits shaving for women. Understand the basis of each school’s interpretation.
The hadith's apparent prohibition is interpreted by Shafi'is as permissible due to qiyas with men.
5
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
Walk through a typical woman's Hajj journey: after rami and dhabh, she must trim a small portion of her hair (minimally the length of a fingertip) to exit ihram.
Shaving would be makruh tahrimi and sinful; she must avoid it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۶۸۵] (۸۱) ولا تحلق ولكن تقصر
[۶۸۵] (۸۱) اور عورت سر کا حلق نہ کرائے گی۔ حج میں رمی یا ذبح کے بعد محرم سر منڈاتے ہیں یا عمرے میں سعی کے بعد سر منڈواتے ہیں لیکن عورت اس وقت سر نہیں منڈوائے گی بلکہ صرف ایک انگلی کے برابر اپنے بال کاٹ کر احرام کھو لیگی (۱) بال منڈوانے سے عورت گنجی ہو جائے گی جو اس کی زینت کے خلاف ہے اس لئے صرف قصر کرے گی (۲) ان ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله ليس على النساء حلق انما على النساء التقصير (د)ابو داؤد باب الحلق والتقصير ص ۲۷۹ نمبر ۱۹۸۳ر ترمذی شریف باب ما جاء في كرابيتة الحلق للنساء ص ۱۸۲ نمبر ۹۱۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت حلق نہ کرائے وہ صرف تقصیر کرائے اور پورے بھر بال کٹوا کر حلال ہو جائے۔ حلق : سرکو منڈوانا۔ قصر : کچھ بال رکھنا کچھ کو کٹوانا۔
[685] (81) She should not shave (her head) but should trim (her hair). [685] (81) And the woman should not shave her head. In Hajj, after rami or dhabh, the muhrim shave their heads, or in Umrah after sa'i they get their heads shaved, but the woman will not shave her head at that time; rather, she will cut her hair by about a finger's length and then exit ihram. (1) Shaving the head would make the woman bald, which is against her adornment, so she will only do qasr. (2) From Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah said: 'There is no shaving for women; only trimming is for women' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). From this hadith it is known that a woman should not get her head shaved; she should only get her hair trimmed, and by cutting a bit of hair she becomes halal. Halq: shaving the head. Qasr: keeping some hair and cutting some.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that women should not shave their heads when leaving ihram; instead they should trim a small portion of their hair (qasr), about the length of a fingertip. Men are required to shave or trim, but women are prohibited from shaving because it would disfigure them and go against their beauty. The proof is a hadith from Ibn Abbas where the Prophet explicitly says there is no shaving for women, only trimming. The Hanafi school holds that women must not shave; it is makruh tahrimi or haram? The text implies prohibition due to the explicit hadith. The practical implication is that women cut a small lock of hair to exit ihram, avoiding the baldness that would result from shaving.

Key Terms
حلق (halq): Shaving the entire head
قصر (qasr): Trimming the hair, keeping some and cutting some (at least a finger's length)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Women must never shave their heads when leaving ihram; they must only trim a bit of hair.

Women's Hair Removal After Hajj/Umrah: Taqsir, Not Halq
Ruling on hair removal for women during Hajj/Umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hair removal for women after Hajj/Umrah and distinguish between halq and taqsir.

Core Idea
Women must shorten hair (taqsir), not shave (halq), to exit ihram.

In this short passage, the author cites hadith evidence to establish a clear rule for women completing Hajj or Umrah. Understanding the difference between halq (shaving the entire head) and taqsir (cutting some hair) is critical because the ruling differs fundamentally from that for men, who may shave. This lesson anchors a key fiqh distinction based on modesty and sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
What is the specific act being ruled upon? (Women's hair removal at the end of Hajj/Umrah). What is the hukm (obligatory, prohibited, etc.)?
The act is 'taqsir' (shortening) for women; 'halq' (shaving) is prohibited.
2
Locate the Dalil
What proof does the author cite? The passage references Abu Dawood and Tirmidhi hadith. Examine how the hadith supports the ruling.
The hadith explicitly states that women should not shave but only shorten.
3

Understand the precise meanings of 'halq' and 'taqsir' as used in the text. Halq = complete shave; Taqsir = cutting some hair, leaving some.
These definitions are essential for applying the ruling correctly.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Is there a difference of opinion? The Hanafi school prohibits halq for women, while the Shafi'i school permits it but dislikes it. Identify the thamarah (practical consequence).
For Hanafis, halq invalidates the ritual if done intentionally? Actually, it is a sin but the ihram is still exited? The text doesn't specify invalidation, but the ruling is clear.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement establishing the rule for women regarding hair removal after completing Hajj or Umrah. The author cites references from Abu Dawood and Tirmidhi as evidence. The ruling is that women must not shave their heads (halq); instead, they should only shorten a portion of their hair (taqsir). The definition of halq is shaving the entire head, while taqsir is cutting some hair and leaving the rest. This distinction is important because for men, shaving (halq) is permissible and often preferred, but for women, shaving is not allowed due to modesty and the prohibition of resembling men in appearance. The consequence is that a woman becomes halal (released from ihram) by performing taqsir, not halq.

Key Terms
حلق (halq): Shaving the head completely.
تقصير (taqsir): Cutting some hair, leaving some; shortening.

The Hanafi Proof for the Superiority of Qiran
Hanafi argument for Qiran superiority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the best form of Hajj and explain the four proofs supporting it.

Core Idea
Qiran combines Hajj and Umrah with greater difficulty, earning greater reward.

This passage addresses a well-known inter-madhhab dispute: which form of Hajj is most virtuous? The Hanafi school holds that Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram) is superior to Tamattu' and Ifrad. The author provides four proofs from the sunnah to support this view, emphasizing that greater difficulty yields greater reward.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and Hanafi position
The issue is which type of Hajj is most virtuous. The Hanafi position is that Qiran is superior. Note the definitions of the three types.
The author defines each term before presenting the argument.
2
Understand the four proofs
The text gives four proofs: (1) greater difficulty leads to greater reward; (2) the hadith of 'Umar where the Prophet was commanded to say 'Umrah in Hajj'; (3) the Prophet's own talbiyah for both; (4) the hadith of Umm Salamah commanding combination.
These are all dalil naqli (textual evidence) from the sunnah.
3
Note the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i considers Ifrad superior, citing the hadith of 'Aisha about the Farewell Pilgrimage.
The text mentions this briefly; it does not provide a full rebuttal.
4
Recognize the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: a Hanafi should prefer Qiran, while a Shafi'i would prefer Ifrad.
This is a school-based recommendation, not an obligation.

Chapter of Qiran
[686] (1) Qiran is superior according to us over Tamattu' and Ifrad.
Chapter of Qiran
Necessary note: One combines Hajj and Umrah in the same journey, and ties the ihram for Umrah with Hajj; this is called Qiran. The meaning of Qiran is to combine, because Hajj and Umrah are combined together, so it is called Qiran.
[686] (1) Qiran, according to us, is superior to Tamattu' and Ifrad.
One who ties only the ihram for Hajj is called Hajj Ifrad. One first ties the ihram for Umrah, completes it and opens the ihram, stays within the boundaries of the miqat, then in the months of Hajj ties the ihram for Hajj and completes Hajj, that is called Hajj Tamattu'. The meaning of Tamattu' is to take benefit, because one took benefit of opening the ihram after Umrah, so this Hajj is called Hajj Tamattu'. And the meaning of Qiran has passed above. According to us, Qiran is superior because:
(1) It contains more difficulty (mushaqqat), and with more difficulty, reward is greater. Therefore Hajj Qiran is superior.
(2) 'Umar said: I heard the Prophet (peace be upon him) in Wadi al-'Aqiq saying: 'Last night a messenger came to me from my Lord, and said: Pray in this blessed valley, and say: Umrah in Hajj.' (Bukhari, Bab Qawl al-Nabi...; Abu Dawud) This hadith shows that he was commanded to explicitly combine Umrah with Hajj, so Qiran is superior.
(3) Anas ibn Malik (may Allah be pleased with him) said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) reciting talbiyah for both Hajj and Umrah together, saying: 'Labbayk 'Umratan wa Hajjan, Labbayk 'Umratan wa Hajjan' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Muslim). This hadith indicates that the Prophet tied ihram for both Hajj and Umrah, showing that Qiran is superior.
(4) I entered upon Umm Salamah... I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) saying: 'Enter, O family of Muhammad, with Umrah in Hajj.' (Bayhaqi) This hadith also expresses the importance of Qiran.
Therefore, according to the Hanafis, Qiran is superior.
Benefit: Imam al-Shafi'i considers Ifrad to be superior. His evidence is the hadith: From 'Aisha that she said: We went out with the Messenger of Allah in the year of the Farewell Pilgrimage; some of us declared ihram for Umrah, and some...
Footnote: (a) I heard the Prophet... (b) I heard the Prophet... (c) I heard the Prophet...
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the best form of Hajj: Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah with one ihram), Tamattu' (performing Umrah first, then Hajj with separate ihram), or Ifrad (Hajj only). The author begins by defining these terms. Then he states the Hanafi position: Qiran is superior. He gives four proofs: (1) more difficulty means greater reward; (2) the hadith of Umar where the Prophet was commanded to say 'Umrah in Hajj'; (3) the Prophet's own practice of declaring ihram for both; (4) the hadith of Umm Salamah where the Prophet told his family to combine. Then he contrasts with Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds Ifrad superior, citing a hadith from Aisha about the Farewell Pilgrimage where people performed different types. The Hanafi position is that Qiran is the best because it combines the acts of worship in a single journey with greater effort. The practical consequence (thamarah) is that a Hanafi should prefer to perform Qiran if possible, while a Shafi'i would prefer Ifrad. The text does not provide a detailed response to Shafi'i's evidence, but simply states the difference.

Key Terms
قران (qiran): A type of Hajj where the pilgrim combines Hajj and Umrah with one ihram and one niyyah.
تمتع (tamattu'): A type of Hajj where the pilgrim performs Umrah first, exits ihram, then performs Hajj in the same year.
افراد (ifrad): A type of Hajj where the pilgrim performs only Hajj with a single ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which form of Hajj is most virtuous?
A) Ifrad
B) Tamattu'
C) Qiran
D) All are equal

Key Takeaway
According to Hanafis, Qiran is the most virtuous form of Hajj because it involves greater difficulty and is supported by explicit commands from the Prophet.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Qiran Superior: Hanafi Proofs and Rebuttals of Shafi'i and Maliki Views
States Hanafi view and rebuts Shafi'i and Maliki arguments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that Qiran is superior to both Tamattu' and Ifrad, and evaluate the proofs and counter-proofs from the Shafi'i and Maliki schools, applying the Hanafi rebuttal.

Core Idea
Qiran is the best Hajj form due to explicit Prophetic command and greater hardship.

This lesson explores the Hanafi view that Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram) is the most virtuous form of pilgrimage. While all three methods are valid, the Hanafis argue that Qiran is superior based on multiple hadiths and the principle of greater reward for greater hardship. We will also examine the proofs of the Shafi'i and Maliki schools and see how the Hanafis respond to them. This dispute is only about preference, not validity.

Guided Path
1
Define the three forms of Hajj
Clearly understand Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram), Tamattu' (Umrah first, then Hajj in separate ihrams), and Ifrad (only Hajj). These definitions are essential for following the dispute.
The terms appear in the first part of the source.
2
State the Hanafi position and its primary proof
The Hanafis hold Qiran as superior. The first proof is that Qiran involves greater hardship, and greater hardship earns greater reward. This is a general principle in Islam.
This is the first reason given in the passage.
3
Examine the three specific hadith proofs for Qiran
The author quotes three hadiths: (1) Umar's hadith about the command 'Umrah within Hajj', (2) Anas's hadith that the Prophet performed talbiyah for both Hajj and Umrah, (3) Umm Salamah's hadith commanding the family to combine. These show direct Prophetic command or practice.
These are the Hanafi dalil.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i proof and the Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i relies on Aisha's hadith that the Prophet performed Ifrad in the Farewell Pilgrimage. The Hanafi response: the hadith shows the Prophet's action, but the explicit commands to combine take precedence, and the Prophet may have done Ifrad for specific reasons.
This is the first dispute (vs Shafi'i).
5
Analyze the Maliki proof and the Hanafi response
Imam Malik relies on Quran 2:196 ('whoever performs Tamattu'...') and the hadith of Jabir and Aisha where the Prophet commanded those without hadi to perform Umrah. The Hanafi response: the Quranic verse is conditional and does not indicate preference; the command was for those without a hadi, while the Prophet himself combined, showing Qiran's superiority.
This is the second dispute (vs Maliki).
6
Conclude with the thamarah al-khilaf
All schools agree that all three forms are valid. The difference is only in preference (afdaliyyah). The Hanafis follow Qiran, Shafi'is follow Ifrad, Malikis follow Tamattu'. The Hanafi view is mufta bihi for Hanafis.
This is the practical outcome of the dispute.

[٦٨٦] (۱) قران ہمارے نزدیک تمتع اور افراد سے افضل ہے۔
صرف حج کا احرام باندھے تو اس کو حج افراد کہتے ہیں۔ پہلے عمرے کا احرام باندھے اس کو پوارا کر کے احرام کھول دے اور میقات کے حدود میں ٹھہرار ہے پھر اشہر حج میں حج کا احرام باندھے اور حج پورا کرے تو اس کو حج تمتع کہتے ہیں۔ تمتع کے معنی ہیں فائدہ اٹھانا، چونکہ اس نے عمرہ کے بعد احرام کھولنے کا فائدہ اٹھایا اس لئے اس حج کو حج تمتع کہتے ہیں۔ اور قرآن کے معنی اوپر گزرے، ہمارے نزدیک قرآن افضل ہونے کی۔
(۱) یہ ہے کہ اس میں مشقت زیادہ ہے اور زیادہ مشقت میں ثواب زیادہ ہوتا ہے اس لئے حج قران افضل ہے (۲) سمعت عمر يقول سمعت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بوادي العقيق يقول انا ني الليلة آت من ربى فقال صل فى هذا الوادى المبارك وقل عمرة في حجه (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب قول النبی بالحقیقی و اد مبارک ص ۲۰۷ نمبر ۵۳۴ اسرا بود او د شریف، باب فی الا قران ص ۲۵۷ نمبر ۱۸۰۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آپ کو باضابطہ عمرہ کونج کے ساتھ ملانے کا حکم دیا اس لئے قران افضل ہوگا (۳) عن انس بن مالك رضي الله عنه انهم سمعوه يقول سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يلبي بالحج والعمرة جميعا يقول لبيك عمره و حجا لبیک عمرة و حجا (ب ) ( ابوداؤد شریف ، باب الاقران ص ۷ ۲۵ نمبر ۷۹۵ ارترندی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی الجمع بین الحج والعمر ص ۶۹ نمبر ۸۲۱ مسلم شریف، باب فی الافراد والقرآن ص ۴۰۴ نمبر ۱۲۳۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے حج اور عمرہ دونوں کا احرام باندھا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ قرآن افضل ہے (۴) فدخلت على ام سلمة ... سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول اهلوا يا آل محمد بعمرة في حج (ج) سن البیقی ، باب العمرة قبل الحج والمج قبل العمرة ج رابع ص ۵۷۹ نمبر ۸۷۸۶) اس حدیث میں بھی قرآن کی اہمیت بیان کی گئی ہے۔ اس لئے حنفیہ کے نزدیک قران افضل ہے۔ فائدہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک افراد افضل ہے۔
ان کی دلیل یہ احادیث ہیں۔ عن عائشة انها قالت خرجنا مع رسول الله عام حجة الوداع فمنا من اهل بعمرة ومنا من اهـل بـحــج و عمرة ومنا من اهل بالحج واهل رسول الله بالحج فاما من اهل بالحج او جمع الحج والعمرة لم يحل حتى كان يوم النحر (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب استمع والا قران و الافراد بالج ص ۲۱۲ نمبر ۱۵۶۲ را بو داؤد شریف، باب فی افراد امج ص ۲۵۴ نمبر ۷۷۹ ارے ۱۷۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضور حجتہ الوداع میں مفرد تھے اس لئے مفرد زیادہ بہتر ہوگا۔ امام مالک کے نزدیک تمتع زیادہ افضل ہے۔ ان کی دلیل ہے کہ قرآن میں تمتع کا ذکر ہے۔ آیت میں ہے فاذا امنتم فمن تمتع بالعمرة الى الحج فما استيسر من الهدی (ب) ( آیت ۹۶ اسورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں تمتع کی طرف اشارہ ہے اس لئے تمتع افضل ہے (۲) حضور نے ان صحابہ کو جو ہدی ساتھ نہیں لے گئے عمرہ کر کے حلال ہونے کے لئے فرمایا ارشاد ہے عن جابر قال قدم رسول الله و اصحابه لا ربع ليـال خـلـون ... قال رسول الله اجعلوها عمرة الا من كان معه الهدى (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی افراد الحج ص ۲۵۶ نمبر ۱۷۸۸) (۳) عن عائشة قالت خرجنا مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ولا نرى الا انه الحج فلما قدمنا تطوفنا بالبيت فامر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من لم يكن ساق الهدى ان يحل فحل من لم يكن ساق الهدى (و) ( بخاری شریف، باب التمتع والاقران والا فراد بالج ص ۲۱۲ نمبر ۱۵۶۱) اس حدیث میں حضور نے صحابہ کو عمرہ کر کے حلال ہونے کا حکم دیا اس لئے بھی تمتع افضل ہے۔ یہ بھی حضرت امام مالک کی دلیل ہے کر تمتع افضل ہے۔ یہ اختلاف صرف افضلیت کا ہے۔
[686] (1) Qiran is superior in our view to Tamattu' and Ifrad.
Essential note: One combines Hajj and Umrah in a single journey and ties the ihram for Umrah with Hajj. This is called Qiran. Qiran means to combine, because Hajj and Umrah are combined together, so it is called Qiran.
[686] (1) Qiran in our view is superior to Tamattu' and Ifrad.
If one ties ihram only for Hajj, it is called Hajj Ifrad. If one first ties ihram for Umrah, completes it and unties the ihram, then stays within the miqat boundaries, then ties ihram for Hajj during the months of Hajj and completes Hajj, that is called Hajj Tamattu'. Tamattu' means to take benefit, because one takes benefit of untying ihram after Umrah. And Qiran has its meaning as above. In our view, the reason Qiran is superior:
(1) Because there is more hardship in it, and more hardship brings more reward, so Hajj Qiran is superior. (2) I heard Umar say: I heard the Prophet (peace be upon him) in Wadi al-Aqiq say: 'A visitor came to me tonight from my Lord and said: Pray in this blessed valley and say: Umrah included in Hajj.' (a) [Bukhari, Hadith 1534; Abu Dawud, Hadith 1800] From this hadith it is understood that he was commanded to formally combine Umrah with Hajj, so Qiran is superior. (3) Anas ibn Malik (may Allah be pleased with him) said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) reciting talbiyah for both Hajj and Umrah together, saying: 'Labbaik Umratan wa Hajjan, Labbaik Umratan wa Hajjan.' (b) [Abu Dawud, Hadith 1795; Tirmidhi, Hadith 821; Muslim, Hadith 1232] In this hadith, the Prophet tied ihram for both Hajj and Umrah, indicating Qiran is superior. (4) I entered upon Umm Salamah... I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'Proclaim, O family of Muhammad, Umrah within Hajj.' (c) [Baihaqi, Sunan al-Kubra, vol. 4, p. 579, Hadith 8786] This hadith also states the importance of Qiran. So the Hanafis hold Qiran as superior.
Benefit: Imam Shafi'i holds Ifrad as superior. His evidence is the hadith of Aisha: She said, 'We went out with the Messenger of Allah in the Farewell Pilgrimage. Some of us proclaimed Umrah, some proclaimed Hajj and Umrah, and some proclaimed Hajj. And the Messenger of Allah proclaimed Hajj. As for those who proclaimed Hajj or combined Hajj and Umrah, they did not become halal until the Day of Nahr.' (a) [Bukhari, Hadith 1562; Abu Dawud, Hadith 1779] From this hadith it is understood that the Prophet was a Mufrid in the Farewell Pilgrimage, so Ifrad is better. Imam Malik holds Tamattu' as superior. His evidence is that the Quran mentions Tamattu': 'When you are secure, whoever performs Tamattu' of Umrah to Hajj, then an offering of whatever is easy.' (b) [Quran 2:196] This verse indicates Tamattu', so Tamattu' is superior. (2) The Prophet commanded those companions who did not bring a hadi to become halal by performing Umrah. The narration: Jabir said: The Prophet and his companions arrived on the fourth night... The Prophet said: 'Make it Umrah, except for those who have a hadi.' (c) [Abu Dawud, Hadith 1788] (3) Aisha said: 'We went out with the Prophet, and we intended nothing but Hajj. When we arrived and performed tawaf of the House, the Prophet commanded those who had not brought a hadi to become halal. So those who had not brought a hadi became halal.' (d) [Bukhari, Hadith 1561] In this hadith, the Prophet commanded the companions to become halal by Umrah, so Tamattu' is superior. This is also Imam Malik's evidence that Tamattu' is superior. This difference is only regarding preference.
Source pages p. 426

Key Terms
قرآن (Qiran): Combining Hajj and Umrah in a single ihram from the miqat
تمتع (Tamattu'): Performing Umrah first during the months of Hajj, then after completing Umrah and untying ihram, performing Hajj in the same year
افراد (Ifrad): Performing only Hajj, without Umrah, in the months of Hajj
مشقت (Mashaqqah): Hardship; the principle that greater hardship yields greater reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the primary reason for the superiority of Qiran over Tamattu' and Ifrad?
A) It is explicitly mentioned in the Quran.
B) It involves less ritual, making it easier.
C) It involves greater hardship and is commanded by the Prophet in multiple hadiths.
D) The Prophet performed it in his final Hajj.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds Qiran as the most virtuous form of Hajj due to explicit Prophetic commands and the principle of more hardship, more reward, but all three forms are valid.

The Method of Qiran: Entering Ihram for Hajj and Umrah Together
Defines the manner of Qiran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the prescribed manner (sifah) of performing Qiran according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Qiran is performed by entering ihram for Umrah and Hajj together at the miqat and reciting a specific supplication after prayer.

This passage defines the manner (sifah) of Qiran, one of the three types of Hajj. It specifies when and how to enter ihram, as well as the supplication to be said. Understanding this procedure ensures the pilgrim performs Qiran correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act described
The passage describes the method (sifah) of performing Qiran. Qiran is a type of Hajj where one combines Hajj and Umrah with a single ihram.
2
Locate the time and place
The ihram for Qiran is entered at the miqat, the designated boundary for entering the state of ihram.
3
Identify the key action
The pilgrim must proclaim ihram for both Umrah and Hajj simultaneously (yuhillu bi al-umrah wa al-hajj ma'an).
4
Note the recommended supplication
After the prayer (presumably at the miqat), the pilgrim says: 'O Allah, I intend Hajj and Umrah, so make them easy for me and accept them.'
This is a recommended du'a, not a pillar or wajib.

[٦۸۷] (۲) وصفة القرآن ان يهل بالعمرة والحج معا من الميقات ويقول عقيب الصلوة اللهم اني اريد الحج والعمرة فيسهما لي وتقبلهما
قران کی صورت یہ ہے کہ عمرہ اور حج کا احرام ایک ساتھ باندھے۔ اور نماز کے بعد کہے اے اللہ ! میں نے حج اور عمرہ کا ارادہ کیا ہے اس لئے ان دونوں کو آسان کر دے اور مجھ سے دونوں قبول کر۔
[687] (2) The description of Qiran is that one should proclaim ihram for Umrah and Hajj together from the miqat, and say after the prayer: 'O Allah, I intend Hajj and Umrah, so make them easy for me and accept them.'
The form of Qiran is that one ties ihram for Umrah and Hajj together. And after the prayer he says: O Allah, I have intended Hajj and Umrah, so make both easy for me and accept both from me.

Key Terms
صفة (Sifah): The prescribed manner or description of how an act of worship is performed
يهل (Yuhillu): To proclaim or enter into ihram, usually by saying the talbiyah or making intention

C) Upon seeing the Kaaba
D) During the tawaf

Key Takeaway
The prescribed manner of Qiran is to enter ihram for both Hajj and Umrah at the miqat and to recite a recommended du'a after prayer.

The Order of Rituals Upon Entering Makkah in Qiran
States the sequence of rituals upon entering Makkah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the order of rituals upon entering Makkah in Qiran and identify the sunnah of ramal in the first three circuits of tawaf.

Core Idea
Upon entering Makkah, tawaf comes before sa'y, with ramal sunnah for men in the first three circuits.

When a qarin pilgrim enters Makkah, the first act is not rest or prayer but the circumambulation of the Kaaba. This passage from al-Sharh al-Sameri lays out the precise sequence: tawaf first, with a specific walk for men, followed by sa'y. Understanding this order is essential for correct Hajj and Umrah performance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first ritual
The passage opens with 'he begins with tawaf' (ibtada'a bil-tawaf). Tawaf is the first action upon entering Makkah.
This applies to Qiran; for other types of Hajj, the order may differ.
2
Describe the tawaf procedure
Tawaf consists of seven circuits (sab'an). In the first three, men perform ramal (brisk walking with shoulder movement); in the remaining four, they walk normally.
Ramal is a sunnah specific to men and only for the first tawaf upon arrival.
3
Identify the second ritual
After tawaf, the pilgrim performs sa'y between Safa and Marwah seven times.
Sa'y is wajib in Hanafi fiqh; its omission requires a sacrifice (dam).
4
Recognize the category of these actions
The passage concludes: 'These are the actions of Umrah.' Thus, upon entering Makkah, the qarin has effectively performed Umrah.
In Qiran, Umrah is performed first, then the pilgrim remains in ihram for Hajj.
5
Summarize the complete sequence
Enter Makkah → Tawaf (7 circuits, ramal in first 3) → Sa'y (7 rounds) → Remain in ihram for Hajj.
This sequence is obligatory (wajib) for the qarin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٦٨٨] (۳) فاذا دخل مكة ابتدأ بالطواف فيطوف بالبيت سبعا يرمُل في الثلاثة الاول ويمشي في الباقي ثم يسعى بين الصفا والمروة وهذا الافعال العمرة
پس جبکہ مکہ میں داخل ہو تو طواف سے شروع کرے، پس بیت اللہ کا طواف کرے سات شوط، تین پہلے میں ریمل کرے اور باقی میں اپنی حالت پر چلے اور اس کے بعد صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان سعی کرے اور یہ عمرہ کے افعال ہیں۔ اتی عمرہ میں تین کام ہوتے ہیں (۱) احرام باندھنا (۲) سات شوط طواف کرنا (۳) صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان سعی کرنا۔
[688] (3) When he enters Makkah, he begins with tawaf: he circles the House seven times, walking briskly (ramal) in the first three and walking normally in the remaining, then he performs sa'y between Safa and Marwah. And these are the actions of Umrah.
So when he enters Makkah, he should begin with tawaf. He performs tawaf of the House of Allah seven circuits, performing ramal in the first three and walking normally in the rest. After that he performs sa'y between Safa and Marwah. And these are the actions of Umrah. In Umrah, there are three actions: (1) tying ihram, (2) performing seven circuits of tawaf, (3) performing sa'y between Safa and Marwah.
Source pages p. 427

Key Terms
طواف (Tawaf): Circumambulation of the Kaaba seven times, starting from the Black Stone
رمل (Ramal): Walking briskly with short steps and moving the shoulders, performed by men in the first three circuits of tawaf upon arrival
سعي (Sa'y): Walking back and forth between the hills of Safa and Marwah seven times

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When entering Makkah as a Qarin (performing Qiran), which act is done first?
A) Sa'y between Safa and Marwah
B) Tawaf of the Kaaba
C) Offering the hadi (sacrifice)
D) Shaving the head

Key Takeaway
Upon entering Makkah in Qiran, the pilgrim begins with tawaf of the Kaaba (with ramal in first three circuits for men), followed by sa'y between Safa and Marwah; these constitute the actions of Umrah.

The Obligation of Hadi for the Qarin and Mutamatti'
Ruling on the obligation of Hadi for Qarin and Mutamatti' with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Hadi for the Qarin and Mutamatti', identify acceptable animals, and cite the Quranic proof.

Core Idea
Hadi is wajib for Qarin and Mutamatti'; the Quran and Sunnah command it.

This passage from the chapter of Hajj establishes the ruling of Hadi (sacrificial animal) for those who perform Hajj in the Qiran or Tamattu' manner. After throwing the Jamrah al-Aqabah on the Day of Nahr, a specific animal must be slaughtered. The text details the types of animals acceptable and provides the Quranic and hadith evidence. Understanding this ruling ensures proper fulfillment of a key wajib in Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Pinpoint that the act is slaughtering Hadi on the Day of Nahr after throwing the Jamrah. The ruling is that Hadi is wajib (obligatory) for both the Qarin and the Mutamatti'.
Distinguish between wajib and fard: in Hanafi fiqh, Hadi falls under wajib, not fard.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary dalil is the Quranic verse (al-Baqarah 2:196) cited in the passage: 'So whoever performs Tamattu' of Umrah to Hajj, then [offer] whatever is easy of the Hadi.' The secondary dalil is the hadith of Ibn Abbas, which confirms that the Companions owed Hadi after combining Hajj and Umrah.
The verse uses the imperative 'fama istaysara', which in Hanafi usul indicates obligation (wujub).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative phrase 'fama istaysara min al-hady' is a command to offer Hadi. Hanafi usul holds that commands in the Quran generally indicate obligation unless there is a contextual shift. No such shift exists here; thus the ruling is wajib.
The dalala (indication) is considered zanni because the interpretation of the imperative is subject to scholarly debate, but the Hanafi school adheres to the apparent meaning.
4
Note the types of animals and the shared sacrifice ruling
Acceptable animals: a sheep, a cow, a camel, or a seventh share of a cow or camel. The hadith of Jabir (nahrna ma'a Rasulillah...) establishes that a camel or cow can be shared among seven persons, which justifies the seventh share ruling.
If one cannot afford Hadi, the alternative is fasting three days during Hajj and seven days after returning home (ten days total), as mentioned in the verse.

فاذا رمى الجمرة يوم النحر ذبح شاة او بقرة او بدنة أو سبع بدنة أو سبع بقرة فهذا دم القرآن۔ پس جب دسویں ذی الحجہ کو جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کرے تو ایک بکری ذبح کرے یا ایک گائے یا ایک اونٹ یا اونٹ کا ساتواں حصہ یا گائے کا ساتوں حصہ، پس یہ قرآن کا دم ہے۔ قارن اور متمتع پر ہدی لازم ہے۔ اور ہدی کی صورت یہ ہے کہ ایک بکری ہو یا ایک گائے ہو یا ایک اونٹ ہو یا گائے کا ساتواں حصہ یا اونٹ کا ساتواں حصہ ہو۔ قارن اور متمتع پر ہدی لازم ہونے کی وجہ یہ آیت ہے فمن تمتع بالعمرة الى الحج فما استيسر من الهدى فمن لم يجد فصيام ثلثة ايام فى الحج وسبعة اذا رجعتم تلك عشرة كاملة ذلك لمن لم يكن اهله حاضری المسجد الحرام۔ اس آیت میں ہے کہ جس نے عمرہ کو حج کے ساتھ ملایا چاہے تمتع کر کے ملایا ہو چاہے قران کر کے ملایا ہو اس پر ہدی لازم ہے۔ اور ہدی نہ دے سکے تو تین دن حج سے پہلے روزے رکھے اور سات دن حج کے بعد روزے رکھے کل ملا کر دس دن روزے رکھے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عباس انه سئل عن متعه الحج فقال ... ثم امرنا عشية التروية ان نهل بالحج فاذا فرغنا من المناسک جئنا فطفنا بالبيت وبالصفا والمروة فقد تم حجنا وعلينا الهدى كما قال الله عز وجل فما استيسر من الهدى۔ اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا تمتع اور قارن پر ہدی لازم ہے۔ اور گائے یا اونٹ کے ساتویں حصے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن جابر بن عبد الله انه قال نحرنا مع رسول الله بالحديبية البدنة عن سبعة والبقرة عن سبعة۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ گائے اور اونٹ سات آدمیوں کی جانب سے کافی ہے۔
Then when he throws the jamrah on the Day of Nahr, he slaughters a sheep, or a cow, or a camel, or a seventh of a camel, or a seventh of a cow; this is the blood of Qiran. (Urdu explanation follows).
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter of Hajj. It states that after throwing the Jamrah al-Aqabah on the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), a Qarin must slaughter a Hadi animal: a sheep, cow, or camel, or a seventh share of a camel or cow. This is because the Qarin has combined Hajj and Umrah and thus owes Hadi. The proof is from the Quran (al-Baqarah 2:196) and the Sunnah, specifically the hadith of Ibn Abbas and the hadith of Jabir about sharing a camel among seven. The passage also clarifies that the same ruling applies to the Mutamatti'. The types of animals acceptable for Hadi are detailed. The text emphasizes that the Hadi is due upon the Qarin and Mutamatti' as a consequence of their combining the two rituals.

Key Terms
قارن (qārin): A person who intends Hajj and Umrah together with a single ihram.
متمتع (mutamatti‘): A person who performs Umrah first, then Hajj with separate ihrams.
هدى (hady): A sacrificial animal offered during Hajj due to a specific obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Hanafi school makes Hadi wajib for both Qarin and Mutamatti', based on the Quranic command and prophetic practice.

Fasting as Substitute for Hadi: Timing and Proof
Ruling with proof on substitute fasting for Hadi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling, timing, and proof for fasting as a substitute for Hadi when a Qarin or Mutamatti' cannot afford an animal.

Core Idea
Three fasts during Hajj end by Arafah; seven after returning; fasts prohibited on Eid and Tashreeq.

When a pilgrim performing Hajj as Qarin or Mutamatti' cannot afford the required Hadi (sacrificial animal), the obligation is replaced by fasting. The Quran and hadith specify the timing: three days during the Hajj season ending on the Day of Arafah, and seven days after returning home. This lesson examines the ruling, its proof, and the prohibition of fasting on the days of Eid and Tashreeq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is fasting as a substitute for Hadi. Establish that it is wajib for Qarin and Mutamatti' when Hadi is unavailable.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The Quranic verse (al-Baqarah 2:196) commands fasting when one cannot offer Hadi. Identify the phrase 'fa-man lam yajid fa-siyamu thalathati ayyamin fi al-hajj'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Hanafi school interprets 'fi al-hajj' as during the Hajj period before the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. Explain how this yields the timing ending at Arafah.
The imperative implies obligation (wajib) in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and prohibitions
Some schools allow fasting on Tashreeq days, but Hanafi prohibits based on hadith. Also note that Eid days are forbidden for fasting.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Confirm that the three fasts must be completed by the 9th of Dhul Hijjah, and the remaining seven after returning home. Ensure no fasting on 10th-13th.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان لم يكن له ما يذبح صام ثلثة ايام في الحج آخرها يوم عرفة۔ پس اگر اس کے پاس ہدی نہ ہو جو ذبح کر سکے تو روزے رکھے، تین دن حج میں اور اس کا آخری دن نویں ذی الحجہ ہو۔ قارن اور متمتع پر ہدی واجب ہے لیکن اگر ہدی ذبیح نہ کر سکے روپیہ نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے یا جانور نہ ملنے کی وجہ سے تو حج سے پہلے تین روزے رکھے اور باقی سات روزے حج کے بعد رکھے۔ حاشیہ : (الف) جس نے عمرہ کو حج کے ساتھ مل کر تمتع کیا تو ہدی میں سے جو آسان ہو۔ اور جو ہدی نہ پائے تو تین روزے رکھے حج کے زمانے میں اور سات جب لوٹے ، یہ دس روزے کامل ہو گئے۔ یہ تمتع اس کے لئے ہے جو مسجد حرام کے پاس نہ ہو (ب ) حضرت عبداللہ بن عباس سے حج تمتع کے بارے میں پوچھا گیا تو انہوں نے فرمایا ہم کو آٹھویں کی شام کو حکم دیا کہ ہم حج کا احرام باندھیں، پس جب ہم مناسک حج سے فارغ ہوئے تو ہم آئے اور بیت اللہ کا اور صفا مروہ کا طواف کیا اور ہمار حج پورا ہو گیا اور ہم پر ہدی ہے جیسا کہ اللہ نے فرمایا فما استیس من الهدی (ج) حضرت جابر نے فرمایا ہم نے رسول اللہ کے ساتھ حدیبیہ میں ایک اونٹ سات کی طرف سے ذبح کیا اور ایک گائے سات کی طرف سے۔ پہلے آیت گزرگئی کہ ہدی نہ ہو تو روزے رکھے، فمن تمتع بالعمرة الى الحج فما استيسر من الهدى فمن لم يجد فصيام ثلثة ايام في الحج و سبعة اذا رجعتم تلك عشرة كاملة (آیت ۹۶ اسورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ ہدی نہ دے سکو تو روزے رکھو۔ تین روزے حج سے پہلے اور سات روزے حج سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد ۔ آخری دن یوم عرفہ ہو اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ اس سے پہلے ہدی پر قدرت ہو جائے جو اصل ہے اس لئے روزہ جو فرع ہے اس کی تاخیر کرے۔ اور یوم الخر یعنی عید کے دن اور ایام تشریق یعنی گیارہویں، بارہویں اور تیرہویں ذی الحجہ کو روزہ اس لئے نہیں رکھے کہ یہ دن کھانے پینے کے ہیں۔ اور روزہ ان دنوں میں ممنوع ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن عقبة بن عامر قال قال رسول الله يوم عرفة ويوم النحر وايام التشريق عيدنا اهل الاسلام وهي ایام اکل و شرب۔ اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ یوم عرفہ اور ایام تشریق سے پہلے پہلے تین روزے رکھ لے (۲) قال ان رسول الله نهي عن صيام هذين اليومين اما يوم الاضحى فتأكلون من لحم نسككم واما يوم الفطر ففطر كم من صيامكم۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عید الاضحی اور عید الفطر میں روزہ رکھنا منع ہے۔ اس لئے دسویں ذی الحجہ میں روزہ نہیں رکھے گا۔
If he does not have what to slaughter, he fasts three days during Hajj, the last of which is the Day of 'Arafah. (Urdu explanation follows).
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the substitute for Hadi when a pilgrim cannot afford it. The text states that if a Qarin or Mutamatti' cannot find or afford an animal to slaughter, he must fast three days during the Hajj period, with the last day being the Day of 'Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah). The remaining seven fasts are to be completed after returning home. The proof is the same Quranic verse (al-Baqarah 2:196). The text also explains the wisdom behind delaying the three fasts until just before 'Arafah: because there is still hope that the pilgrim might acquire the means to offer the Hadi, which is the original obligation. Fasting on the days of 'Eid and the days of Tashreeq (11th, 12th, 13th) is prohibited because these are days of eating and drinking, as established by the hadith of 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir and the hadith prohibiting fasting on the two 'Eids.

Key Terms
صيام (ṣiyām): Fasting as a substitute for Hadi when one cannot offer an animal.
يوم عرفة (yawm ‘Arafah): The 9th of Dhul Hijjah, the last day on which the three fasts during Hajj can be performed.
أيام التشريق (ayyām al-tashrīq): The 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah; days when fasting is prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C. 11th Dhul Hijjah
D. Any day of Hajj

Key Takeaway
The substitute three fasts for Hadi must be completed by the Day of 'Arafah, and fasting on Eid and Tashreeq days is prohibited.

Missed Substitute Fast: When Hadi Becomes Due
Inter-madhhab dispute on missed substitute fast for Mutamatti'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a Mutamatti' who fails to fast before the 10th of Dhul Hijjah and explain the Maliki counter-argument.

Core Idea
If the substitute fast is missed until the Day of Nahr, the Hadi becomes wajib — the original obligation is reinstated.

The Quran permits a Mutamatti' to fast three days during Hajj as a substitute for the Hadi if he cannot afford it. But this substitution is time-limited. What happens if the fast is missed until the Day of Nahr? This lesson explores the Hanafi and Maliki views on this issue, focusing on the role of necessity and the prohibition of fasting on certain days.

Guided Path
1
State the Issue
Identify the scenario: a Mutamatti' (or Qarin) who cannot offer Hadi and intends to fast three days during Hajj, but fails to complete them before the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.
The three days are to be fasted before 'Arafah (9th), as per the Hanafi interpretation.
2
State the Hanafi Position
According to Abu Hanifa and his companions, if the fast is missed until the Day of Nahr, the Hadi becomes due and fasting no longer suffices.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
3
Identify the Hanafi Dalil
The primary proof is the Quranic verse: 'fa-siyamu thalathati ayyamin fi al-hajj' — the phrase 'fi al-hajj' indicates a limited time ending before 'Arafah. The Hanafis also cite athar of Ibn 'Abbas and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.
The days of Tashreeq (11th-13th) are prohibited for fasting by explicit hadith.
4
State the Maliki Position
Imam Malik permits fasting on the days of Tashreeq if the substitute fast was missed, citing necessity (darurah).
The Maliki school considers the prohibition on fasting Tashreeq days to be remissible in this case.
5
Analyse the Hanafi Response
The Hanafis respond that the prohibition on fasting Tashreeq days is established by a sahih hadith and cannot be overridden by necessity. The time for the substitute fast has lapsed.
The Hanafi view is that the original obligation of Hadi is reinstated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان فاته الصوم حتى يدخل يوم النحر لم يجزه الا الدم۔ پہلے آیت گزرگئی کہ ہدی نہ ہو تو روزے رکھے، فمن تمتع بالعمرة الى الحج فما استيسر من الهدى فمن لم يجد فصيام ثلثة ايام في الحج و سبعة اذا رجعتم تلك جو اصل ہے اس لئے روزہ جو فرع ہے اس کی تاخیر کرے۔ اور یوم الخر یعنی عید کے دن اور ایام تشریق یعنی گیارہویں، بارہویں اور تیرہویں ذی الحجہ کو روزہ اس لئے نہیں رکھے کہ یہ دن کھانے پینے کے ہیں۔ اور روزہ ان روزے رکھ لے (۲) قال ان رسول الله نهي عن صيام هذين اليومين اما يوم الاضحى فتأكلون من لحم نسككم واما يوم الفطر ففطر كم من صيامكم۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عید الاضحی اور عید الفطر میں روزہ رکھنا منع ہے۔ اس لئے دسویں ذی الحجہ میں روزہ نہیں رکھے گا۔ (۶۹۲) (۷) پس اگر اس سے روزہ فوت ہو گیا یہاں تک کہ دسویں ذی الحجہ داخل ہو گیا تو نہیں کافی ہوگا مگر ہدی دینا۔ قارن یا متمتع کو ہدی دینا تھا لیکن ہدی نہیں دے سکا اور دسویں ذی الحجہ تک روزہ بھی تین دن تک نہیں رکھ سکا تو اب دم ہی دینا پوڑھے گا، روزہ رکھنا کافی نہیں۔ کیونکہ آیت میں صیام ثلثۃ فی الحج ہے اور اس کا وقت دسویں ذی الحجہ سے پہلے پہلے ہے اور وہ فوت ہو گیا اس لئے اب اصل ہی لازم ہوگا یعنی ہدی لازم ہوگی۔ اثر میں ہے عن ابن عباس قال اذا لم يصم المتمتع فعليه الدم ... وعن عبراهيم قال لا بد من دم ولو يبيع ثوبه۔ اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ دسویں ذی الحجہ تک روزے نہ رکھ سکا تو اس پر اب دم ہی لازم ہے۔ امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ گیارہویں، بارہویں اور تیرہویں ذی الحجہ کو روزہ رکھ لے گا، کیونکہ اگر چہ اس دن کے روزے مکروہ ہیں لیکن ان کے لئے گنجائش ہے کیونکہ وہ مجبور ہے۔ اثر میں ہے عن ابن عمر قال الصيام لمن تمتع بالعمرة الى الحج الى يوم عرفة۔ حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا عرفہ کا دن، اور دسویں ذی الحجہ اور ایام تشریق یعنی گیارہویں، بارہویں اور تیرہویں تاریخ ہمارے اہل اسلام کی عید ہے اور وہ کھانے پینے کے دن ہے (ب) حضور نے ان دونوں دنوں میں روزہ رکھنے سے منع فرمایا، بہر حال عید الاضحی کے دن تو اپنی قربانی کا گوشت کھاؤ، بہر حال عید الفطر کے دن تو تمہارے روزے سے افطار کا دن ہے (ج) ابن عباس فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر تمتع کرنے والا روزہ نہ رکھ سکے تو اس پر دم لازم ہے اور ابراہیم نے فرمایا کہ دم ضروری ہے اگر چہ کپڑے ہی بیچنا پڑے۔
If the fast escapes him until the Day of Nahr enters, nothing avails him except the blood (Hadi). (Urdu explanation follows).
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the ruling for a Mutamatti' or Qarin who fails to fast the three days before the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. The Hanafi position is that if the fast is missed until the Day of Nahr, then the Hadi becomes due and fasting no longer suffices. The proof is that the verse specifies the fasting be 'during the Hajj' which ends at 'Arafah; after that, the opportunity is lost. The Hanafis support this with the athar of Ibn 'Abbas and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. Imam Malik differs, permitting fasting on the days of Tashreeq due to necessity. The Hanafi response holds that the days of Tashreeq are prohibited for fasting in general, and the hadith of 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir confirms they are days of eating and drinking. Therefore, the fasting substitute lapses and the original obligation of Hadi is reinstated.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (Hadi) that becomes due when the substitute fast is missed.
ايام التشريق (ayyām al-tashrīq): The 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah, when fasting is prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling if a Mutamatti' fails to fast before the 10th of Dhul Hijjah?
A. He must fast on the days of Tashreeq
B. He must offer Hadi
C. He must do nothing
D. He must repeat the Hajj

Key Takeaway
If the substitute fast is missed until the Day of Nahr, the Hadi becomes wajib; the opportunity to fast has lapsed.

When a Mutamatti' Misses the Three Fasts Before the Day of Nahr
Ruling and proof for a mutamatti' who misses the three fasts until the day of Nahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a mutamatti' misses the three fasts before the day of Nahr, and explain why a blood sacrifice (dam) is required instead of fasting on the days of Tashriq.

Core Idea
Once the time for substitute fasts expires, the original sacrifice revives.

A mutamatti' who cannot afford a sacrificial animal may fast three days during Hajj and seven after. But what if he fails to complete those three fasts before the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah)? The Hanafi school holds that fasting on the days of Tashriq is prohibited, so the substitute fails and the original obligation of a blood sacrifice returns. This lesson unpacks the textual proofs and reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify the act: a mutamatti' who cannot offer a hady and chooses to fast. The ruling: if he misses the three fasts until the day of Nahr, only a dam (blood sacrifice) is acceptable; fasting no longer suffices.
This is a ruling of wujub (obligation) of the dam.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The primary proof cited is the hadith from 'Uqba ibn 'Amir: the day of Arafah, day of Nahr, and days of Tashriq are days of eating and drinking, not fasting. This establishes the prohibition of fasting on those days.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but relied upon.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly prohibits fasting on these days. Since the three fasts must occur during Hajj before the day of Nahr, missing that deadline means the fasts cannot be completed. Thus the substitute (fasts) fails and the original obligation (sacrifice) becomes binding.
The Quranic verse (2:196) permits fasting as a substitute; the hadith restricts the timing.
4
Note the intra-madhhab and inter-madhhab disagreement
Within the Hanafi school, there is no disagreement. Imam Malik permits fasting on the days of Tashriq for a mutamatti' in necessity. The Hanafi school rejects this based on the explicit prohibition.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

معلوم ہوا کہ عید الاضحی اور عید الفطر میں روزہ رکھنا منع ہے۔ اس لئے دسویں ذی الحجہ میں روزہ نہیں رکھے گا۔ [۶۹۲) (۷) پس اگر اس سے روزہ فوت ہو گیا یہاں تک کہ دسویں ذی الحجہ داخل ہو گیا تو نہیں کافی ہوگا دم ہی لازم ہے۔ انده امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ گیارہویں، بارہویں اور تیر ہوا ذی الحجہ کو روزہ رکھ لے گا، کیونکہ اگر چہ اس دن کے روزے مکروہ ہیں لیکن ان کے لئے گنجائش ہے کیونکہ کہ یہ مجبور ہے (۲) اثر میں ہے عن ابن عمر قال الصيام لمن تمتع بالعمرة الى الحج الى يوم عرفة حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا عرفہ کا دن، اور دسویں ذی الحجہ اور ایام تشریق یعنی گیار جوان ، بارہویں اور تیرہویں تاریخ ہمارے اہل اسلام کی عید ہے اور وہ کھانے پینے کے دن ہے (ب) حضور نے ان دونوں دنوں میں روزہ رکھنے سے منع فرمایا، بہر حال عید الاضحی کے دن تو اپنی قربانی کا گوشت کھاؤ، بہر حال عید الفطر کے دن تو تمہارے روزے سے افطار کا دن ہے (ج) ابن عباس فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر تمتع کرنے والا روزہ نہ رکھ سکے تو اس پر دم لازم ہے اور ابراہیم نے فرمایا کہ دم ضروری ہے اگر چہ کپڑے ہی بیچنا پڑے۔
If the fast is missed until the day of Nahr enters, nothing suffices but the blood (sacrifice). Previously the verse passed: '...So whoever performs Tamattu' by combining Umrah with Hajj, then whatever is easy of the sacrificial animal; and whoever cannot find, then a fast of three days during Hajj and seven when you return; that is ten complete [days]' (Quran 2:196). In this verse: if you cannot give the sacrificial animal, then fast. Three fasts before Hajj and seven after completing Hajj. The last day is the day of Arafah, the reason being that perhaps before that one becomes able to offer the sacrificial animal, which is the original; therefore the fast which is subsidiary is delayed. And on the day of Nahr (i.e., 'Id) and the days of Tashriq (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah), he does not fast because these are days of eating and drinking, and fasting is prohibited on these days. In the hadith: 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir said: The Messenger of Allah said: The day of Arafah, the day of Nahr, and the days of Tashriq are our festivals, O people of Islam; they are days of eating and drinking.' (a) (Abu Dawood, Bab Sawm Ayyam al-Tashriq, p.335 no.12419; Muslim, Bab Tahrim Sawm Ayyam al-Tashriq, p.360 no.1141). This hadith establishes that he should fast the three days before the day of Arafah and the days of Tashriq. (2) He said: The Messenger of Allah forbade fasting on these two days: the day of Adha, you eat from the meat of your sacrifice; and the day of Fitr, it is the breaking of your fast. (b) (Abu Dawood, Bab fi Sawm al-'Eidayn, p.335 no.2416; Muslim, Bab Tahrim Sawm Yawmay al-'Eidayn, p.360 no.1137). This hadith shows that fasting on 'Id al-Adha and 'Id al-Fitr is prohibited. Therefore, he will not fast on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. [692] (7) So if the fast is missed until the 10th of Dhul Hijjah enters, then it does not suffice, except that he must give a blood sacrifice. The qarin or mutamatti' was required to give a sacrificial animal, but he could not give it, and he could not fast for three days until the 10th of Dhul Hijjah; now he must give a blood sacrifice. Because the verse says 'fasting of three days during Hajj' and its time is before the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, and that time has passed. Therefore the original (sacrifice) becomes obligatory. (2) In the athar: Ibn 'Abbas said: If the mutamatti' does not fast, then upon him is blood (sacrifice). ... And Ibrahim said: There is no escape from blood (sacrifice), even if he sells his garment. (c) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 43 fi al-sam' idha fatahu al-sawm, juz 3, p.150 no.12987/1298). From this athar, if he could not fast until the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, then now only blood is obligatory. Imam Malik says that he will fast on the 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah, because although fasting these days is disliked, there is leeway for him because he is compelled. (2) In the athar: Ibn 'Umar said: Fasting is for one who performs Tamattu' from Umrah to Hajj until the day of Arafah. Footnote: (a) He said: The day of Arafah, the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, and the days of Tashriq (11th, 12th, 13th) are the festivals of us Muslims, and they are days of eating and drinking. (b) The Prophet prohibited fasting on these two days; anyway, on the day of Adha you eat the meat of your sacrifice; anyway, on the day of Fitr it is the day of breaking your fast. (c) Ibn 'Abbas says: If the Tamattu' performer cannot fast, then blood is obligatory; and Ibrahim said: Blood is necessary, even if he has to sell his clothes.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses the case of a mutamatti' (one performing Tamattu' Hajj) who is obligated to offer a sacrificial animal (hady) but cannot afford it. In that case, he may fast three days during the Hajj period and seven days after returning. The key issue here is: what if he misses the three fasts until the day of Nahr (10th of Dhul Hijjah)? The text states that fasting is no longer acceptable; he must offer the blood sacrifice (dam). The reasoning is that the original obligation is the sacrifice, and fasting is only a substitute when one cannot afford the sacrifice. Once the time for the fast has passed (before the 10th), the substitute fails, and the original obligation revives. The text supports this with two hadiths: one from 'Uqba ibn 'Amir declaring the days of Arafah, Nahr, and Tashriq as festivals (days of eating and drinking, so fasting is prohibited), and another forbidding fasting on the two 'Eids. Additionally, athar from Ibn 'Abbas and Ibrahim emphasize that blood is obligatory even if the person must sell his garment. The passage also mentions Imam Malik's dissenting view that fasting on the days of Tashriq is permissible due to necessity, but the Hanafi position is that it is not allowed. Thus the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school is that if one misses the three fasts before the day of Nahr, only a dam is acceptable.

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu'): A type of Hajj where one performs Umrah first, then exits ihram, then re-enters ihram for Hajj in the same year, requiring a sacrificial animal.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice, specifically a sheep or goat, offered as compensation for missing an obligatory rite in Hajj.
أيام التشريق (ayyam al-tashriq): The 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah; days when fasting is prohibited according to the hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a mutamatti' cannot afford a sacrificial animal and misses the three fasts before the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah)?
A) He must fast on the days of Tashriq to make up the missed fasts.
B) He must offer a blood sacrifice (dam), and fasting no longer suffices.
C) He is exempt from both, no further obligation.
D) He must combine fasting on the days of Tashriq with a sacrifice.

Key Takeaway
If a mutamatti' fails to complete the three fasts before the day of Nahr, the substitute expires and a blood sacrifice becomes wajib.

Location of the Seven Fasts of Tamattu': Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute on whether the seven fasts can be observed in Makkah or only at home

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on where the seven fasts of tamattu' may be observed and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on the interpretation of the Qur'anic verse.

Core Idea
The seven fasts of tamattu' may be done anywhere after Hajj — not only at home — according to the Hanafi school.

This lesson examines a classical dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over the location for the seven fasts of tamattu'. The matn states that fasting seven days 'when he returns to his family' is permissible, but the Hanafi school, led by Imam Abu Hanifa, interprets 'return' broadly to mean returning from the Hajj itself, not necessarily to one's homeland. This flexibility allows pilgrims to complete their fasts in Makkah or on the road, a practical ease for those who cannot delay. We will explore the textual proofs and the reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What exactly does Abu Hanifa hold regarding the location of these fasts? He permits fasting in Makkah, on the road, or at home.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i insists the fasts must be after returning home.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i interprets 'when you return' as return to family, citing the verse and an athar from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafis take the verse generally as 'return from Hajj' and support with an athar from 'Ata' allowing fasting on the road or in Makkah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: a mutamatti' may fast immediately in Makkah under Hanafi, but must wait under Shafi'i.

ثم يصوم سبعة ايام اذا رجع الى اهله فان صامها بمكة بعد فراغه من الحج جاز [۶۹۳] (۸) پھر سات روزے رکھے جب اپنے گھر واپس آئے ، پس اگر مکہ مکرمہ میں روزے رکھے حج سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد تو بھی جائز ہے۔ جو ہدی نہ پائے اور حج کے بعد سات روزے رکھنا ہو تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک وہ سات روزے گھر آکر بھی رکھ سکتا ہے اور مکہ مکرمہ میں رکھنا چاہے تو وہاں بھی رکھ سکتا ہے۔ آیت میں وسبعة اذا رجعتم کا مطلب ہے اذا رجعتم من الحج کہ جب حج سے فارغ ہو جاؤ تو روزہ رکھو چاہے مکہ مکرمہ میں چاہے گھر واپس آنے کے بعد چاہے راستہ میں رکھ لو۔ عن عطاء قال وسبعة اذا رجعتم (الآية) قال ان شاء صامها فى الطريق وان شاء بمكة (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۴۵ في قضاء السبعة الفرق او الوصل ج ثالث ص ۱۵۱، نمبر ۱۲۹۹۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مکہ مکرمہ میں بھی روزہ رکھ سکتا ہے اور راستے میں رکھ سکتا ہے۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ گھر واپس آکر ہی روزے رکھے۔ ان کا استدلال ہے کہ آیت میں وسبعة اذا رجعتم ہے، یعنی جب واپس آجاؤ گھر کو ۔ اس لئے گھر واپس آنے کے بعد ہی روزے رکھے (۲) اثر میں ہے عن سعيد بن المسيب قال ... فمن لم يجد فصيام ثلثة ايام وسبعة اذا رجع الى اهله (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۴۶ من قال يصوم اذا رجع الی اھلہ ج ثالث ،ص ۱۵۲، نمبر ۱۳۰۰۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ گھر واپس آنے کے بعد روزے رکھے۔ حاشیہ : (ب) عطاء اس آیت و سبعہ اذار جستم کی تفسیر میں فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر چاہے تو راستے میں روزے رکھے اور اگر چاہے تو مکہ میں روزے رکھے (ج) سعید بن مسیب سے روایت ہے کہ جو ہدی نہ پائے تو وہ تین دن روزے رکھے اور سات دن جب گھر واپس آئے۔
Then he fasts seven days when he returns to his family; if he fasts them in Makkah after finishing Hajj, it is permissible. [693] (8) Then he fasts seven days when he returns to his family; so if he fasts in Makkah after finishing Hajj, it is permissible. For one who could not find a sacrificial animal and has to fast seven days after Hajj, according to Imam Abu Hanifa he can fast those seven days either after returning home or in Makkah if he wishes. The meaning of the verse 'and seven when you return' is 'when you return from Hajj' i.e., when you have finished Hajj, fast whether in Makkah, after returning home, or on the road. From 'Ata': he said regarding 'and seven when you return' (the verse): he said if he wishes he fasts them on the road, and if he wishes in Makkah (b) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 45 fi qada' al-sab'a al-faraq aw al-wasl, juz 3, p.151 no.12995). From this athar it is learned that he can fast in Makkah and on the road. Imam al-Shafi'i says that he should fast only after returning home. His argument is that the verse says 'and seven when you return', meaning when you come back home. Therefore he fasts only after returning home. (2) In the athar from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab: ... 'So whoever cannot find, then fasting three days and seven when he returns to his family' (c) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 46 man qala yasumu idha raja'a ila ahlihi, juz 3, p.152 no.13000). From this athar it is learned that he fasts after returning home. Footnote: (b) 'Ata' interprets the verse 'and seven when you return' and says: if he wishes, he fasts them on the road, and if he wishes, he fasts them in Makkah. (c) It is narrated from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab: whoever cannot find (a sacrificial animal), then he fasts three days and seven when he returns to his family.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the location for observing the seven fasts after Hajj for a mutamatti' who cannot afford a sacrifice. The matn states that fasting seven days 'when he returns to his family' is permissible, and Abu Hanifa interprets 'return' as 'return from Hajj', not necessarily returning home. Thus, the fasts can be observed in Makkah, on the road, or after reaching home. The proof is from the verse 'and seven when you return', which Abu Hanifa takes to mean 'when you return from Hajj' (i.e., finish the rites). This is supported by an athar from 'Ata' who said one may fast on the road or in Makkah. In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i insists that the fasts must be after returning home, citing the same verse but interpreting 'return' as return to one's family, and an athar from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab. The Hanafi position is more flexible, allowing the fasts to be done anywhere after the completion of Hajj. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Hanifa, as it gives ease to the pilgrim.

Key Terms
رجعتم (raja'tum): Literal 'you return'; interpreted by Hanafis as returning from Hajj (completion of rites), by Shafi'is as returning to one's homeland.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, where can the seven fasts of tamattu' be observed?
A) Only after returning home.
B) Only in Makkah after finishing Hajj.
C) In Makkah, on the road, or after returning home.
D) Only on the days of Tashriq.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows the seven fasts of tamattu' to be observed anywhere after completing Hajj, whether in Makkah, on the road, or at home.

The Qarin Who Misses Makkah: Abandoning Umrah Before Arafat
Ruling for a qarin failing to perform Umrah before Hajj rites

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a qarin who goes directly to Arafat without performing Umrah and explain the change in obligation.

Core Idea
Skipping Umrah before Arafat invalidates the qiran; a new dam and qada' become wajib.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in Hajj: a person who enters ihram for both Hajj and Umrah (qiran) but fails to enter Makkah to perform the Umrah before proceeding to Arafat. The Hanafi school clarifies the legal consequences: the qiran is not valid, and different obligations arise. The passage also discusses the option of fasting on the days of Mina if a sacrifice cannot be made, supported by an athar from Ibn 'Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? (A qarin going directly to Arafat without entering Makkah). What is the initial hukm? (Qiran invalid; Umrah abandoned).
2
Determine the change in obligations
What happens to the qiran sacrifice? (Drops). What becomes wajib? (Dam for abandoning Umrah and qada' of Umrah).
The original qiran dam is no longer due because the qiran condition was not met.
3
Locate the dalil for the fasting concession
The footnote cites Ibn 'Umar's statement about fasting on days of Mina for tamattu'. How does this apply to the qarin case?
The fasting option is mentioned for those who cannot afford a sacrifice, extending the ruling from tamattu' by analogy.
4
Analyze the sequence requirement
Why is it necessary to perform Umrah before Hajj for qiran? What is the underlying principle?
Qiran requires entering Makkah and performing Umrah before the Hajj rites; failure to do so changes the legal status.

فان لم يدخل القارن بمكة وتوجه الى عرفات فقد صار رافضا لعمرته فان لم يجد هديا ولم يصم صام ايام منى ( الف ) ( بخاری شریف، باب صیام ایام التشريق ص ۲۶۸ نمبر ۱۹۹۹ مصنف ابن ابی شیبہ ۴۴ من رخص في الصوم ولم بر علیه حد یا حثالث ص ۱۵۱، نمبر ۱۲۹۹۱) (۱۹۴) (۹) پس اگر قارن مکہ مکرمہ میں داخل نہیں ہوا اور عرفات کی طرف متوجہ ہو گیا، پس وقوف عرفہ کی وجہ سے عمرہ چھوڑ نینوالا ہو گیا اور اس سے دم قران ساقط ہو جائے گا، اور اس پر عمرہ کے چھوڑنے کا دم لازم ہوگا اور اس پر عمرہ کی قضا لازم ہوگی۔ الشرق قارن بننے کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ حج سے پہلے عمرہ کیا ہو، اگر حج کے بعد عمرہ کیا تو وہ قارن نہیں بنے گا اور نہ اس پر دم قرآن لازم ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ قارن ہی نہیں بنا۔ اب جو آدمی مکہ مکرمہ ہی نہیں آیا سیدھا عرفات چلا گیا تو یقینی بات ہے کہ وہ حج سے پہلے عمرہ نہ کر سکا اس کا عمرہ حاشیہ : (الف) ابن عمر نے فرمایا روزہ اس آدمی کے لئے ہے جو عمرہ کو حج کے ساتھ ملا کر تمتع کرے عرفہ کے دن تک، پس اگر ہدی نہ پائے اور روز و نہ رکھ سکے تو منی کے دنوں میں روزے رکھے (یعنی ایام تشریق میں روزے رکھے )
If the qarin does not enter Makkah and proceeds to Arafat, then he becomes one who abandons his Umrah; if he does not find a sacrificial animal and does not fast, he fasts the days of Mina (i.e., days of Tashriq). (a) (Bukhari, Bab Sawm Ayyam al-Tashriq, p.268 no.1999; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 44 man rakhkhasa fi al-sawm wa lam yarah 'ala hadd, juz 3, p.151 no.12991). (194) (9) So if the qarin did not enter Makkah and headed towards Arafat, then by standing at Arafat he becomes one who has abandoned his Umrah, and the blood (sacrifice) of qiran drops, and upon him becomes obligatory a blood (sacrifice) for abandoning the Umrah, and qada' of the Umrah becomes obligatory. For becoming a qarin, it is necessary that he performed Umrah before Hajj; if he performed Umrah after Hajj, he does not become a qarin and the qiran sacrifice is not obligatory because he did not become a qarin. Now, a person who did not come to Makkah at all and went straight to Arafat, it is certain that he could not perform Umrah before Hajj. His Umrah... Footnote: (a) Ibn 'Umar said: Fasting is for one who performs Tamattu' with Umrah to Hajj until the day of Arafah; then if he does not find a sacrificial animal and does not fast, he fasts the days of Mina (i.e., the days of Tashriq).
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling for a qarin (one who performs Hajj and Umrah together in a single state of ihram) who fails to enter Makkah before proceeding to Arafat for the Hajj. The key point: to be a valid qarin, one must perform Umrah before performing the Hajj rites. If the person goes directly to Arafat without entering Makkah to perform Umrah, he has effectively abandoned the Umrah. Consequently, the obligation of the qiran sacrifice (dam qiran) is dropped. Instead, he must offer a different blood sacrifice (dam) for abandoning the Umrah, and he must also make up (qada') that Umrah at a later time. The text also mentions that if such a person cannot afford a sacrifice and cannot fast, he may fast on the days of Mina (days of Tashriq). This part is supported by an athar from Ibn 'Umar, though it seems more relevant to a mutamatti' but is applied here. The footnote clarifies that the days of Tashriq are permissible for fasting in this case of necessity, contrary to the normal prohibition. The ruling underscores the importance of sequence in qiran: Umrah must precede Hajj within the same ihram.

Key Terms
قارن (qarin): One who performs Hajj and Umrah together in a single state of ihram, also known as Qiran.
رافض لعمرته (rafid li-'umratihi): One who abandons his Umrah by not performing it before the Hajj rites, leading to an invalid Qiran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to a qarin who goes directly to Arafat without entering Makkah to perform Umrah?
A) His qiran is valid, and he only needs the qiran sacrifice.
B) He abandons his Umrah, so the qiran sacrifice drops, and he must offer a dam for abandoning Umrah and perform qada' of Umrah.
C) He must perform Umrah after Hajj to complete the qiran.
D) He is excused from any sacrifice because of the difficulty.

Key Takeaway
A qarin who goes directly to Arafat without performing Umrah invalidates the qiran and must offer a separate dam and make up the Umrah.

Timing of the Seven Post-Hajj Fasts: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on post-Hajj fasting timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when the seven fasts for a mutamatti' may be performed, identify the key evidence (Quranic verse and athar), and distinguish the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The seven fasts may be fasted anywhere after Hajj — not only at home.

When a pilgrim performing tamattu' or qiran cannot afford a sacrificial animal, they must fast ten days: three during Hajj and seven after. But where and when must those seven be observed? The Hanafi school, led by Imam Abu Hanifah, grants flexibility — Makkah, the road, or home — while Imam al-Shafi'i insists they must be delayed until returning to one's family. This lesson unpacks the textual evidence and reasoning behind both views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Dispute
Locate the exact issue: the timing and location of the seven fasts for a mutamatti' or qarin who substitutes fasting for sacrifice. Note the two positions: Hanafi flexibility vs. Shafi'i restriction.
2
Examine the Hanafi Evidence
Read the Quranic verse (2:196) 'and seven when you return' and note how Hanafis interpret 'return' as 'return from Hajj' (not necessarily to home). Then review the athar from 'Ata that explicitly permits fasting on the road or in Makkah.
Hanafi interpretation relies on broadening the meaning of 'raja'tum'.
3
Examine the Shafi'i Evidence
Read the same verse and observe the Shafi'i reading: 'when you return' means 'when you return to your families'. Note the supporting athar from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib that links fasting to 'when he returns to his family'.
Shafi'i view takes the literal sense of 'ila ahlihim'.
4
Analyze the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
Contrast the real-world outcome: a Hanafi pilgrim can fast in Makkah immediately after Hajj or on the road home, while a Shafi'i must wait until reaching home. Understand that both consider the fasts valid, but the timing obligation differs.
