[193) (8) Then he fasts seven days when he returns to his family. If he fasts them in Makkah after completing Hajj, it is permissible. [294] (9) If the qarin does not enter Makkah and proceeds to Arafat, he becomes an abandoner of his Umrah. If he does not find a sacrificial animal and does not fast, he fasts the days of Mina. (a) (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter on Fasting the Days of Tashriq, p. 268 no. 1999; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah 44, no. 12991) From this athar it is understood that if he does not find a sacrificial animal and also cannot fast, he fasts during the days of Tashriq, and keeps the remaining seven fasts after Hajj. [693] (8) Then he fasts seven days when he returns to his home. So if he fasts in Makkah after completing Hajj, it is also permissible. According to Imam Abu Hanifah, if he does not find a sacrificial animal and needs to fast seven days after Hajj, he can fast those seven days upon returning home, or if he wishes to fast in Makkah, he may do so there. The meaning of the verse 'and seven when you return' is 'when you return from Hajj': when you finish Hajj, then fast, whether in Makkah, after returning home, or on the road. From Ata: He said regarding the verse 'and seven when you return', he said: If he wishes, he fasts them on the road, and if he wishes, in Makkah. (b) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah 45, no. 12995) From this athar it is understood that he can fast in Makkah and on the road. Imam al-Shafi'i says: He fasts only after returning home. His evidence is that the verse says 'and seven when you return', meaning when you return home. Therefore he fasts only after returning home. (2) There is an athar from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib: ... Whoever cannot find [a sacrificial animal], then fasting three days and seven when he returns to his family. (c) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah 46, no. 13000) From this athar it is understood that he fasts after returning home. Footnote: (a) Ibn Umar said: Fasting is for the one who combines Umrah with Hajj as tamattu' until the day of Arafah. If he does not find a sacrificial animal and cannot fast, then he fasts in the days of Mina (i.e., days of Tashriq). (b) Ata in interpretation of the verse 'and seven when you return' says: If he wishes, he fasts on the road, and if he wishes, in Makkah. (c) Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib reports: Whoever does not find [a sacrificial animal], then he fasts three days and seven when he returns to his family.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i regarding the timing of the seven fasts that a mutamatti' or qarin must observe if they cannot afford a sacrificial animal (hady). The source text (matn) states the ruling: 'Then he fasts seven days when he returns to his family, but if he fasts them in Makkah after completing Hajj, it is permissible.' The commentary then explains the Hanafi position of Imam Abu Hanifah: the seven days may be fasted anywhere—in Makkah, on the road, or at home—because the Quranic phrase 'when you return' (idha raja'tum) is interpreted as 'when you return from Hajj' (min al-Hajj), not specifically to one's home. Support is provided by an athar from 'Ata who allows fasting on the road or in Makkah. The Shafi'i position is then presented: they maintain that the fasts must be performed only after returning home, citing the literal meaning of 'to your families' (ila ahlihim) in the verse and an athar from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib that explicitly mentions 'when he returns to his family'. The passage thus presents both positions with their respective evidence, typical of Hanafi fiqh works that document ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
قارن (qārin): One who performs Hajj and Umrah together (qiran), i.e., enters ihram for both simultaneously.
هدی (hady): Sacrificial animal offered as a ritual obligation for those performing tamattu' or qiran.
أيام التشريق (ayyām al-tashrīq): The three days following the Day of Sacrifice (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah).
رجعتم (raja'tum): The key word in the Quranic verse meaning 'you return', interpreted differently by schools.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) between the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the seven fasts?
A) Hanafi requires fasting only in Makkah; Shafi'i allows anywhere.
B) Hanafi allows fasting in Makkah, on the road, or at home; Shafi'i only after returning home.
C) Both schools agree that fasting must be in Makkah.
D) Hanafi says the fasts are not wajib; Shafi'i says they are fard.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits the seven substitute fasts to be performed anywhere after the completion of Hajj, while the Shafi'i school restricts them to after returning home — a difference rooted in the interpretation of the Quranic word 'raja'tum'.

Ruling on a Qarin Who Bypasses Makkah
States the ruling for a qarin who bypasses Makkah and the evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a qarin who proceeds directly to Arafat without entering Makkah and explain the evidence from the hadith of Aisha.

Core Idea
A qarin who misses Umrah must sacrifice for abandoning Umrah and make it up, but the qiran dam falls.

Imagine you have entered ihram for Hajj and Umrah together (qiran), but due to travel constraints you bypass Makkah and head straight to Arafat. What happens to your Umrah? This passage from a Hanafi fiqh text clarifies that such a person is considered to have abandoned the Umrah. The sacrificial animal for qiran is no longer required; instead, a separate sacrifice and a makeup Umrah become obligatory. We will explore the reasoning and the prophetic evidence behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act: a qarin who does not enter Makkah and goes directly to Arafat. The ruling: the dam for qiran is dropped (saaqit), and a dam for abandoning Umrah (dam al-rafd) and qada of Umrah become wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith of Aisha (Bukhari, no. 1786) where she performed Umrah after Hajj due to menses, and the Prophet did not require a sacrifice for qiran. Instead, he sacrificed a cow for her, interpreted as a dam for abandoning Umrah.
Also supporting evidence from Muslims hadith of Jabir and athar of Tawus.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In Aisha's case, she was not a qarin because she could not perform Umrah before Hajj. The Prophet's sacrifice on her behalf was not a qiran dam but a compensation for abandoning the intended Umrah. This shows that if Umrah is abandoned for a valid reason, a dam is required, but not the qiran dam.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a qarin who fails to enter Makkah must still sacrifice for abandoning Umrah and perform qada, but he is not burdened with the qiran dam. This distinguishes between two types of sacrifices.
5
Evaluate the evidence strength
The hadith is sahih with qat'i thubut, but its dalala is zanni (open to interpretation). The Hanafi interpretation aligns with the principle that dam al-rafd replaces dam al-qiran when the combined intention is thwarted.

Source Text

اخبرتني عائشة قالت خرجنا مع رسول الله الله موا فين لهلال ذى الحجة ... ارسل معى عبد الرحمان الى التنعيم فارد فها فاهللت بعمرة مكان عمرتها فقضى الله حجها وعمرتها ولم يكن في شيء من ذلك هدى ولا صدقة ولا صوم (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب الاعتمار بعد الج بغیر ہی ص ۲۴۰ نمبر ۱۷۸۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عمرہ چھوڑنے کے بدلے عمرہ کرنا ہوگا۔ اور یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ حج کے بعد عمرہ کرنے کی وجہ سے دم قران لازم نہیں ہوگا البتہ عمرہ چھوڑنے سے عمرہ چھوڑ نے کا دم لازم ہوگا ۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن جابر قال ذبح رسول الله الا الله عن عائشة بقرة يوم النحر (ب)(مسلم شريف، باب جواز الاشتراك في المهدي الخ ص ۴۲۴ نمبر ۱۳۱۹) اس حدیث میں حضرت عائشہ کی جانب سے حضور نے گائے ذبح کی ، اور حضرت عائشہ قارن تو تھی نہیں کیونکہ حیض آنے کی وجہ سے وہ عمرہ چھوڑ چکی تھیں، پھر بھی آپ نے ان کی جانب سے ایک گائے ذبح کی۔ اس کا مطلب یہ کہ یہ عمرہ چھوڑنے کی وجہ سے دم تھا، اس لئے عمرہ چھوڑنے کی وجہ سے دم لازم ہو گا (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن طاؤس فـي الـحـرم لـعمرة اعترض له قال يبعث بهدى ثم يحسب كم يسير ثم يحتاط بايام ثم يحل (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ۵۷ فی الرجل اذا اصل بعمرة فاحصر ، ج ثالث ، ص ۱۵۹، نمبر ۱۳۰۷۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عمرہ نہ کر سکے تو اس کی ہدی بھیجے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عائشہ فرماتی ہیں کہ ہم حضور کے ساتھ ذی الحجہ کے چاند کے وقت نکلے. میرے ساتھ عبد الرحمان کو تعمیم تک بھیجا، پس انہوں نے حضرت عائشہ کو پیچھے بٹھایا ، پس عمرہ کی جگہ انہوں نے عمرہ کا احرام باندھا، پس اللہ نے ان کے حج اور عمرہ کو پورا کیا اور اس کی وجہ سے ہدی ، صدقہ اور روزے بھی لازم نہیں ہوئے (ب) حضور نے عائشہ کے لئے دسویں ذی الحجہ کو گائے ذبح کی۔
(194) (9) So if the qarin does not enter Makkah and proceeds towards Arafat, then due to the standing at Arafat he becomes an abandoner of his Umrah, and the dam for qiran is dropped from him, and he owes a dam for abandoning the Umrah, and he owes the qada of that Umrah. Al-Sharh: For one to become a qarin, it is necessary that he perform Umrah before Hajj. If he performs Umrah after Hajj, he does not become a qarin, and the dam for qiran is not obligatory on him, because he did not become a qarin. Now the person who did not enter Makkah and went directly to Arafat, it is certain that he could not perform Umrah before Hajj; his Umrah was lost due to the standing, and the dam for qiran is dropped, and he owes a dam for abandoning the Umrah, and he owes its qada. So he did not become a qarin. However, due to abandoning the Umrah, qada of Umrah is obligatory, and due to abandoning Umrah after entering ihram, dam for abandonment (dam al-rafd) is obligatory. Aisha narrated: We went out with the Messenger of Allah ... when the new moon of Dhul-Hijjah appeared ... He sent Abdur Rahman with me to al-Tan'im, and he seated me behind him, and I entered ihram for Umrah in place of her Umrah, and Allah fulfilled her Hajj and Umrah, and there was no sacrificial animal, charity, or fasting involved in that. (a) (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter on Umrah after Hajj without Hady, p. 240 no. 1786) From this hadith it is understood that in place of the abandoned Umrah, one must perform Umrah. And it is also understood that performing Umrah after Hajj does not necessitate dam for qiran; rather, abandoning Umrah necessitates dam for abandonment. Its evidence is the hadith from Jabir: The Messenger of Allah sacrificed a cow on behalf of Aisha on the Day of Sacrifice. (b) (Sahih Muslim, Chapter on Permissibility of Sharing in Sacrificial Animals, p. 424 no. 1319) In this hadith, the Prophet sacrificed a cow on behalf of Aisha, and Aisha was not a qarin because she had abandoned her Umrah due to menstruation; yet the Prophet sacrificed a cow on her behalf. This means that this was a dam for abandoning Umrah, so dam is obligatory for abandoning Umrah. (2) There is an athar from Tawus regarding one who is prevented from Umrah by an obstacle: He said: He sends a sacrificial animal, then calculates how many days (he will travel), then takes precaution with additional days, then exits ihram. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah 57, no. 13078) From this athar it is understood that if one cannot perform Umrah, he sends a sacrificial animal. Footnote: (a) Aisha said: We went out with the Prophet at the time of the new moon of Dhul-Hijjah. He sent Abdur Rahman with me to al-Tan'im, and he seated me behind him, and I entered ihram for Umrah in place of her Umrah, and Allah fulfilled her Hajj and Umrah, and no sacrificial animal, charity, or fasting was required. (b) The Prophet sacrificed a cow for Aisha on the 10th of Dhul-Hijjah.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding a qarin who fails to enter Makkah and proceeds directly to Arafat. The matn states that such a person abandons his Umrah, so the dam for qiran (combined Hajj and Umrah) is dropped, and instead he owes a dam for abandoning Umrah (dam al-rafd) and must perform qada (make-up) of the Umrah. The commentary clarifies the prerequisite for qiran: the Umrah must be performed before Hajj; if one goes directly to Arafat, he cannot perform Umrah beforehand, so he does not become a qiran. Hence the dam qiran falls, but he still owes dam for abandoning the Umrah he had intended. The commentary then provides evidence: the hadith of Aisha, who, due to menstruation, could not perform her Umrah before Hajj? Actually, the hadith shows that Aisha performed Umrah after Hajj (with the help of Abdur Rahman), indicating that Umrah after Hajj is valid but does not make one a qarin. The Prophet sacrificed a cow for her on the Day of Sacrifice, which was not a dam for qiran (since she was not a qarin) but rather a dam for abandoning Umrah, thus supporting the ruling. Another athar from Tawus discusses one who is prevented from completing Umrah (ihsar) and must send a sacrificial animal. The passage thus establishes that the dam for abandoning Umrah is a separate obligation, and qada of the Umrah is also required.

Key Terms
رفض العمرة (rafḍ al-ʿumrah): Abandoning the performance of Umrah after having entered ihram for it, necessitating a dam (sacrificial penalty).
دم القران (dam al-qirān): The sacrificial animal required for one performing Hajj qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram).
قضاء (qaḍāʾ): Making up a missed or invalidated religious obligation, such as Umrah that was abandoned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to the dam for qiran when a qarin bypasses Makkah and goes directly to Arafat?
A) It remains obligatory.
B) It is dropped and no other dam is due.
C) It is dropped, and he owes a dam for abandoning Umrah.
D) It is dropped, and he must fast instead.

Key Takeaway
A qarin who cannot perform Umrah before Arafat owes a dam and makeup Umrah, but not the qiran dam.

Ruling on a Qarin who Misses Umrah: Qada and Dam Rafd
Explains ruling for Qarin who misses Umrah and its compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a Qarin who misses Umrah, identify the evidence from hadith, and distinguish between dam al-Qiran and dam rafd.

Core Idea
A Qarin who misses Umrah must make it up and sacrifice a dam for abandonment, but not the dam of Qiran.

Imagine you intend both Hajj and Umrah together as a Qarin, but due to menstruation or another excuse, you cannot perform the Umrah before the Hajj. What is your obligation? This passage clarifies that the dam of Qiran is not required because you did not complete the combination; instead, you must make up the missed Umrah after Hajj and sacrifice a separate dam (dam rafd) for abandoning the Umrah after entering ihram. The text supports this with hadith and athar, and contrasts with the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
Extract the Three-Part Ruling
Identify the three components of the ruling: (1) no dam al-Qiran is due, (2) a dam for abandonment (dam rafd) is wajib, (3) making up the missed Umrah (qada) is wajib.
The ruling is not about the validity of Hajj but about compensating a missed wajib act.
2
Analyze the First Hadith (Aisha)
Read the hadith from Bukhari: Aisha missed Umrah due to menstruation, made it up after Hajj, and the Prophet did not prescribe any dam or charity. This establishes that qada is sufficient; no dam al-Qiran is due.
The hadith does not explicitly mention dam rafd, so another proof is needed for that.
3
Analyze the Second Hadith (Cow Sacrifice)
Read the hadith from Muslim: The Prophet sacrificed a cow for Aisha on the Day of Nahr. Since Aisha was not a Qarin, the sacrifice must have been for abandoning Umrah. This proves dam rafd is wajib.
This hadith provides the basis for the separate dam, even though Aisha was not a Qarin.
4
Consider the Athar from Tawus
Read the athar: one prevented from Umrah sends a hady and estimates to become halal. This supports the principle of sending a sacrifice for missed Umrah, reinforcing the dam rafd.
This athar is about ihsar (prevention), but the text uses it to strengthen the concept of sacrifice for missed Umrah.
5
Contrast the Shafi'i Position
Note that the Shafi'i school holds that a Qarin who misses Umrah simply becomes a Mufrid (single intent for Hajj) and no dam is required. The Hanafi school requires both qada and dam rafd.
The difference stems from whether the missed Umrah is considered a deficiency requiring compensation or a change of intent.

The Book of Hajj: [The Qarin] who stands [at Arafat] but misses the Umrah: he is not required to sacrifice the dam of Qiran, but he must sacrifice a dam for abandoning the Umrah and must make it up. [Urdu commentary:] He missed [the Umrah] so he did not become a Qarin. Rather, due to abandoning the Umrah, making it up becomes necessary, and due to abandoning the Umrah after tying the ihram, a dam for abandonment becomes necessary. Aisha narrated: We went out with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) ... He sent Abdur Rahman with me to Tan'im, he seated me behind him, and I entered ihram for Umrah in place of my [missed] Umrah. Allah completed her Hajj and Umrah, and there was no sacrificial animal, charity, or fasting in that. (Bukhari, Bab al-I'timar ba'd al-Hajj, no. 1786). From this hadith we learn that for abandoning Umrah, one must perform Umrah [as qada]. And we also learn that performing Umrah after Hajj does not necessitate dam al-Qiran, but abandoning Umrah necessitates dam for abandonment. The proof for this is the hadith of Jabir: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) sacrificed a cow for Aisha on the Day of Nahr. (Muslim, Bab Jawaz al-Ishtirak fi al-Hady, no. 1319). In this hadith, the Prophet sacrificed a cow for Aisha, and she was not a Qarin because she had abandoned Umrah due to menstruation; nevertheless, the Prophet sacrificed a cow for her. This means that this dam was for abandoning Umrah, therefore dam becomes necessary for abandoning Umrah. (2) An athar: From Tawus concerning one who is prevented from completing Umrah while in the Haram: he said, 'He should send a hady, then calculate how far [he has traveled], then be cautious with days, then become halal.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, no. 13078). From this athar we learn that if one cannot perform Umrah, he should send the hady.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling for a person who performs Hajj as a Qarin but misses the Umrah due to a valid excuse like menstruation. The author states that such a person does not incur the dam of Qiran because he did not complete the Qiran combination; rather, he must make up the missed Umrah and sacrifice a dam for abandoning it after assuming ihram. The text then cites two hadiths to support this: first, the hadith of Aisha, in which she missed Umrah due to menstruation during the Farewell Hajj, and the Prophet instructed her to perform Umrah from Tan'im after the Hajj, and no additional sacrifice was required. This proves that missing Umrah only necessitates qada, not dam al-Qiran. The second hadith shows that the Prophet sacrificed a cow for Aisha on the Day of Nahr, indicating that a dam is due for abandoning Umrah, even though she was not a Qarin. Additionally, an effect (athar) from Tawus is mentioned for the case of one who is prevented from completing Umrah (ihsar), stating that he should send a sacrificial animal and then make a reasonable estimate to become halal. The passage concludes with footnotes explaining the hadiths.

Key Terms
دم رفض (dam rafd): A blood sacrifice required for abandoning an obligatory act of Hajj or Umrah after assuming ihram.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed obligatory act of worship, here referring to performing the missed Umrah after the Hajj.
قارن (qarin): A person intending both Hajj and Umrah together in one ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He must still sacrifice dam al-Qiran
B) He must make up the Umrah (qada) and no dam is due
C) He must make up the Umrah and sacrifice a dam for abandoning it
D) He does not need to do anything extra

Key Takeaway
A Qarin who misses Umrah must make it up (qada) and sacrifice a dam rafd; he does not owe dam al-Qiran.

Tamattu' in Hajj: Definition, Superiority, and Method
Opening of the chapter on Tamattu' in the book of Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of Tamattu', explain its superior status over Ifrad in the Hanafi school with Quranic and hadith proofs, and describe its practical method including the two types of mutamatti'.

Core Idea
Tamattu' combines Umrah and Hajj in one journey; it is the superior form of Hajj in the Hanafi school.

Welcome to the chapter on Tamattu'! This lesson will clarify what Tamattu' is, why the Hanafi school considers it the best way to perform Hajj, and how it is actually done. You will learn the key proofs from the Quran and Sunnah, as well as an important difference of opinion within the school itself.

Guided Path
1
Define Tamattu'
Identify the core meaning: Tamattu' is performing Umrah during the Hajj months (Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, first ten days of Dhul Hijjah), becoming halal, then later performing Hajj in the same year.
The word 'tamattu' implies enjoyment, as one enjoys being in a halal state between Umrah and Hajj.
2
Understand its superiority
The passage states clearly that Tamattu' is superior to Ifrad in the Hanafi school. Identify the two proofs: Quran 2:196 and the hadith from Aisha about the Farewell Hajj. Note the reasoning: two acts in one journey, and the Prophet's command to those without hady.
There is also a narration from Abu Hanifa that Ifrad is superior; note this as an intra-madhhab difference but the relied-upon view is Tamattu'.
3
Recognize the two types of Mutamatti'
The passage divides the mutamatti' into those who drive the sacrificial animal (hady) from the miqat and those who do not. The key difference is whether one brings the hady along or acquires it later.
The Prophet himself drove the hady during the Farewell Hajj.
4
Describe the practical method
Outline the steps: entering ihram for Umrah from the miqat, entering Makkah, performing tawaf, sa'y, then shaving or trimming hair to become halal. Later, for Hajj, one re-enters ihram.
This method ensures one is in a halal state between the two rites, which is the distinguishing feature of Tamattu'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التمتع
[۲۹۵] (۱) التمتع افضل من الافراد عندنا [ ۹۶ (۲) والمتمتع على وجهين متمتع يسوق الهدى ومتمتع لا يسوق الهدى [۲۹۷](۳) وصفة التمتع ان يبتدأ من الميقات فيحرم بالعمرة ويدخل مكة فيطوف لها ويسعى ويحلق أو يقصر وقد حل من عمرته 
باب التمتع )
ضروری نوں حج کے مہینے شوال، ذی قعدہ اور ذی الحجہ کی دس تاریخ میں عمرے کا احرام باندھے پھر عمرہ کر کے حلال ہو جائے اور حج کے زمانے میں حج کا احرام باندھ کر حج پورا کرے اس کو تمتع کہتے ہیں۔ اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ فمن تمتع بالعمرة الى الحج فما استيسر من الهدى (الف ) ( آیت ۹۶ اسورة البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت سے تمتع ثابت ہوتا ہے (۲) حجتہ الوداع میں وہ احادیث ہیں جن میں آپ نے صحابہ کو عمرہ کر کے احرام کھلوایا۔ [۶۹۵](۱) ہمارے نزدیک تمتع افراد سے افضل ہے۔
تمتع میں دو عبادتیں ایک سفر میں ادا کی جاتی ہیں عمرہ اور حج اس لئے یہ افضل ہو گا (۲) صحابہ کو حجتہ الوداع میں عمرہ کر کے حلال ہونے کے لئے آپ نے فرمایا عن عائشة قالت خرجنا مع النبي الا الله ... فامر النبي الا الله من لم يكن ساق الهدى ان يحل فحل من لم يكن ساق الهدى (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب استمتع والاقران والافراد بالملح ص ۲۱۲ نمبر ۱۵۶) اس حدیث میں آپ نے صحابہ کو عمرہ کر کے حلال ہونے کا حکم دیا جس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ تمتع افضل ہے۔ نانه امام ابو حنیفہ کی ایک روایت یہ بھی ہے کہ افراد افضل ہے۔ کیونکہ اس میں صرف حج کے لئے سفر ہوتا ہے اور حج کے لئے تلبیہ اور تکبیر کی کثرت ہوتی ہے۔
[۲۹](۲) متمتع کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) متمتع جو ہدی ہانکے اور دوسرا متمتع جو ہدی نہ ہانکے۔ تقریب کے لوگ میقات سے ہی ہدی لیکر جاتے ہیں تو وہ ہدی ہانکنے والا متمتع ہوا اور جو لوگ ہدی ساتھ نہ لے جائے بلکہ بعد میں ہدی خرید کر ذبح کرے وہ متمتع ہے جو ہدی ساتھ نہ لے جائے ۔ حضور حجتہ الوداع میں ہدی ساتھ لیکر تشریف لے گئے تھے۔ [۶۹۷] (۳) تمتع کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ میقات سے عمرے کا احرام شروع کرے اور مکہ میں داخل ہو۔ پس عمرے کا طواف کرے ، سعی کرے اور حلق یا قصر کرائے اور اپنے عمرے سے حلال ہو جائے۔
اس کی تفصیل گزر چکی ہے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) جس نے عمرہ کو حج کے ساتھ مل کر تمتع کیا تو جو کچھ ہدی میں سے آسان ہو وہ لازم ہے (ب) حضور نے ان کو حکم دیا جس نے ہدی نہ ہانکی ہو کہ حلال ہو جائے۔ تو جس نے ہدی نہ ہانکی تھی وہ حلال ہو گئے۔
Chapter on Tamattu'. [295] (1) Tamattu' is superior to Ifrad according to us. (2) The Mutamatti' is of two types: one who drives the hady and one who does not drive the hady. [297] (3) The description of Tamattu' is that one begins from the miqat and enters ihram for Umrah, enters Makkah, performs tawaf for it, performs sa'y, and shaves or shortens [hair], and becomes halal from his Umrah. [Urdu commentary:] Essential note: One should enter ihram for Umrah during the months of Hajj - Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah - then perform Umrah and become halal, then enter ihram for Hajj during the Hajj season and complete the Hajj. This is called Tamattu'. Its proof is the verse: 'Then whoever performs Tamattu' of Umrah to Hajj, then [sacrifice] whatever is easy of the hady' (Quran 2:196). This verse establishes Tamattu'. Also, during the Farewell Hajj, there are hadiths in which the Prophet commanded the Companions to perform Umrah and then take off their ihram. [695] (1) According to us, Tamattu' is superior to Ifrad. Because in Tamattu', two worship acts are performed in one journey: Umrah and Hajj, so it is superior. Also, during the Farewell Hajj, the Prophet ordered the Companions to perform Umrah and become halal. He said [as per the hadith]: 'Aisha said: We went out with the Prophet... and the Prophet ordered those who had not driven the hady to become halal, so those who had not driven the hady became halal.' (Bukhari, Bab al-Tamattu' wa al-Qiran wa al-Ifrad bi al-Hajj, no. 156). In this hadith, the Prophet commanded them to perform Umrah and become halal, which indicates that Tamattu' is superior. However, there is also a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that Ifrad is superior because in it the journey is solely for Hajj, and there is abundant talbiyah and takbir for Hajj. [29] (2) There are two types of Mutamatti': one who drives the hady and one who does not drive the hady. The people of the vicinity take the hady from the miqat, so they are the ones who drive the hady. Those who do not take the hady with them but later buy and sacrifice it are Mutamatti' who do not drive the hady. The Prophet (peace be upon him) took the hady with him during the Farewell Hajj. [697] (3) The method of Tamattu' is that one begins the ihram for Umrah from the miqat, enters Makkah, performs tawaf of Umrah, performs sa'y, and shaves or shortens [hair], and becomes halal from his Umrah. Its detail has already passed. Footnotes: (a) 'Then whoever performs Tamattu' of Umrah to Hajj, then whatever is easy of the hady is required.' (b) 'The Prophet ordered those who had not driven the hady to become halal, so those who had not driven the hady became halal.'
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage introduces the Chapter of Tamattu' in the book of Hajj. It begins by stating three key points: first, that Tamattu' is superior to Ifrad according to the Hanafi school. The author explains the reasoning: Tamattu' combines two worship acts (Umrah and Hajj) in one journey, making it more virtuous. He supports this with the Quranic verse (2:196) and the hadith from Aisha about the Farewell Hajj, where the Prophet ordered those without sacrificial animals to make their ihram for Umrah and then become halal. However, an alternative narration from Imam Abu Hanifa himself mentions that Ifrad may be superior because it focuses solely on Hajj with more acts of devotion. Second, the passage divides the Mutamatti' into two types: those who bring a sacrificial animal (hady) from the miqat and those who do not. Third, it describes the practical method of Tamattu': one enters ihram for Umrah from the miqat, performs tawaf and sa'y in Makkah, shaves or shortens hair, and becomes halal. Then later, for Hajj, one re-enters ihram. The footnotes clarify the Quranic verse and hadith.

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu'): A type of Hajj in which one first performs Umrah during the Hajj months, becomes halal, then later performs Hajj in the same year.
افراد (ifrad): A type of Hajj where one enters ihram only for Hajj, without combining Umrah.
هدي (hady): A sacrificial animal brought or sent to the Haram for the purpose of Hajj or Umrah, often required for Tamattu' and Qiran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school's preferred view, which type of Hajj is superior?
A) Ifrad
B) Tamattu'
C) Qiran
D) It depends on the situation

Key Takeaway
Tamattu' is the superior form of Hajj in the Hanafi school, combining Umrah and Hajj in one journey, supported by Quranic verse and prophetic practice, and requiring a sacrifice for non-residents of Makkah.

Tamattu' is Superior to Ifrad: Proofs and Dispute
Ruling with proofs and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that tamattu' is superior to ifrad, explain the Quranic and hadith proofs, and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on this issue.

Core Idea
Tamattu' combines two acts of worship in one journey, making it superior to ifrad.

This passage establishes the Hanafi ruling that tamattu' is better than ifrad. It defines tamattu', provides scriptural evidence, and acknowledges a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that prefers ifrad. We will analyze the proofs and see which position is relied upon.

Guided Path
1
Define the two forms of Hajj
First, understand what tamattu' and ifrad mean. Tamattu' is performing 'umrah during the Hajj months, then becoming halal, then performing Hajj in the same journey. Ifrad is performing Hajj alone without 'umrah in the same journey.
Tamattu' requires a sacrificial animal (hady).
2
Identify the Hanafi position
The text states that according to the Hanafi school, tamattu' is superior (afdal) to ifrad. This is the mufta bihi position.
Both are valid, but tamattu' brings more reward.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
The verse 2:196 is cited: 'Whoever performs 'umrah [during the Hajj months] followed by Hajj, [must offer] whatever is available as a sacrificial animal.' This verse shows the validity and recommendation of tamattu'.
The obligation of a sacrifice indicates its virtue.
4
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith of Aisha reports that the Prophet ordered those who had not brought a sacrificial animal to become halal after 'umrah, showing tamattu' was practiced and encouraged.
This hadith from Bukhari (no. 156) is a key proof.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
There is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that ifrad is superior, because it focuses solely on Hajj with more talbiyah and takbir. However, the relied-upon position is that tamattu' is superior.
The dispute is within the Hanafi school; both views are valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التمتع
[۲۹۵] (۱) التمتع افضل من الافراد عندنا
ضروری نوں حج کے مہینے شوال، ذی قعدہ اور ذی الحجہ کی دس تاریخ میں عمرے کا احرام باندھے پھر عمرہ کر کے حلال ہو جائے اور حج کے زمانے میں حج کا احرام باندھ کر حج پورا کرے اس کو تمتع کہتے ہیں۔ اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ فمـن تـمــع بـالـعمـرة الـى الـحـج فما استيسر من الهدى (الف ) ( آیت ۹۶ اسورة البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت سے تمتع ثابت ہوتا ہے (۲) حجتہ الوداع میں وہ احادیث ہیں جن میں آپ نے صحابہ کو عمرہ کر کے احرام کھلوایا۔ [۶۹۵](۱) ہمارے نزدیک تمتع افراد سے افضل ہے۔

Chapter of Tamattu'. [295] (1) Tamattu' is superior to ifrad according to us. It is necessary that during the months of Hajj—Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul Hijjah—one enters ihram for 'umrah, then after completing 'umrah becomes halal, and then during the Hajj season enters ihram for Hajj and completes it; this is called tamattu'. Its proof is this verse: 'Whoever performs 'umrah [during the Hajj months] followed by Hajj, [must offer] whatever is available as a sacrificial animal' (Quran 2:196). This verse establishes tamattu'. (2) In the Farewell Hajj, there are hadiths in which the Prophet commanded the Companions to perform 'umrah and then become halal. [695](1) According to us, tamattu' is superior to ifrad. Tamattu' combines two acts of worship in one journey: 'umrah and Hajj, so it is superior. The Prophet said, as narrated by Aisha: 'We went out with the Prophet... and the Prophet ordered those who had not brought a sacrificial animal to become halal, so those who had not brought a sacrificial animal became halal.' (Bukhari, chapter on tamattu', qiran, and ifrad, p.212, no.156). This hadith shows that tamattu' is superior. There is also a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that ifrad is superior, because in ifrad one travels solely for Hajj and there is more talbiyah and takbir for Hajj.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the superiority of tamattu' over ifrad according to the Hanafi school. The author first defines tamattu': performing 'umrah during the Hajj months, then becoming halal, then performing Hajj in the same journey. This combines two acts of worship. The proof is the Quranic verse 2:196, which explicitly mentions tamattu' and attaches the obligation of a sacrificial animal, indicating its validity and recommendation. Additionally, the hadith of Aisha in Bukhari shows the Prophet ordering the Companions to do tamattu' in the Farewell Hajj, which establishes its virtue. The text then mentions an intra-Hanafi dispute: a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa holds that ifrad (Hajj alone) is superior because it involves exclusive focus on Hajj with more talbiyah and takbir. However, the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that tamattu' is afdal, as the commentary endorses it with evidence.

Key Terms
التّمتع (al-tamattu'): Combining 'umrah and hajj in one journey by first performing 'umrah, becoming halal, then performing hajj with a sacrifice.
الإفراد (al-ifrad): Performing hajj alone without 'umrah in the same journey.
الهَدْي (al-hady): The sacrificial animal required for tamattu' and qiran.

Key Takeaway
Tamattu' is superior to ifrad in the Hanafi school, supported by Quran and hadith, despite an intra-Hanafi narration preferring ifrad; the mufta bihi is tamattu'.

Two Types of Mutamatti'
Classification of mutamatti' based on bringing a sacrificial animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two types of mutamatti' based on the presence of the hady and state the ruling for each.

Core Idea
A mutamatti' either brings a sacrificial animal from the miqat or purchases it later—both are valid, but the first follows the Prophet's practice.

In Hanafi fiqh, pilgrims performing tamattu' (combining 'umrah and hajj in one journey) fall into two categories. The distinction lies in whether they bring a sacrificial animal (hady) from the miqat or procure it later in Makkah. This classification clarifies obligations and recommended acts for the pilgrim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Read the text and name the two types of mutamatti' mentioned.
The key phrase is 'yasūqu al-hady' (drives the hady).
2
Understand the difference
Explain what 'driving the hady' means: bringing the sacrificial animal from the miqat, versus not driving it and purchasing later.
Both types still owe a sacrifice; timing differs.
3
Note the Prophetic practice
Recognize that the Prophet (peace be upon him) drove the hady during the Farewell Hajj, making this type more virtuous.
This is referenced to show preference.
4
Determine the ruling
State that both types are valid (permissible), but driving the hady is sunnah (recommended) because it follows the Prophet's example.
The classification does not affect validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمتمتع على وجهين متمتع يسوق الهدى ومتمتع لا يسوق الهدى
متمتع کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) متمتع جو ہدی ہانکے اور دوسر استمتع جو ہدی نہ ہانکے۔ تقریب کے لوگ میقات سے ہی ہدی لیکر جاتے ہیں تو وہ ہدی ہانکنے والا متمتع ہوا اور جو لوگ ہدی ساتھ نہ لے جائے بلکہ بعد میں ہدی خرید کر ذبح کرے وہ متمتع ہے جو ہدی ساتھ نہ لے جائے ۔ حضور حجتہ الوداع میں ہدی ساتھ لیکر تشریف لے گئے تھے۔
And the mutamatti' is of two types: a mutamatti' who drives the sacrificial animal, and a mutamatti' who does not drive the sacrificial animal. There are two types of mutamatti': (1) the mutamatti' who drives the hady, and (2) the mutamatti' who does not drive the hady. Those who, from the miqat, bring the hady are the ones who drive it; those who do not bring it but later purchase and slaughter it are those who do not drive the hady. The Prophet, in the Farewell Hajj, drove the hady.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage is a straightforward classification of the mutamatti' (the one performing tamattu'). It divides him into two categories: one who brings a sacrificial animal (hady) from the miqat, and one who does not, but instead purchases it later in Makkah. The first type is called 'mutamatti' who drives the hady', as he drives it along with him. This is based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the Farewell Hajj, who drove the hady. The second type does not drive the hady but still owes a sacrifice; he will slaughter it after entering ihram for hajj. This classification is important because it affects the ruling of remaining in ihram or becoming halal after 'umrah.

Key Terms
متمتع (mutamatti'): One who performs tamattu': combines 'umrah and hajj in one journey.
يسوق الهدى (yasūqu al-hady): Driving the sacrificial animal; bringing the hady from the miqat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A mutamatti' is of two types based on whether he drives the hady from the miqat or not; both are valid but driving is more virtuous.

Procedure of Tamattu' (صفة التمتع)
Step-by-step procedure of tamattu' from miqat to halal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequence of actions in tamattu' from the miqat to becoming halal with correct order.

Core Idea
Tamattu' begins with ihram for 'umrah at the miqat and ends with halq or taqsir.

This lesson presents the concise description of tamattu' as found in classical Hanafi texts. Memorizing this five-step sequence is essential for performing or teaching the 'umrah portion of tamattu'. The passage is straightforward but foundational.

Guided Path
1
Identify the starting point
Recognize that tamattu' begins at the miqat with the intention and ihram for 'umrah.
The miqat is the designated boundary; one cannot cross it without ihram.
2
List the actions in order
After ihram, the pilgrim enters Makkah, performs tawaf, then sa'i, and finally shaves or shortens hair.
No action is omitted; the sequence is fixed.
3
Understand the completion
After halq or taqsir, the pilgrim becomes halal (exits ihram) for 'umrah.
This completes the 'umrah, and the pilgrim awaits hajj.
4
Relate to previous lessons
The passage notes that details of tawaf, sa'i, and halq have been covered earlier.
Review those sections for full rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصفة التمتع ان يبتدأ من الميقات فيحرم بالعمرة ويدخل مكة فيطوف لها ويسعى ويحلق أو يقصر وقد حل من عمرته
تمتع کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ میقات سے عمرے کا احرام شروع کرے اور مکہ میں داخل ہو۔ پس عمرے کا طواف کرے اور سعی کرے اور حلق یا قصر کرائے اور اپنے عمرے سے حلال ہو جائے۔ اس کی تفصیل گزر چکی ہے۔
The description of tamattu' is that one begins from the miqat, enters ihram for 'umrah, enters Makkah, performs tawaf for it, performs sa'i, and shaves or shortens the hair, and thereby becomes halal from his 'umrah. The method of tamattu' is that he starts ihram for 'umrah from the miqat, enters Makkah, then performs tawaf of 'umrah, performs sa'i, and shaves or shortens, and becomes halal from his 'umrah. Its detail has passed.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage gives the procedure (sifa) of tamattu'. It is a concise description: the pilgrim enters ihram for 'umrah from the miqat (the designated boundary). Upon reaching Makkah, he performs tawaf of 'umrah (circumambulation of the Ka'bah), then sa'i between Safa and Marwah, then shaves his head (halq) or shortens his hair (taqsir). After this, he becomes halal (exits ihram). This completes the 'umrah part. The commentary notes that the full details of these acts have been previously covered in the book. This description is foundational for understanding tamattu'.

Key Terms
صفة التمتع (sifat al-tamattu'): The description or procedure of performing tamattu'.
الميقات (al-mīqāt): The boundary beyond which one cannot pass without ihram for hajj or 'umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Enter ihram for 'umrah from the miqat
C) Perform tawaf
D) Shave the head

Key Takeaway
Tamattu' follows a specific sequence: ihram at miqat, entering Makkah, tawaf, sa'i, and halq/tagsir; any omission of a rukn invalidates the 'umrah.

Cutting Off Talbiyah When Beginning Tawaf
Ruling on when to cease talbiyah for the mutamatti' during 'umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when to cease talbiyah during 'umrah and explain the proof from the hadith of Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
Talbiyah ends when tawaf begins, for the pilgrim has arrived and the summons is fulfilled.

In this lesson, we examine the specific moment when the mutamatti' should stop reciting the talbiyah during 'umrah. The Hanafi school holds that the cessation coincides with the start of tawaf, based on a clear prophetic directive. Understanding this ruling prevents unnecessary continuation of a practice whose purpose has been accomplished.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine which act is being ruled upon (the cutting of talbiyah) and its legal status (sunnah, not wajib).
2
Understand the rationale behind the timing
The reason: talbiyah is a declaration of presence; once you begin tawaf, you have already presented yourself, so repeating the declaration is inappropriate.
3
Locate the proof from Sunnah
The hadith from Ibn Abbas: the Prophet (peace be upon him) said the mutamatti' recites talbiyah until he touches the Black Stone.
4
Analyse the dalalah
The phrase 'until he touches the Black Stone' indicates that the end point is the start of tawaf, which begins with istilam.
The phrase 'until' places a temporal limit.

Source Text

يقطع التلبية اذا ابتدأ بالطواف
اور تلبیہ ختم کر دیگا جب طواف شروع کرے۔ جب عمرے کا طواف شروع کرے تو اب تلبیہ پڑھنا ختم کر دے۔ لبیک کے معنی ہیں میں حاضر ہوں۔ اور وہ حاضر ہو گیا تو اب دوبارہ میں حاضر ہوں کہنا اچھا نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اب تلبیہ پڑھنا چھوڑ دے عن ابن عباس عن النبي و قال يلبى المعتمر حتى يستلم الحجر (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب متى يقطع المعتمر التلبية ص ۲۵۹ نمبر ۱۸۱۷ار ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاءتي يقطع التلبية في العمرة ص ۱۸۵ نمبر ۹۱۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حجر اسود کا بوسہ دے اور طواف شروع کرے تو تلبیہ پڑھنا چھوڑ دے۔
He cuts off the talbiyah when he begins tawaf. And he will stop talbiyah when he starts tawaf. When he begins the tawaf of 'umrah, he should stop reciting talbiyah. The meaning of 'labbaik' is 'I am present'. Since he has become present, it is not good to say 'I am present' again. Therefore, he should leave off talbiyah. From Ibn Abbas from the Prophet: The one performing 'umrah recites talbiyah until he touches the Black Stone (Abu Dawud, chapter on when the mutamatti' cuts talbiyah, p.259, no.1817; Tirmidhi, chapter on cutting talbiyah in 'umrah, p.185, no.919). From this hadith, we learn that when he kisses the Black Stone and begins tawaf, he should stop reciting talbiyah.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on when to cease reciting talbiyah for the mutamatti'. The talbiyah (saying 'labbaik Allahumma labbaik') is recited during ihram. According to the Hanafi school, when the pilgrim begins the tawaf of 'umrah, he should stop talbiyah. The reasoning is that talbiyah signifies presence before Allah; once he reaches the House and begins tawaf, the purpose of announcing presence is fulfilled. The hadith from Ibn Abbas supports this: the Prophet (peace be upon him) said that the one performing 'umrah recites talbiyah until he touches the Black Stone (at the start of tawaf). Thus, the moment of touching or beginning tawaf marks the cessation.

Key Terms
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The invocation recited by a pilgrim in ihram: 'Labbaik Allahumma labbaik...'
يستلم الحجر (yastalam al-hajar): To touch or kiss the Black Stone (al-Hajar al-Aswad) at the start of tawaf.

B) When he begins tawaf
C) When he completes sa'i
D) When he shaves his head

Key Takeaway
The mutamatti' should stop talbiyah at the start of tawaf, as indicated by the Prophet's instruction to recite until touching the Black Stone.

Staying in Makkah in a Halal State
Ruling that the mutamatti' stays in Makkah as halal after 'umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for the mutamatti' after 'umrah and identify the proof from the hadith of Jabir.

Core Idea
After 'umrah, the mutamatti' stays halal until the day of tarwiyah, then enters ihram for hajj.

In tamattu' hajj, the pilgrim performs 'umrah first, then becomes halal. Many assume that the state of ihram continues until hajj, but the sunnah is to remain in a halal state until the day of tarwiyah. This lesson examines the ruling and its prophetic evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
Determine who this ruling applies to (the mutamatti') and what action is prescribed: staying in Makkah as halal after 'umrah.
2
Find the dalil
Locate the primary evidence: the hadith of Jabir ibn Abdullah in Sahih Bukhari.
The hadith is ahad, giving it zanni al-thubut.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Examine the key phrase 'stay as halal' and understand how it indicates the ruling.
The command is explicit but carries the weight of sunnah due to its epistemological level.
4
Determine the time period
Note the temporal limit: 'until the day of tarwiyah' (8th Dhul Hijjah).
5
State the hukm classification
Classify the ruling: it is sunnah, not wajib, because the evidence is zanni.

And he resides in Makkah as halal. And he should stay in Makkah al-Mukarramah as halal. Since they have become halal from 'umrah, they should now stay in Makkah in a halal state. (2) There is a hadith: Jabir ibn Abdullah narrated that he performed hajj with the Messenger of Allah on the day he drove the sacrificial animals, while the people had entered ihram for hajj alone (ifrad). He said to them: 'Exit from your ihram by performing tawaf of the House and sa'i between Safa and Marwah, and shorten your hair, then stay as halal until the day of tarwiyah, then enter ihram for hajj and make what you have come for a tamattu'.' This passage states that after completing 'umrah and becoming halal, the mutamatti' should stay in Makkah in a halal state (not in ihram) until the day of tarwiyah (8th of Dhul Hijjah). The proof is the hadith of Jabir, in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed the Companions to do tamattu': after 'umrah, they were to become halal and remain so until the day of tarwiyah, then enter ihram for hajj. This establishes the sunnah practice for the mutamatti'.

Key Terms
حلال (halāl): The state of being out of ihram, free from its restrictions.
يوم التروية (yawm al-tarwiyah): The 8th of Dhul Hijjah, when pilgrims typically enter ihram for hajj.

Ihram for Hajj on the Day of Tarwiyah and Obligation of Dam
Procedure for entering ihram for hajj and obligation of dam for tamattu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the procedure for a mutamatti' entering ihram for hajj on the day of Tarwiyah and state the obligation of dam according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
On the day of Tarwiyah, the mutamatti' enters ihram for hajj from the Haram and must offer a sacrifice (dam) for tamattu'.

After completing 'umrah, the mutamatti' remains in Makkah in a halal state. On the 8th of Dhul Hijjah (day of Tarwiyah), he enters ihram for hajj from within the Haram, similar to a Makkan resident. He then performs all the rituals of hajj like a mufrid, but additionally owes a sacrifice (dam) because he is performing tamattu'. This lesson covers the ruling, its evidence, and the practical steps.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Determine what the mutamatti' is required to do on the day of Tarwiyah. The passage states: enter ihram for hajj from Masjid al-Haram, perform hajj actions like a mufrid, and offer the dam of tamattu'.
The dam is wajib, not fard.
2
Locate the proof
The passage references the hadith of Ibn Abbas about miqats and the hadith of Jabir about tamattu'. The hadith of Ibn Abbas establishes the miqats for those entering from outside, implying that those already in Makkah enter from the Haram. The hadith of Jabir confirms the tamattu' procedure.
The Quranic verse (2:196) is also a basis.
3
Understand the reasoning
The mutamatti' becomes like a Makkan resident after 'umrah, so he does not need to go to a miqat for hajj; instead he enters ihram from the Haram.
This is a legal analogy (qiyas) to the Makkan.
4
Identify the legal category of dam
The dam for tamattu' is classified as wajib in the Hanafi school. If unable to sacrifice, one must fast ten days (three during hajj, seven after returning).
Obligation level: wajib (not fard) due to zanni evidence.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Some early scholars held the dam to be fard rather than wajib, though the Hanafi position is well-established. The practical consequence is minimal, but it affects the ruling if one misses it intentionally.
This is a legitimate scholarly difference.

فاذا كان يوم التروية احرم بالحج من المسجد الحرام وفعل ما يفعله الحاج المفرد وعليه دم التمتع.
پس جبکہ آٹھویں تاریخ ہو تو ہر حاجی حج کا احرام باندھے اور وہی اعمال کرے جو افراد والے کرتے ہیں۔ اور اس پر دم تمتع لازم ہے. چونکہ یہ مکّی کی طرح ہو گئے اور مکّی حج کا احرام حرم سے باندھتے ہیں اس لئے یہ بھی آٹھویں تاریخ کو حج کا احرام حرم سے باندھیں گے۔ اور مفرد بالحج جو اعمال کرتے ہیں مثلا عرفات جاتے ہیں، مزدلفہ میں ٹھہرتے ہیں، رمی جمار کرتے ہیں اور طواف زیارت کرتے ہیں وہی اعمال یہ آدمی بھی کرے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ بھی مفرد بالحج کی طرح ہو گیا ہے۔ اور چونکہ یہ تمتع ہوا اس لئے اس پر دم تمتع لازم ہوگا۔ مسجد حرام سے یا حرم سے حرام باندھنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابن عباس قال وقت رسول الله الله لاهل المدينة ذا الحليفة ولاهل الشام الجحفة ولاهل نجد قرن المنازل ولاهل اليمن يلملم فهن لهن ولمن اتى عليهن من غير حاشیہ : (الف) آپ سے روایت ہے کہ عمرہ کرنے والا حجر اسود کے چومنے تک تلبیہ پڑھے (ب) حضرت جابر فرماتے ہیں کہ انہوں نے حضور کے ساتھ اس وقت حج کیا جب وہ ہدی لے کر چل رہے تھے۔ لوگوں نے مفرد بالحج کا احرام باندھا۔ آپ نے فرمایا طواف بیت اللہ اور سعی بین الصفا والمروۃ کے بعد حلال ہو جاؤ اور بال کا قصر کرو، پھر حلال ہو کر ٹھہرے رہو ۔ یہاں تک کہ جب آٹھویں تاریک ہو تو حج کا احرام باندھو اور جو پہلے عمرہ کیا اس کو متعہ بناؤ۔
So when the day of tarwiyah comes, he enters ihram for hajj from Masjid al-Haram and does what the mufrid (one performing ifrad) does, and upon him is the dam of tamattu'. So when the eighth day comes, every pilgrim should enter ihram for hajj and perform the same actions as those doing ifrad. And upon him is the sacrifice of tamattu' as obligatory. Since they have become like a Makkan (resident), and the Makkan enters ihram for hajj from the Haram, so they too on the eighth day will enter ihram from the Haram. And the mufrid (one doing ifrad) performs actions such as going to Arafat, staying at Muzdalifah, stoning the jamarat, and performing tawaf al-ziyarah; this person will also do the same actions. Because he has become like a mufrid. And since he is doing tamattu', the sacrifice of tamattu' is obligatory upon him. The proof for entering ihram from the Masjid al-Haram or the Haram is this hadith from Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) designated for the people of Madinah Dhul Hulayfah, for the people of Syria al-Juhfah, for the people of Najd Qarn al-Manazil, and for the people of Yemen Yalamlam. These are for them and for those who come upon them from other places. (Footnote (a): From him, it is narrated that the one performing 'umrah recites talbiyah until he kisses the Black Stone. (b): Jabir said: He performed hajj with the Prophet while he drove the hady. The people had entered ihram for ifrad. The Prophet said: 'After tawaf of the House and sa'i between Safa and Marwah, become halal and shorten your hair, then stay halal until the day of tarwiyah, then enter ihram for hajj and make what you came for a tamattu'.'
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage details the actions of the mutamatti' on the day of tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah). He enters ihram for hajj from Masjid al-Haram (or the Haram area), as he is now like a Makkan resident (since he has been staying halal in Makkah). He then performs all the rituals that a mufrid (one doing ifrad, i.e., hajj alone) does: going to Arafat, staying at Muzdalifah, stoning the jamarat, and performing tawaf al-ziyarah. Additionally, because he is doing tamattu', he must offer a sacrifice (dam). The proof from the hadith of Ibn Abbas establishes the miqat for those entering hajj from outside Makkah, but since the mutamatti' is already in Makkah, he enters ihram from the Haram itself. The footnote references the hadith of Jabir that was quoted earlier, reinforcing the procedure.

Key Terms
دم التمتع (dam al-tamattu'): The sacrificial animal required for tamattu' as a compensation for combining 'umrah and hajj in one journey.
المسجد الحرام (al-Masjid al-Haram): The Sacred Mosque in Makkah; the recommended place to enter ihram for hajj for the mutamatti'.

Ihram for Hajj on the Day of Tarwiyah and the Obligation of Dam al-Tamattu‘
Ruling for Mutamatti‘ to enter ihram from Haram and obligation of dam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on where the Mutamatti‘ enters ihram for Hajj and identify the proof for the obligation of dam al-tamattu‘.

Core Idea
The Mutamatti‘ enters ihram from the Haram, not from his original miqat, and must offer a sacrificial animal.

This lesson examines the third major step of Hajj al-Tamattu‘: on the day of Tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah), the Mutamatti‘ transitions from his halal state after Umrah to the ihram for Hajj. The Hanafi school, relying on the practice of the Companions and the Quran, rules that he enters ihram from within the Haram—unlike the Mufrid—and that he must sacrifice an animal as a requirement of tamattu‘. We will walk through the textual proofs and the underlying legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rulings
The passage states two key rulings: the Mutamatti‘ enters ihram from the Haram (preferably Masjid al-Haram), and he must offer a sacrificial animal (dam al-tamattu‘).
2
Examine the Quranic proof for the dam
The verse (2:196) is cited: 'فَمَنْ تَمَتَّعَ بِالْعُمْرَةِ إِلَى الْحَجِّ فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدْيِ' – the particle 'ف' indicates obligation, and 'مَا اسْتَيْسَرَ' imposes the sacrifice.
The verse also mentions fasting as an alternative.
3
Examine the hadith proofs for ihram location
Two hadith are given: (1) Ibn Abbas reporting the miqat assignment where Makkans start from Makkah; (2) the Companions entering ihram from al-Abtah during the Farewell Pilgrimage.
These show that the Mutamatti‘, being like a Makkan, enters from within the Haram.
4
Understand the analogy (qiyas)
The Mutamatti‘ after Umrah is present in Makkah in a halal state, so he becomes like a resident of Makkah whose miqat is the Haram itself.
This analogy distinguishes him from the Mufrid who enters from outside.
5
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
The Shafi‘i school holds that the Mutamatti‘ must return to his original miqat, based on the Prophet’s practice as a Mufrid. The Hanafi response distinguishes the Prophet’s type (Ifrad) from Tamattu‘.
The thamarah al-khilaf is convenience vs. required travel.

فاذا كان يوم التروية احرم بالحج من المسجد الحرام وفعل ما يفعله الحاج المفرد وعليه دم التمتع. [۷۰۰] (۲) پس جبکہ ساتویں تاریخ ہو تو حج کا احرام باندھے اور وہی اعمال کرے جو حج افراد والے کرتے ہیں۔ اور اس پر دم تمتع ہے۔ چونکہ یہ مکی کی طرح ہو گئے اور مکی حج کا احرام حرم سے باندھتے ہیں اس لئے یہ بھی ساتویں تاریخ کو حج کا احرام حرم سے باندھیں گے۔ اور مفرد بالحج جو اعمال کرتے ہیں مثلا عرفات جاتے ہیں، مزدلفہ میں ٹھہرتے ہیں، رمی جمار کرتے ہیں اور طواف زیارت کرتے ہیں وہی اعمال یہ آدمی بھی کرے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ بھی مفرد بالحج کی طرح ہو گیا ہے۔ اور چونکہ یہ تمتع ہوا اس لئے اس پر دم تمتع لازم ہوگا۔ مسجد حرام سے یا حرم سے احرام باندھنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابن عباس قال وقت رسول الله لاهل المدينة ذا الحليفة ولاهل الشام الجحفة ولاهل نجد قرن المنازل ولاهل اليمن يلملم فهن لهن ولمن اتى عليهن من غير حاشیہ : (الف) آپ سے روایت ہے کہ حضور نے میقات متعین کیا، اہل مدینہ کے لئے ذوالحلیفہ ، اہل شام کے لئے مجہہ ، اہل نجد کے لئے قرن المنازل، اہل یمن کے لیے یامسلم ، پس یہ مقامات ان لوگوں کے لئے اور ان پر جو آئے ، اس کے علاوہ اور جو ان میقات کے اندر ہو تو اس کے لئے میقات اس کے اہل میں سے ہے اور ایسا ہی یہاں تک کہ اہل مکہ احرام باندھے گا مکہ سے (ب) جب ہم عمرہ سے حلال ہوئے تو حضور نے ہمیں حکم دیا کہ ہم احرام باندھ لیں جب ہم منی کی طرف جانے لگے، فرمایا کہ ہم نے مقام اصبح سے احرام باندھا (ب) (مسلم شریف، باب بیان وجوه الاحرام وانه یجوز افراد الحج و استمع و القرآن الخ ص ۳۹۲ نمبر ۱۲۱۴) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ صحابہ کرام نے حجتہ الوداع میں اصبح جو مکہ مکرمہ میں ایک جگہ ہے وہاں سے حج کا احرام باندھا۔ اور متمتع پر دم تمتع ہے اس کی دلیل پہلے گزر چکی ہے تاہم یہ آیت نص ہے فمن تمتع بالعمرة الى الحج فما استيسر من الهدى فمن لم يجد فصيام ثلثة ايام فى الحج و سبعة اذا رجعتم تلك عشرة كاملة ذلك لمن لم يكن اهله حاضری المسجد الحرام (ج) ( آیت ۹۶ اسورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ جس نے تمتع کیا اس پر ہدی لازم ہے اور ہدی نہ دے سکا تو تین روزے حج سے پہلے رکھے اور سات روزے حج سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد رکھے۔
Then when it is the day of Tarwiyah, he enters ihram for Hajj from the Sacred Mosque and does what the single-minded (mufrid) pilgrim does, and upon him is the dam of tamattu‘. [700] (2) So when it is the 7th (correct: 8th – see note) day, he should bind ihram for Hajj and perform the same actions as those who perform Hajj al-Ifrad. And upon him is the dam of tamattu‘. Since they have become like the people of Makkah, and the people of Makkah bind ihram for Hajj from the Haram, they will also bind ihram for Hajj from the Haram on the 7th day. And the mufrid bi’l-Hajj performs actions such as going to Arafat, staying at Muzdalifah, stoning the jamarat, and performing tawaf al-ziyarah; this person will also do those actions because he has become like the mufrid bi’l-Hajj. And because he did tamattu‘, the dam of tamattu‘ becomes obligatory upon him. The proof for binding ihram from the Masjid al-Haram or the Haram is this hadith: from Ibn Abbas who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ appointed for the people of Medina Dhul-Hulayfah, for the people of Syria al-Juhfah, for the people of Najd Qarn al-Manazil, and for the people of Yemen Yalamlam. These (miqats) are for them and for whoever comes upon them from outside... footnote (a): ...and likewise the people of Makkah bind ihram from Makkah. (b) When we became halal from Umrah, the Prophet ﷺ ordered us to bind ihram when we set out for Mina. He said: We bound ihram from al-Abtah. (Muslim, chapter on the manifestations of ihram types... p. 392 no. 1214). From this hadith it is also known that the Companions during the Farewell Pilgrimage bound ihram for Hajj from al-Abtah, a place in Makkah. And the dam of tamattu‘ upon the Mutamatti‘ has its proof earlier, but this verse is conclusive: 'And whosoever enjoys the Umrah unto the Hajj, then what is easy of the sacrificial animal. And whoever does not find (the animal), then a fast of three days during the Hajj and seven when you return home; that is complete ten. That is for him whose family is not present at the Masjid al-Haram.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:196). In this verse it is that whoever performed tamattu‘, a sacrificial animal is obligatory upon him, and if he cannot give it, then fast three days before Hajj and seven days after completing Hajj.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage deals with the third major step of Tamattu‘. On the day of Tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah), the Mutamatti‘ enters ihram for Hajj from within the Haram (preferably from Masjid al-Haram). He then performs all the actions of a mufrid (one performing Hajj al-Ifrad): staying at Arafat, Muzdalifah, stoning, tawaf al-ziyarah, etc. The commentary explains that since the Mutamatti‘ is now like a resident of Makkah, his miqat for Hajj is from the Haram itself. This is supported by two hadiths: one from Ibn Abbas defining miqats (where Makkans start from Makkah), and another from Jabir where the Companions entered ihram from al-Abtah during the Farewell Pilgrimage. Additionally, the Mutamatti‘ must offer a sacrificial animal (dam) as a requirement for combining Umrah and Hajj in a single journey. The proof is the Quranic verse (2:196) which imposes the dam or alternative fasting.

Key Terms
دم التمتع (dam al-tamattu‘): The sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) that the Mutamatti‘ must slaughter as an obligatory act due to combining Umrah and Hajj.
حرم (haram): The sacred precinct of Makkah from which a resident may enter ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
From where does the Mutamatti‘ enter ihram for Hajj according to the Hanafi school?
A) From the miqat he originally used for Umrah
B) From the Haram (e.g., Masjid al-Haram)
C) From a hill outside Makkah
D) It is not specified

Key Takeaway
The Mutamatti‘ enters ihram from the Haram and owes a sacrificial dam.

Fasting as Substitute for the Sacrificial Animal in Tamattu‘
Ruling and details of fasting when lacking a sacrificial animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of fasting as a substitute for dam in tamattu‘, identify the timing and sequence of the fasts, and cite the Quranic proof.

Core Idea
When a Mutamatti‘ cannot sacrifice, wajib fasting of 3+7 days substitutes for the dam.

In the previous chapter on Qiran, the full details of the alternative to sacrificing an animal in tamattu‘ were covered. This passage condenses the key ruling: if the pilgrim cannot find or afford a sacrificial animal, fasting becomes obligatory. The Quranic basis is clear, and the sequence is fixed—three days during Hajj before the day of Nahr, and seven days after returning home. Understanding this substitution is essential because the timing is part of the obligation; flexibility is not permitted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is fasting (siyam) as a substitute for the sacrificial animal (dam) for the Mutamatti‘. Determine its legal level: Hanafi school considers it wajib (obligatory), not merely recommended, because the Quranic command indicates obligation.
The ruling is conditional on not being able to find or afford an animal.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is Quran 2:196, which says: 'فَمَن لَّمْ يَجِدْ فَصِيَامُ ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فِي الْحَجِّ وَسَبْعَةٍ إِذَا رَجَعْتُمْ'. This verse is the primary textual evidence.
The dalil is qat'i in transmission (Quran) but zanni in dalalah regarding the exact obligation level.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative noun 'فَصِيَامُ' (then a fast) is interpreted as a command. In Hanafi usul, the imperative form (amr) indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is a qarinah to the contrary. No such qarinah exists here; thus the fast is wajib.
The verse also specifies timing: 'in al-Hajj' (during Hajj) and 'when you return'.
4
Apply the ruling: timing and sequence
The three days must be observed during the Hajj period, before the day of Nahr (10th Dhul-Hijjah). The seven days are observed after returning home (after completing Hajj and reaching one's homeland). This order is fixed.
It is not permissible to fast the seven before the three, or to fast all ten consecutively during Hajj.
5
Reference the fuller treatment
The passage notes that 'its full detail and proof has passed in the chapter on Qiran'. This indicates that detailed conditions, exceptions, and intra-school disputes are covered elsewhere. For this lesson, the core ruling suffices.
For further study, consult the chapter on Qiran in classical Hanafi texts like Al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان لم يجد ما يذبح صام ثلثة ايام في الحج وسبعة اذا رجع الى اهله [۷] (۷) پس اگر نہ پائے ایسا جانور جو ذبح کر سکے تو تین دن روزے رکھے حج میں اور سات دن جب النے گھر لوٹے ۔ اس کی پوری تفصیل اور دلیل باب القران میں گزر چکی ہے۔
And if he does not find (an animal) to slaughter, he fasts three days during the Hajj and seven when he returns to his family. [7] (7) So if he does not find an animal that he can slaughter, then he fasts three days during the Hajj and seven days when he returns to his home. Its full detail and proof has passed in the chapter on Qiran.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage provides the alternative for the Mutamatti‘ who cannot afford a sacrificial animal (dam). The Quranic verse (2:196) prescribes fasting: three days during the Hajj (before the day of sacrifice) and seven days after returning home. The commentary notes that the complete discussion and proofs were given earlier in the chapter on Qiran. Thus, the fast is a substitute, and its sequence is fixed: 3+7=10 days total.

Key Terms
صيام (siyam): Fasting as a substitute for sacrificial animal in tamattu‘.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
When a Mutamatti‘ cannot sacrifice, wajib fasting of 3+7 days in fixed order substitutes for the dam based on Quran 2:196.

Driving a Hadi for Mutamatti‘ – A Recommended Practice
Ruling on driving a hadi for the Mutamatti‘ with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on driving a hadi for a Mutamatti‘ and identify the evidence from the Sunnah that establishes it as mustahab.

Core Idea
Driving a sacrificial animal for tamattu‘ is mustahab, not wājib — following the Prophet’s example.

When performing Hajj al-Tamattu‘, a pilgrim has the option to bring a sacrificial animal (hadi) from home. This lesson examines the ruling on this practice: is it obligatory or simply recommended? We will look at the evidence from the Prophet ﷺ and clarify the Hanafi position that it is a commendable act but not a requirement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is a Mutamatti‘ driving a hadi from home. What is the hukm level in the Hanafi school?
The passage states it is 'afdal' (better), which in Hanafi terminology corresponds to mustahab.
2
Locate the dalil
What evidence is cited? The hadith from Ibn Umar in Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim describing the Prophet’s action during the Farewell Pilgrimage.
The Prophet ﷺ performed tamattu‘ and drove a hadi from Dhul-Hulayfah.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
How does this hadith prove the ruling? The Prophet’s action is an example. The verb 'ساق' (drove) indicates he physically brought it, and this is understood as a recommended practice, not a command implying obligation.
In Hanafi usul, a prophetic action (fi‘l) indicates recommendation unless there is evidence of obligation.
4
Note the practical implication
What is the consequence? The Mutamatti‘ may bring a hadi or not. If he does not, the dam (sacrificial animal) for tamattu‘ is still wājib, but he misses the reward of emulating the Prophet.
Some mistakenly think driving the hadi is itself wājib; this lesson clarifies it is not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان اراد المتمتع ان يسوق الهدى احرم وساق هديه [۷۰۲] (۸) اگر تمتع کرنے والا ہدی ہانکنے کا ارادہ کرے تو اپنے ساتھ ہدی لے جائے۔ پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ تمتع کرنے والے کے لئے افضل یہ ہے کہ گھر سے ساتھ ہدی لے جائے۔ اس لئے اگر ہدی ساتھ لے جائے تو یہ بہتر ہے۔ حضور حجتہ الوداع میں ہدی ساتھ لیکر تشریف لے گئے تھے۔ ان ابن عمر قال تمتع رسول الله في حجة الوداع بالعمرة الى الحج واهدى فساق معه الهدى من ذي الحليفة وبدا رسول الله الا الله فاهل بالعمرة ثم اهل بالحج فتمتع الناس مع النبي الا الله بالعمرة الى الحج (و) ( بخاری شریف، باب من ساق البدن معهد ص ۲۲۹ نمبر ۲۹ ارمسلم شریف ، باب وجوب الدم علی حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عبداللہ بن عمر فرماتے ہیں کہ حضور حجتہ الوداع میں عمرہ کو حج کے ساتھ مل کر تمتع کیا۔ اور ہدی ذوالحلیفہ سے ساتھ لے گئے ۔ اور حضور نے شروع کیا پس عمرے کا احرام (باقی اگلے صفحہ پر )
And if the Mutamatti‘ intends to drive a sacrificial animal, he enters ihram and drives his sacrificial animal. [702] (8) If the one performing tamattu‘ intends to drive a hadi, he takes a hadi with him. It has passed before that for the Mutamatti‘ it is better to take a hadi from home. Therefore, if he takes a hadi with him, it is better. The Prophet ﷺ during the Farewell Pilgrimage took a hadi with him. Ibn Umar said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ performed tamattu‘ during the Farewell Pilgrimage with Umrah to Hajj, and he offered a sacrificial animal and drove it from Dhul-Hulayfah. And he began... (the text cuts off).
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage states that the Mutamatti‘ may choose to drive a sacrificial animal (hadi) along with him from the start of his journey. It is considered preferable (afdal) to bring a hadi from home, following the example of the Prophet ﷺ during the Farewell Pilgrimage. The hadith from Ibn Umar confirms that the Prophet ﷺ performed tamattu‘ and brought a hadi from Dhul-Hulayfah. This is a recommended practice (mustahab) but not obligatory.

Key Terms
هدي (hadi): A sacrificial animal (sheep, goat, cow, or camel) driven to the Haram by a pilgrim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Driving a hadi for tamattu‘ is a recommended act (mustahab) based on the Prophet’s practice, not an obligation.

Fasting as Substitute for Sacrifice in Tamattu'
Ruling on fasting three days during Hajj and seven after returning for a mutamatti' without a sacrifice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fasting for a mutamatti' who cannot afford a sacrifice, explain the Quranic proof (2:196), and identify the sequence of fasting (three days during Hajj, seven after returning).

Core Idea
If a mutamatti' cannot afford a sacrifice, he must fast three days during Hajj and seven after returning, per Quran 2:196.

In this passage, the author presents the ruling for the mutamatti' pilgrim who cannot find a sacrificial animal. The ruling is based on a clear Quranic command. We will examine the textual evidence and the legal reasoning behind the obligation to fast in lieu of the sacrifice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and condition
The act is fasting; the condition is that the mutamatti' does not find a sacrifice (hady). The ruling applies when he cannot afford or obtain an animal.
The condition is clear: 'if he does not find an animal to slaughter'.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that fasting is wajib (obligatory) as a substitute for the sacrifice. It is not optional.
The Hanafi school considers this wajib, not fard, because the dalil is zanni in dalalah (though thubut is qat'i).
3
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is Quran 2:196, which commands fasting for those who cannot find a sacrifice.
The verse is explicitly quoted in the text.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative form 'فصيام' (then fast) after the negative condition 'فمن لم يجد' indicates obligation in Hanafi usul. Al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
The command is clear and unrestricted.
5
Note the sequence and total
The fasting is split: three days during the Hajj period (before the day of Nahr) and seven days after returning home, totaling ten days.
The verse explicitly states the total of ten days.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
[۷] (۷) فان لم يجد ما يذبح صام ثلثة ايام في الحج وسبعة اذا رجع الى اهله
اهلهن لمن كان يريد الحج والعمرة فمن كان دونهن فمهله من اهله و كذلك حتى اهل مكة يهلون منها (الف) (بخاری شریف، باب محل اهل الشام ص ۲۰۶ نمبر ۱۵۲۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ اہل مکہ مکہ سے احرام باندھیں گے اور متمتع احرام کھولنے کے بعد مکی کی طرح ہو گئے اس لئے وہ بھی مکہ سے احرام باندھیں گے (۲) مسلم شریف میں ہے عن جابر بن عبد الله قال امرنا النبي لما احللنا ان نحرم اذا توجهنا الى منى قال فاهللنا من الابطح (ب) (مسلم شریف، باب بیان وجوه الاحرام وانه یجوز افراد الحج و استمع و القرآن الخ ص ۳۹۲ نمبر ۱۲۱۴) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ صحابہ کرام نے حجتہ الوداع میں اصبح جو مکہ مکرمہ میں ایک جگہ ہے وہاں سے حج کا احرام باندھا۔ اور متمتع پر دم تمتع ہے اس کی دلیل پہلے گزر چکی ہے تاہم یہ آیت نص ہے فمن تمتع بالعمرة الى الحج فما استيسر من الهدى فمن لم يجد فصيام ثلثة ايام فى الحج و سبعة اذا رجعتم تلك عشرة كاملة ذلك لمن لم يكن اهله حاضری المسجد الحرام (ج) ( آیت ۹۶ اسورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ جس نے تمتع کیا اس پر ہدی لازم ہے اور ہدی نہ دے سکا تو تین روزے حج سے پہلے رکھے اور سات روزے حج سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد رکھے۔
[۷] (۷) پس اگر نہ پائے ایسا جانور جو ذبح کر سکے تو تین دن روزے رکھے حج میں اور سات دن جب النے گھر لوٹے ۔ اس کی پوری تفصیل اور دلیل باب القران میں گزر چکی ہے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت ابن عباس سے روایت ہے کہ حضور نے میقات متعین کیا، اہل مدینہ کے لئے ذوالحلیفہ ، اہل شام کے لئے مجھہ ، اہل نجد کے لئے قرن المنازل، اہل یمن کے لیے یامسلم ، پس یہ مقامات ان لوگوں کے لئے اور ان پر جو آئے ، اس کے علاوہ اور جو ان میقات کے اندر ہو تو اس کے لئے میقات اس کے اہل میں سے ہے اور ایسا ہی یہاں تک کہ اہل مکہ احرام باندھے گا مکہ سے (ب) جب ہم عمرہ سے حلال ہوئے تو حضور نے ہمیں حکم دیا کہ ہم احرام باندھ لیں جب ہم منی کی طرف جانے لگے، فرمایا کہ ہم نے مقام اصبح سے احرام باندھا (ج) جس نے عمرہ کو حج کے ساتھ ملا کر تمتع کیا تو جو آسان ہدی میں سے، پس جو ہدی نہ پائے تو وہ تین دن روزے رکھے حج میں اور سات دن جب تم واپس لوٹو ۔ یہ دس دن ہوئے ۔ یہ تمتع اس کے لئے ہے جو مسجد حرام کے پاس نہ ہو
Chapter of Hajj. [7] (7) So if he does not find an animal to slaughter, he fasts three days during Hajj and seven when he returns to his family. 'Their families for whoever intends Hajj and Umrah, and whoever is beyond them, his miqat is from his family, and likewise until the people of Makkah enter ihram from Makkah.' (a) (Bukhari, chapter of the miqat of the people of Syria, p. 206, no. 1526) From this hadith it is understood that the people of Makkah will enter ihram from Makkah, and the mutamatti' after removing his ihram becomes like a Makkan, so he too will enter ihram from Makkah. (2) In Sahih Muslim it is narrated from Jabir ibn Abdullah: The Prophet commanded us when we became halal to enter ihram when we set out towards Mina. He said: So we entered ihram from al-Abtah. (b) (Muslim, chapter on the types of ihram, p. 392, no. 1214) From this hadith it is also understood that the Companions in the Farewell Hajj entered ihram for Hajj from al-Asbah, a place in Makkah. And the mutamatti' owes a dam (sacrifice) for tamattu', its evidence has passed before, however this verse is a clear text: 'Then whoever performs Umrah within the Hajj, then offer whatever sacrifice is easy. And whoever cannot find [a sacrifice], then fast three days during Hajj and seven when you return – that is ten days complete. That is for those whose family is not present at al-Masjid al-Haram.' (j) (Verse 196 of Surah al-Baqarah) In this verse, whoever performs tamattu' is required to offer a sacrifice, and if he cannot offer a sacrifice, then he fasts three days before Hajj and seven days after finishing Hajj. [7] (7) So if he does not find an animal to slaughter, he fasts three days during Hajj and seven days when he returns to his home. Its full detail and evidence have passed in the chapter of Qiran. Footnote: (a) From Ibn Abbas: The Prophet fixed the miqats: for the people of Madinah Dhul-Hulayfah, for Syria Juhfah, for Najd Qarn al-Manazil, for Yemen Yalamlam. So these are for those people and for those who come from elsewhere, and for those within these miqats, their miqat is from their homes, and likewise until the people of Makkah enter ihram from Makkah. (b) When we became halal from Umrah, the Prophet commanded us to enter ihram when we started towards Mina; he said we entered ihram from al-Abtah. (j) Whoever combines Umrah with Hajj in tamattu', then whatever sacrifice is easy; then if he cannot find a sacrifice, he fasts three days during Hajj and seven when you return – that is ten days. This tamattu' is for those whose family is not near the Masjid al-Haram.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage from Al Sharh Ul Sameri presents the ruling for a mutamatti' (one who performs Umrah first and then Hajj in the same journey) who cannot afford a sacrificial animal (hady). The matn states: if he does not find an animal to slaughter, he fasts three days during the Hajj period and seven days after returning home. The sharh expands by citing a hadith about miqat, establishing that a mutamatti' after becoming halal from Umrah is like a resident of Makkah for the purpose of assuming ihram for Hajj. Then it quotes Quranic verse 2:196 as the primary textual proof, which explicitly commands fasting for those who cannot find a sacrifice. The commentary also mentions that the complete detail and evidence for this ruling are given in the chapter on Qiran. The footnotes provide the exact wording of the relevant hadith and the verse, confirming the obligation.

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu'): A type of Hajj where one first performs Umrah during the Hajj season, then becomes halal, and then performs Hajj in the same year.
هدي (hady): A sacrificial animal (camel, cow, goat) offered in the Haram during Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the total number of fasting days for a mutamatti' who cannot afford a sacrifice?
A) 3
B) 7
C) 10
D) 14

Key Takeaway
A mutamatti' who cannot afford a sacrifice must fast three days during Hajj and seven after returning, per Quran 2:196.
