Ruling on a Mutamatti' Driving Hady
Ruling with prophetic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a mutamatti' driving hady and explain the evidence from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Core Idea
Driving a sacrificial animal (hady) is a confirmed sunnah for the mutamatti'—a recommended act of devotion, not an obligation.

This passage addresses a recommended practice during Hajj tamattu': the pilgrim driving a sacrificial animal (hady) with him on his journey. The Hanafi school classifies it as a sunnah muakkadah, based on the explicit action of the Prophet in the Farewell Hajj. Understanding the difference between recommended (sunnah) and obligatory (wajib) is essential for proper fiqh application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'sawq al-hady' (driving the hady) for a mutamatti'. Ruling: sunnah muakkadah (confirmed recommended).
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof is a hadith from Ibn Umar (ra) recording the Prophet's action in the Farewell Hajj: he performed tamattu' and drove the hady from Dhul-Hulayfah.
The hadith is reported by Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Understand the evidence (wajh al-dalalah)
The Prophet's action indicates desirability. In Hanafi usul, an action of the Prophet that is not expressly commanded is taken as sunnah muakkadah if done consistently.
4
Note the Hanafi categorization
The Hanafi school classifies it as sunnah muakkadah—not wajib, but highly recommended. The commentary uses 'afdal' (preferable).
This is the mufta bihi position.
5
Distinguish from obligation
If it were wajib, omitting it would require compensation (dam). For sunnah muakkadah, omission is disliked but no penalty.
Common mistake: assuming the Prophet's action makes it obligatory.

Source Text

Footnote: (d) Abdullah ibn Umar said that the Prophet performed tamattu' in the Farewell Hajj, combining Umrah with Hajj, and he brought the hady from Dhul-Hulayfah. He began with the ihram of Umrah... (continued on next page).
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage from Al Sharh Ul Sameri addresses the recommendation for a mutamatti' to drive a sacrificial animal (hady) with him. The matn states: if the mutamatti' intends to drive the hady, he should enter ihram and drive it. The commentary explains that it is preferable (afdal) for him to bring the hady from home, as this is better. It then provides evidence from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) during the Farewell Hajj, as narrated by Ibn Umar: the Prophet performed tamattu' and drove the hady from Dhul-Hulayfah. The footnote gives the exact wording of the hadith. This shows that driving the hady is not obligatory but a recommended act that the Prophet himself did, thus establishing its desirability.

Key Terms
سوق الهدى (sawq al-hady): Driving the sacrificial animal from one's place to the Haram, often by leading it or having it accompany one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah).
C) It is disliked (makruh).
D) It is prohibited (haram).

Key Takeaway
Driving hady in Hajj tamattu' is a confirmed sunnah muakkadah, established by the Prophet's practice, and is not obligatory.

Ish'ar: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Marking the Sacrificial Camel
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether ish'ar is sunnah or not.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi disagreement on ish'ar and identify the evidence for each position.

Core Idea
Ish'ar is not obligatory but a sunnah according to the Sahibayn; Abu Hanifa permitted it but considered it unnecessary.

This passage examines a difference within the Hanafi school itself: whether one should mark the sacrificial camel by cutting its hump (ish'ar). The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it a sunnah based on prophetic practice, while Abu Hanifa argues it is not required because the garland (taqlid) suffices and it causes pain. The later Hanafi school generally follows the Sahibayn's view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
Recognize that ish'ar is a practice done to a camel brought as a sacrificial offering (hady) to the Kaaba. It involves cutting the right side of the hump to let blood flow, as a visible mark.
The act is specific to camels, not other animals.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn), ish'ar is a sunnah (recommended). According to Abu Hanifa, it is not necessary; the taqlid (garland) alone suffices.
Both positions are within the Hanafi school.
3
Examine the evidence for the Sahibayn
They cite the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet both garlanded and marked his hady, and the practice of Ibn Umar who stabbed the hump at Dhul-Hulayfah.
These are considered strong dalil, especially the hadith.
4
Examine Abu Hanifa's evidence
Abu Hanifa relies on the statement of Ibn Abbas that one may choose to mark or not. He also argues that ish'ar causes unnecessary pain and that the purpose of marking is achieved by taqlid.
Abu Hanifa did not deny ish'ar absolutely; he rejected excessive practice.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and preferred view
The practical difference: if one omits ish'ar, the hady is still valid and no compensation is due. The later Hanafi school (mufta bihi) considers ish'ar sunnah, following the Sahibayn.
This is an example of legitimate ikhtilaf within a single madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۷۰۳](۹) فان كانت بدنة قلدها بمزادة او نعل واشعر البدنة عند ابي يوسف و محمد رحمهما الله تعالى وهو ان يشق سنامها من الجانب الايمن ولا يشعر عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى
[۷۰۳] (۹) پس اگر اونٹ ہو تو اس کو پرانے چڑے یا جوتے کا ہار پہنائیں گے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اونٹ کو شعار کریں گے۔ اور وہ یہ ہے کہ اونٹ کی کوہان کو دائیں جانب سے پھاڑ دے۔ اور امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک شعار نہیں ہے۔
ہدی لے چلے تو اس پر ہدی کی علامت لگائے ، اونٹ کے لئے ہدی کی علامت دو ہیں۔ کو ہان کو پھاڑ کر اس کے خون کو کو ہان پر مل دینا (۲) پرانا چھڑایا جو تا گردن میں لٹکا دینا تا کہ لوگ دیکھ کر اس کا احترام کریں اور چور ڈاکو ہدی کو نہ چھیڑیں۔ حضور نے ہدی کے لئے دونوں کام کئے ہیں۔ عن عائشة قالت قتلت قلائد هدى النبى الله ثم اشعرها وقلدها او قلدتها ثم بعث بها الى البيت (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب اشعار البدن ص ۲۳۰ نمبر ۱۹۹۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ اونٹ کی گردن میں قلادہ ڈالنا بھی سنت ہے اور شعار کرنا بھی (۲) كان ابن عمر اذا اهدى زمن الحديبة قلده و اشعره بذي الحليفة يطعن في شق سنامه الايمن بالشفرة ووجهها قبل القبلة باركة (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب من اشعر و قلد بذی الحلیفة ثم احرم ص ۲۲۹ نمبر ۱۹۹۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اونٹ کی دائیں کو ہان میں چھری مار کر خون نکالے۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک یہی سنت ہے۔ کیونکہ حدیث سے ثابت ہے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزد یک اشعار ضروری نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس میں تعذیب حیوان ہے اور قلادہ ڈالنے کا طریقہ بھی ہے اس لئے اشعار کرنا ضروری نہیں۔ ان کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے عن ابن عباس قال ان شئت فاشعر الهدى وان شئت فلا تشعر (ج ) ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۷۵ فی الاشعار واجب ھوام لاج ثالث ، ص۱۷۲، نمبر ۱۳۲۰۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اشعار ضروری نہیں ہے۔ وت امام صاحب کے اہل علاقہ بہت گہرائی کے ساتھ اشعار کرتے تھے جس سے حیوان کو زیادہ تکلیف ہوتی تھی اس لئے اپنے اہل زمانہ کے اشعار کا انکار کیا ہے۔ اصل اشعار کا انکار نہیں ہے۔
ات مزادة : پرانا چھڑا۔ اشعر : چھری مار کر کو ہان پھاڑنا۔
[703] (9) So if it is a camel, he gives it a garland of a worn-out water-skin or sandal, and the camel is marked (ish'ar) according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) – that is, he splits its hump from the right side – and it is not marked according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him). [703] (9) So if it is a camel, he puts a garland of an old skin or sandal, and according to the two companions, they make ish'ar on the camel, which is to split the camel's hump from the right side. And according to Imam Abu Hanifa, ish'ar is not done. When driving the hady, he places a sign on it. There are two signs for the camel: (1) splitting the hump and rubbing the blood on the hump, (2) hanging an old sandal on the neck so that people see it and respect it, and thieves and robbers do not touch the hady. The Prophet (peace be upon him) did both for his hady. Aisha said: I used to twist the garlands for the hady of the Prophet, then he would mark it and garland it (or she garlanded it), then send it to the House. (Bukhari, chapter on ish'ar of the budn, p. 230, no. 1999) From this hadith it is understood that putting a garland around the camel's neck is sunnah, and making ish'ar is also sunnah. (2) When Ibn Umar would send a hady during the treaty of Hudaybiyyah, he would garland it and mark it at Dhul-Hulayfah, stabbing the right side of its hump with a blade, facing it toward the qibla while it was sitting. (Bukhari, chapter on those who mark and garland at Dhul-Hulayfah then enter ihram, p. 229, no. 1995) From this effect it is understood that he struck the right hump with a knife and drew blood. According to the two companions, this is sunnah because it is established by hadith. And according to Imam Abu Hanifa, ish'ar is not necessary because it involves causing pain to the animal, and there is also the method of garlanding, so ish'ar is not required. Their evidence is this effect from Ibn Abbas who said: If you wish, mark the hady, and if you wish, do not mark it. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, vol. 7, chapter on ish'ar being wajib or not, p. 172, no. 13209) From this effect it is understood that ish'ar is not necessary. And Imam Abu Hanifa's people in his region used to perform ish'ar very deeply, causing great pain to the animal, so he denied their practice. He did not deny the original ish'ar. (Glossary: at-mizada: old skin; ish'ar: splitting the hump with a knife.)
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage addresses the issue of marking the sacrificial camel (ish'ar) – a practice of cutting the hump to let blood flow as a sign. The matn states that according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions), ish'ar is required, while Abu Hanifa says it is not. The commentary explains that there are two signs for the camel: the garland (taqlid) and the ish'ar. It then presents evidence: the hadith of Aisha shows the Prophet did both; the athar of Ibn Umar shows stabbing the right hump. The Sahibayn consider this sunnah. Abu Hanifa argues ish'ar is not necessary because it causes pain, and the garland suffices; his evidence is the statement of Ibn Abbas that one may or may not do it. The commentator adds that Abu Hanifa actually rejected the excessive practice of his time, not the original ish'ar itself. Thus, the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that ish'ar is not wajib, but it is a sunnah according to the Sahibayn.

Key Terms
اشعار (ish'ar): Marking the sacrificial camel by cutting the hump to cause blood to flow, as a sign it is for sacrifice.
تقليد (taqlid): Garlanding the neck of the sacrificial animal with a leather sandal or worn-out skin to mark it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on ish'ar (marking the camel by splitting the hump) according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn)?
A) It is wajib (obligatory).
B) It is sunnah (recommended).
C) It is makruh (disliked).
D) It is haram (prohibited).

Key Takeaway
Ish'ar is a recommended sunnah according to the Sahibayn and later Hanafi practice, but not obligatory; the garland alone suffices.

Ruling on a Mutamatti' with Hady: Staying in Ihram until Hajj
Ruling on tawaf, sa'y, and staying in ihram for a mutamatti' with hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a mutamatti' who has driven a hady upon entering Makkah, and explain why he remains in ihram based on the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
A mutamatti' with hady does not become halal after Umrah but remains in ihram until Hajj.

In this lesson, we examine the specific ruling for a mutamatti' who has brought a sacrificial animal (hady). The Hanafi school holds that such a person, upon completing Umrah, does not exit ihram. Instead, he stays in the state of consecration until the 8th of Dhul-Hijjah when he assumes ihram for Hajj. This is based on the practice of the Prophet in his Farewell Hajj. Let us walk through the analytical steps to understand the rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the mutamatti' entering Makkah with hady after performing Umrah. The ruling is that he does not become halal; he must remain in ihram until he assumes ihram for Hajj on the 8th of Dhul-Hijjah.
This is the operative position for fatwa.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the Prophet's action in the Farewell Hajj where he performed tamattu' and brought a hady, and he did not become halal after Umrah. The text references hadith no. 1227.
The dalil is a sunnah fi'liyyah (action) of the Prophet.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action of not becoming halal because he had a hady indicates the ruling. For a mutamatti' with hady, staying in ihram is established by following the Prophet's example.
The hady is the distinguishing factor that changes the ruling.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The text notes that this is mukhtalaf fih (disputed). Some other schools may hold that the mutamatti' becomes halal regardless of hady. The Hanafi school firmly takes the position of remaining in ihram.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both sides have evidence.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that the mutamatti' with hady does not become halal. The authority is the Prophet's practice and the zahir al-riwayah texts.
No intra-Hanafi conflict is mentioned; the position is unanimous.

Commentary
This final lesson in the window addresses the actions of a mutamatti' who has driven a hady: upon entering Makkah, he performs tawaf (circumambulation) and sa'y (walking between Safa and Marwah) for his Umrah, but he does not remove his ihram (become halal) until he assumes ihram for Hajj on the 8th of Dhul-Hijjah. The commentary explains that because he has a hady with him, he continues the prohibitions of ihram: he does not shave his head, does not wear sewn clothes, and does not apply perfume. This is unlike a mutamatti' without hady who would become halal after Umrah. The footnotes provide additional hadith evidence about the Prophet's practice of combining Umrah and Hajj, and the marking of the hady. The ruling establishes that bringing a hady changes the rules for the mutamatti', making him like a qarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together) in terms of remaining in ihram.

Key Terms
تحلل (tahallul): To come out of the state of ihram by shaving or trimming hair, removing restrictions.
متمتع (mutamatti'): One who performs tamattu', i.e., performs Umrah during the Hajj season and then performs Hajj in the same journey, becoming halal in between if no hady is brought.
هدي (hady): A sacrificial animal brought by a pilgrim performing tamattu' or qiran, to be slaughtered on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul-Hijjah).

Mutamatti' with Hadi: No Tahlul After Umrah
Ruling on tawaf and sa'i without tahlul for mutamatti' with hadi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a mutamatti' with hadi regarding tahlul and explain the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
A mutamatti' with hadi remains in ihram — no tahlul until after Hajj.

This lesson addresses a specific rule for tamattu' in hajj. When a mutamatti' brings a sacrificial animal (hadi), the usual pattern changes: he does not become halal after Umrah. Instead, he stays in ihram until he assumes ihram for Hajj on the 8th of Dhul Hijja. This is based on the Prophet's action in Hajjat al-Wida' and supported by hadith from Aisha and Ibn Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The mutamatti' enters Makkah, performs tawaf and sa'i, but does not perform tahlul. He remains in ihram.
2
Locate the dalil
The Prophet himself did this. Also hadith from Aisha about the Prophet's hadi, and Ibn Umar sending hadi.
The dalil is the practice of the Prophet (sunnah fi'liyyah).
3
Understand the reason
Bringing the hadi prevents tahlul; it is a sign that the mutamatti' will combine Umrah and Hajj without break.
4
Note cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Other schools may allow tahlul, but Hanafis require remaining in ihram.
The dispute is over the interpretation of the Prophet's action.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that the mutamatti' with hadi does not perform tahlul until after completing Hajj.

This passage addresses the mutamatti' who has brought a hadi (sacrificial animal). Upon entering Makkah, he performs tawaf al-qudum and sa'i for Umrah, but he does not remove his ihram (tahlul). تحلل (tahlul): Removal of ihram and becoming permissible to previously forbidden things.
هدي (hadi): A sacrificial animal brought by the pilgrim, often required for certain types of Hajj like tamattu'.

Halq on Yawm al-Nahr Releases Both Ihrams
Ruling that halq on the 10th ends both ihrams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that halq on Yawm al-Nahr removes both Umrah and Hajj ihrams for a qarin or mutamatti' with hadi, and identify the hadith evidence from Sahih al-Bukhari.

Core Idea
On the 10th of Dhul Hijja, shaving ends both Umrah and Hajj restrictions at once.

This passage clarifies a key moment in Hajj for those combining Umrah and Hajj without a break (qiran or tamattu' with hadi). Because they remain in ihram from the start, the first permissible act that removes all restrictions is shaving the head on the Day of Sacrifice. The ruling is supported by a hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its timing
The act is shaving the head (halq) and it must be performed on Yawm al-Nahr (10th of Dhul Hijja).
This is the day of sacrifice, not any other day.
2
Recognize the two ihrams involved
The person is in ihram for both Umrah and Hajj simultaneously because they performed qiran or tamattu' with hadi and never exited the first ihram.
This dual state is the reason both are removed.
3
Understand the condition for the ruling
The ruling applies only to those who did not become halal from the first ihram before starting Hajj. They remain in ihram throughout.
If they had exited Umrah ihram, they would be mutamatti' without hadi and would not get this ruling.
4
Locate the hadith evidence
The passage cites a hadith from Bukhari: the Prophet (peace be upon him) said that the pilgrim does not become halal until he completes his Hajj and sacrifices on the Day of Sacrifice.
The hadith is narrated by multiple Companions and is authentic.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
A qarin on the 10th performs stoning, sacrifice, and shaves. At that moment, he becomes halal from everything forbidden in ihram for both Umrah and Hajj.
Shaving is the culminating act that signals completion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۷۰۶] (۱۲) فاذا حلق يوم النحر فقد حل من الاحرامين 
پس جب دسویں ذی الحجہ کو حلق کرائے تو دونوں احراموں سے حلال ہو جائے گا۔
ان چونکہ عمرے کا احرام نہیں کھولا تھا اور حج کا احرام باندھ لیا تھا اس لئے دسویں تاریخ کو دونوں احراموں سے حلال ہوگا۔ اس کی دلیل مسئلہ نمبرہ میں گزرگئی ہے۔ ثم لم يحلل من شيء حرم منه حتى يقضى حجه نحر هدية يوم النحر (بخارى شریف نمبر (۱۶۹)
When he shaves his head on the Day of Sacrifice, he becomes halal from both ihrams. So when he shaves on the 10th of Dhul Hijja, he becomes halal from both ihrams. Because since he did not remove the ihram of Umrah and had assumed the ihram of Hajj, on the 10th he becomes halal from both. The evidence for this passed in the numbered issue. Then he does not become halal from anything forbidden until he completes his Hajj and sacrifices his hadi on the Day of Sacrifice. (Bukhari no. 169)
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This ruling states that for a person who performed qiran or tamattu' with hadi (since he did not remove the first ihram), on the 10th of Dhul Hijja (yawm al-nahr), after shaving his head (halq), he becomes halal from both the ihram of Umrah and Hajj simultaneously. This is because he remained in the state of ihram throughout. The commentary references the hadith that the Prophet said, 'Then he does not become halal from anything forbidden until he completes his Hajj and sacrifices his hadi on the Day of Sacrifice.' This is the evidence for this ruling.

Key Terms
حلق (halq): Shaving the head completely, which is one of the rites of Hajj that removes the state of ihram.
قران (qiran): Combining Umrah and Hajj with a single ihram intention, without separating them.
تمتع (tamattu'): Performing Umrah first, then exiting ihram, and later assuming ihram for Hajj in the same year.

Key Takeaway

Tamattu' and Qiran Invalid for Makkans
Ruling that tamattu' and qiran are invalid for residents of Makkah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tamattu' and qiran for residents of Makkah and explain the dalil from Surah Al-Baqarah 2:196.

Core Idea
Tamattu' and qiran are only for those whose families are not present at the Sacred Mosque.

In this lesson, we explore a key distinction in Hajj rites. While tamattu' and qiran are often recommended for pilgrims, the Hanafi school holds that they are not valid for residents of Makkah and those within the miqat boundaries. We will examine the Quranic proof and the reasoning behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the main ruling: tamattu' and qiran are not valid for the people of Makkah; they must perform ifrad.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the Quranic verse (2:196) and the specific phrase 'dhalika liman lam yakun ahluhu hadiri al-masjidi al-haram'.
3
Explain the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the phrase restricts tamattu' to those whose families are not present at the Sacred Mosque, i.e., non-residents.
4
Understand the rationale
The concession of combining Hajj and Umrah in one journey is for those who travel; residents do not benefit from this concession.
5
Apply to a scenario
Consider a person living in Jeddah (within miqat): they must perform ifrad, not tamattu' or qiran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۷۰۷] (۱۳) وليس لاهل مكة تمتع ولا قرآن 
اہل مکہ کے لئے نہ تمتع ہے اور نہ قرآن ہے صرف ان کے لئے حج افراد ہے۔
(۱) آیت میں ہے ذلك لمن لم يكن اهله حاضری المسجد الحرام (ب) ( آیت ۹۶ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں ذلک کا اشارہ تمتع اور اس کے تحت میں قرآن ہے۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ تمتع اور قرآن اس کے لئے ہے جو مسجد حرام کے قریب نہ ہو یعنی لکھی نہ ہو۔ اس لئے حنفیہ کے نزدیک مکی اور میقات کے اندر والوں کے لئے تمتع اور قران نہیں ہے (۲) ایک سفر میں حج اور عمرہ کر کے فائدہ اٹھانے کو تجمع کرنا کہتے ہیں۔ لیکن سفر ہی نہ ہو تو فائدہ اٹھانا کیا ہوگا۔ اس لئے اہل مکہ کے لئے تمتع اور قرآن نہیں ہے۔
There is no tamattu' and no qiran for the people of Makkah. For the people of Makkah, there is neither tamattu' nor qiran; only ifrad (Hajj alone) is for them. (1) In the verse it says: 'That is for him whose family is not present at the Sacred Mosque' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:196). In this verse, 'that' refers to tamattu', and under it is qiran. Its meaning is that tamattu' and qiran are for one whose family is not near the Sacred Mosque, i.e., not a resident of Makkah. Therefore, according to the Hanafis, there is no tamattu' and no qiran for the people of Makkah and those within the miqat boundaries. (2) Tamattu' is called combining Hajj and Umrah in one journey to benefit, but if there is no journey (i.e., one is already present), what benefit is there? Thus, for the people of Makkah, there is no tamattu' or qiran.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage expounds the ruling that tamattu' (performing Umrah first then Hajj in the same journey) and qiran (combining Umrah and Hajj with a single ihram) are not permissible for the residents of Makkah and those whose permanent residence is within the Haram boundaries (including the miqat limits). The primary evidence is the Quranic verse: 'That is for him whose family is not present at the Sacred Mosque' (al-Baqarah 2:196). The word 'that' refers to the permission of tamattu' and by extension qiran. The rationale is that the concession of tamattu' was granted to those who travel from distant lands to combine both pilgrimages in one trip for convenience. Since the people of Makkah are already present, they do not need this concession and should perform Hajj individually (ifrad). The Hanafi position is that for a Makkan or anyone within the miqat, tamattu' and qiran are not valid; they must perform ifrad.

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu'): Performing Umrah first during Hajj months, then performing Hajj in the same year with a break for tahlul.
قران (qiran): Combining Umrah and Hajj with a single ihram and no tahlul between them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, what type of Hajj is valid for a person living in Makkah?
A) Tamattu' only
B) Qiran only
C) Ifrad only
D) Both tamattu' and qiran

Key Takeaway
Tamattu' and qiran are not valid for residents of Makkah or those within the miqat boundaries; only ifrad is permissible for them based on Quran 2:196.

Entering Ihram Before Yawm al-Tarwiyah
Ruling on bringing forward Hajj ihram before the 8th of Dhul Hijjah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on entering Hajj ihram before the 8th of Dhul Hijjah and identify the obligation of dam al-tamattu'.

Core Idea
Bringing forward Hajj ihram is permissible but imposes the obligation of tamattu' dam.

This passage addresses a practical question for pilgrims: What if someone enters ihram for Hajj a day or two early? The Hanafi ruling confirms it is valid and even commendable, but due to the nature of tamattu', a sacrificial animal becomes wajib. Understanding this ruling clarifies the boundaries of ihram timing and the interaction with tamattu' obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act being ruled upon
The act is entering ihram for Hajj before Yawm al-Tarwiyah (the 8th of Dhul Hijjah).
2
Determine the hukm (legal classification)
The matn explicitly states it is 'jā'iz' (permissible/valid).
In Hanafi terminology, jā'iz often equates to mubah.
3
Identify the attached obligation
The passage states 'upon him is the blood of tamattu'' – a dam (sacrificial animal) is wajib.
This obligation arises because early ihram effectively makes the pilgrim a mutamatti'.
4
Understand the recommended nature
The commentary adds that it is 'rather better' (بلکہ افضل) because it shows eagerness for worship.
Thus the ruling is not merely permissible but recommended.
5
Note the condition for the dam
The dam applies specifically to those performing tamattu' (or qiran); if the pilgrim performs ifrad, no dam is required for early ihram.
The ruling on permissibility applies regardless, but the dam is tied to tamattu'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان قدم الاحرام قبله جاز وعليه دم التمتع [۷۰۵] (۱۱) پس اگر آٹھ تاریخ سے پہلے حج کا احرام باندھ لے تو جائز ہے اور اس پر تمتع کا دم لازم ہوگا۔ ر او پر یہ گزرا کہ آٹھویں ذی الحجہ کو حج کا احرام باندھے لیکن اگر آٹھ تاریخ سے پہلے حج کا احرام باندھے تو جائز ہے بلکہ افضل ہے کیونکہ عبادت کی طرف جلدی کر رہا ہے۔
If he brings forward the ihram before it, it is permissible and upon him is the blood of tamattu'. So if he ties the ihram of Hajj before the 8th date, it is permissible and upon him the blood of tamattu' is obligatory. It has passed that he ties the ihram of Hajj on the 8th of Dhul Hijjah, but if he ties before the 8th, it is permissible, rather it is better because he is hastening towards worship.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn stating that if a person enters ihram for Hajj before the prescribed time of Yawm al-Tarwiyah (the 8th of Dhul Hijjah), it is still valid. However, since he is performing tamattu' (or if he is a mutamatti'), he owes a dam (sacrificial animal). The commentary explains that it is actually better to do so because it indicates eagerness to worship. This ruling is based on the principle that ihram for Hajj is valid before its time, though the normal practice is to enter on the 8th.

Key Terms
دم التمتع (dam al-tamattu'): A sacrificial animal required for someone performing tamattu'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person enters ihram for Hajj on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah?
A) Invalid, must repeat on the 8th
B) Valid but requires a dam
C) Valid and no dam required
D) Makruh and should be avoided

Key Takeaway
Entering Hajj ihram before Yawm al-Tarwiyah is valid (jā'iz) and even commendable, but obligates the dam of tamattu'.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
8 min
Release from Both Ihrams on the Day of Nahr
Ruling on becoming halal from both ihrams after shaving on the 10th

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a Qarin becoming halal from both ihrams on the day of Nahr and identify the prophetic proof that supports it.

Core Idea
Shaving on the day of Nahr releases the Qarin from both ihrams at once — the Umrah and Hajj conclude together.

This passage from the matn establishes a key moment in the Hajj journey: the day of sacrifice (10th Dhul Hijjah). For a person performing Qiran (combining Umrah and Hajj in one ihram), shaving the head on that day completes both consecrations. The ruling is supported by a hadith from Bukhari, showing the Prophet's practice. Understanding this clarifies the distinct stages of release from ihram for different Hajj types.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is shaving (halq) on the day of Nahr. The ruling is that it releases the Qarin from both ihrams (Umrah and Hajj) simultaneously.
The Qarin is distinct from the Mufrid (Hajj only) and Mutamatti' (separate Umrah then Hajj).
2
Parse the legal context
Why are there two ihrams? Because the Qarin entered with both Umrah and Hajj intentions without separating. He did not open the Umrah ihram, so both remain tied until the day of Nahr.
The text says: 'because he had not removed the ihram of Umrah and had tied the ihram of Hajj'.
3
Locate the proof (dalil)
The passage cites a hadith from Bukhari: 'Then he did not become halal from anything that was made haram until he completed his Hajj and slaughtered his Hadi on the day of Nahr.' This indicates that the Prophet remained in ihram until that moment.
The hadith is a proof (dalil naqli) for the combined release.
4
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The key phrase 'lam yahlal... hatta yaqdi hajjahu' shows that completion of Hajj (which includes the Umrah for a Qarin) and the sacrifice are conditions for becoming halal. Thus, the Qarin's Umrah is subsumed within the Hajj.
The hadith's implication is that no partial release occurs before the day of Nahr.
5
Note the practical implication
The Qarin does not get a separate release after Umrah; he remains in full ihram until the 10th. Shaving (and slaughter) on that day renders him completely halal.
This ruling contrasts with the Mutamatti', who becomes halal after Umrah before entering ihram for Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاذا حلق يوم النحر فقد حل من الاحرامين [۷۰۶] (۱۲) پس جب دسویں ذی الحجہ کو حلق کرائے تو دونوں احراموں سے حلال ہو جائے گا۔ ان چونکہ عمرے کا احرام نہیں کھولا تھا اور حج کا احرام باندھ لیا تھا اس لئے دسویں تاریخ کو دونوں احراموں سے حلال ہوگا۔ اس کی دلیل مسئلہ نمبرہ میں گزرگئی ہے۔ ثم لم يحلل من شيء حرم منه حتى يقضى حجه نحر هدية يوم النحر (بخارى شریف نمبر (۱۶۹)
When he shaves on the day of Nahr, he becomes released from both ihrams. So when on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah he performs shaving, he will become halal from both ihrams. Because he had not removed the ihram of Umrah and had tied the ihram of Hajj, so on the 10th he will become halal from both. Its proof has passed in issue number []. Then: 'He is not halal from anything that was made haram until he completes his Hajj and slaughters his Hadi on the day of Nahr' (Bukhari no. 169).
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn that on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), shaving the head (halq) brings about the completion of both ihrams for one who entered with qiran or tamattu'? Specifically, for the Qarin who ties both ihrams together, he remains in ihram until he completes both. The proof is a hadith from Bukhari indicating that the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) did not become halal until after slaughter on the day of Nahr. The commentary explains that because the person did not open the ihram of Umrah and had tied both, they become halal from both on that day.

Key Terms
حلق (halq): Shaving the head, one of the rites of completing ihram.
الاحرامين (al-ihraamayni): The two ihrams: one for Umrah and one for Hajj for a Qarin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a person performing Qiran become halal from both ihrams?
A) After completing Umrah only
B) After completing Hajj only
C) On the day of Nahr after shaving
D) After the first stoning

Key Takeaway
On the day of Nahr, shaving (halq) releases the Qarin from both Umrah and Hajj ihrams simultaneously.
